Buyu — Sales and Trade

Possession Before Separation in Sarf
States that both items must be possessed before separation and defines iftiraq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of possession in sarf, define iftiraq, and apply it to distinguish valid from invalid contracts.

Core Idea
In sarf, both exchange items must be possessed before the parties physically separate, otherwise riba occurs.

This lesson explores the second critical condition of a valid sarf (currency exchange) contract: possession (qabd) before separation (iftiraq). The Hanafi school derives this from hadith and rational analogy to prevent riba. You will learn the precise definition of separation and its application in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on possession
The passage states that possession of both exchange items is necessary before separation. This is a wajib condition; its omission invalidates the contract.
The ruling is specific to sarf contracts.
2
Understand the proofs
The author cites the hadith 'yadan bi yad' and the statements of Umar and Ibn Umar. The hadith implies immediate hand-to-hand transfer; Umar's statement prohibits deferment; Ibn Umar defines separation as bodily departure.
These are zanni proofs but collectively establish the ruling.
3
Define iftiraq (separation)
Iftiraq means physical separation of the bodies. Walking away together, sleeping, or unconsciousness do not break the contract; only actual bodily departure (e.g., one leaving the room) invalidates it.
This definition is specific to sarf and differs from khiyar al-mukhayyira.
4
Apply to scenarios
Apply the condition: if both items are possessed before bodily separation, the contract is valid. If separation occurs before possession, the contract is invalid.
Possession must be actual physical control.
5
Compare with salam and khiyar
The same definition of qabd applies to salam capital, but khiyar al-mukhayyira is invalidated by turning away (i'rad), which is a lower threshold than bodily separation.
This highlights the specificity of sarf conditions.

Source Text

بیع الصرف میں عوضین پر قبضہ ضروری ہے
قال ولا بد من قبض العوضين قبل الافتراق لما روينا ولقول عمر وان استنظرك ان يدخل بيته فلا تنظره ولانه لا بد من قبض احدهما ليخرج العقد عن الكالئى بالكالتى ثم لا بد من قبض الآخر تحقيقا للمساواة فلا يتحقق الربوا ولان احدهما ليس باولى من الآخر فوجب قبضهما سواء كانا يتعينان كالمصوغ اولا يتعينان كالمضروب اويتعين احدهما ولا يتعين الأخر لا طلاق ماروينا ولا نه ان كان يتعين ففيه شبهة عدم التعيين لكونه ثمنا خلقة فيشترط قبضه اعتباراً للشبهة فى الربوا والمراد منه الافتراق بالابدان حتى لو ذهبا عن المجلس يمشيان معافى جهة واحدة اونا مافى المجلس او اغمى عليهما لا يبطل الصرف لقول ابن عمر وان وثب من سطح فشب معه وكذا المعتبر ما ذكرناه فى قبض رأس مال السلم بخلاف خيار المخيرة لانه يبطل بالاعراض
ترجمہ اور جدا ہونے سے پہلے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر وہ تجھ سے اپنے گھر میں داخل ہونے کی مہلت مانگے تو ، تو اس کو مہلت مت دے اور اس لئے کہ دونوں عوضوں میں سے ایک پر قبضہ کرنا اسلئے ضروری ہے تا کہ عقد کالی بالکائی ہونے سے خارج ہو جائے۔ پھر مسادات ثابت کرنے کیلئے دوسرے عوض پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ ربوا متحقق نہ ہو۔ اور اس لئے کہ دونوں عوضوں میں سے ایک دوسرے سے اولیٰ نہیں ہے۔ پس دونوں پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ برابر ہے کہ دونوں عوض متعین ہو جاتے ہوں جیسے ڈھلی ہوئی چیز ، یا متعین نہ ہوتے ہوں جیسے سکہ یا ان ہیں سے ایک متعین ہو اور دوسرا متعین نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ جو حدیث ہم نے روایت کی ہے وہ مطلق ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اگر وہ متعین ہو جا تا ہو مگر پھر بھی اس میں متعین نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے کیونکہ وہ پیدائشی طور پر شمن ہے۔ پس شبت الربو کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور افتراق سے مراد بدن سے جدا ہونا ہے حتی کہ اگر دونوں عقد کرنے والے مجلس سے اٹھ کر ایک سمت میں ساتھ ساتھ چلتے رہے یا دونوں مجلس میں سو گئے یا دونوں پر بے ہوشی طاری ہوگئی تو عقد صرف باطل نہیں ہوا ۔ کیونکہ ابن عمرؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر وہ چھت سے کود گیا تو تو بھی اس کے ساتھ کود جا۔ اور مسلم کے راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے میں بھی یہی معتبر ہے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ برخلاف خیار مخیرہ کے کیونکہ اعراض سے اس کا خیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔
تشریح تمام علماء کا اتفاق ہے کہ عقد صرف کے دونوں عوضوں پر بدن کے اعتبار سے جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل منقول یعنی حدیث یدا بید پہلے گزر چکی ہے یدا بید کے معنی ہاتھ درہاتھ یا ہا تھوں ہاتھ یا نقد انقدی کے ہیں اسی کو نقابض کہا جاتا ہے یعنی با ہمی قبضہ کرنا ۔ بہر حال لفظ يداً بيد اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ اگر سونے کی بیچ سونے کے عوض یا چاندی کی بیع چاندی کے عوض ہو یعنی عقد صرف ہو تو عوضین پر جدا ہونے سے پہلے قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اور بخاری شریف کی حدیث ہے لا تبيعوا منها غائبا بناجز لين
In the contract of sarf, possession of the exchange items is necessary. He said: Possession of both items is necessary before separation, due to what we narrated, and due to the saying of Umar: 'If he asks you to wait until he enters his house, do not give him respite.' And because it is necessary to take possession of one to remove the contract from being kalai bi kalai (deferred for deferred), then it is necessary to take possession of the other to achieve equality so that riba does not occur. And because neither of the two items is prior to the other, so possession of both is obligatory, whether both are specified (like jewelry) or unspecified (like coins), or one is specified and the other not, due to the generality of what we narrated. And because if it (the item) becomes specified, there is still a doubt of non-specification because it is by nature a price (thaman), so possession is stipulated considering the suspicion of riba. And the meaning of 'iftiraq' is separation of bodies, so if both parties walk away from the sitting together in one direction, or both sleep in the sitting, or both become unconscious, the sarf contract does not become invalid, because Ibn Umar said: 'If he jumps off a roof, jump with him.' And similarly what we mentioned is considered in the possession of the capital in salam, unlike the option of choice (khiyar al-mukhayyira) because it becomes invalid by turning away. Translation: It is necessary to take possession of both items before separation, due to the hadith we narrated, and because Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) said: 'If he asks you to wait to enter his house, do not give him respite.' And because it is necessary to take possession of one so that the contract is no longer a deferred-for-deferred exchange, then possession of the other is necessary to establish equality so that riba does not occur. And because neither of the two are prior to the other, so possession of both is necessary. It is equal whether both are specified (like jewelry) or unspecified (like coins), or one is specified and the other not, because the hadith we narrated is general. And because even if it becomes specified, there is a suspicion of non-specification since it is by nature a price, so possession is stipulated considering the suspicion of riba. And by 'iftiraq' is meant separation of bodies, so if both contractors get up from the sitting and walk together in one direction, or both fall asleep in the sitting, or both become unconscious, the sarf contract does not become invalid, because Ibn Umar said: 'If he jumps off a roof, jump with him.' And similarly what we mentioned is considered in the possession of capital in salam, contrary to the option of choice because it becomes invalid by turning away. Explanation: All scholars agree that in the sarf contract, possession of both items is necessary before bodily separation. The transmitted proof, the hadith 'yadan bi yad' has passed before. 'Yadan bi yad' means hand to hand or cash, it is called 'naqabada' meaning mutual possession. In any case, the phrase 'yadan bi yad' indicates that if it is a sale of gold for gold or silver for silver, i.e., a sarf contract, then possession of the exchange items before separation is a condition. And in Sahih Bukhari there is a hadith: 'Do not sell from it an absent (item) for a present (item)...'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage establishes the second major condition of sarf: possession (qabd) of both exchange items must occur before the parties separate. The author provides multiple proofs: the hadith 'yadan bi yad' (hand to hand), the statement of Umar, and rational reasoning that one item must be possessed to avoid deferred exchange (kalai bi kalai) and both to avoid riba. The passage also defines iftiraq (separation) as physical separation of the bodies: leaving the sitting, walking away together, sleeping, or unconsciousness do not break the contract, but actual bodily separation does. The author also compares with the possession of capital in salam and distinguishes from khiyar al-mukhayyira where turning away invalidates.

Key Terms
قبض (qabd): Possession: taking physical control of the exchange item in the contracting session.
افتراق (iftiraq): Separation of the two contracting parties' bodies from the place of contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if both parties stand up and walk away together in the same direction without taking possession?
A) The contract becomes invalid
B) The contract remains valid because they did not separate
C) The contract becomes fasid
D) The contract is suspended till possession

Key Takeaway
In sarf, possession of both exchange items before bodily separation is wajib; the definition of iftiraq is physical departure, not inattention.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate

The Requirement of Hand-to-Hand Exchange in Sarf
Establishes necessity of possession of both countervalues before separation in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of immediate possession (qabd) in a sarf contract and apply it to determine the validity of an exchange.

Core Idea
In a currency exchange (sarf), both items must be exchanged hand-to-hand before parting — delay invalidates the sale.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh masterwork Al-Hidayah establishes a critical condition for the validity of currency exchange (sarf). While many are aware that riba is prohibited, fewer know the precise mechanism that prevents it in gold and silver transactions. The text explains why immediate possession is non-negotiable and what happens if parties separate without full exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text discusses the sarf contract (exchange of gold/silver for gold/silver). The ruling is that possession (qabd) of both countervalues before physical separation (ifttiraq) is a condition for validity.
2
Locate the transmitted proofs
The author cites the hadith 'Gold for gold, like for like, hand to hand' and the statement of Umar from Muwatta, which forbids even a brief respite to fetch the item. Both indicate immediate exchange.
The phrase 'yadan bi yad' is key.
3
Analyze the rational proofs
Two rational arguments: (1) Avoiding kali' bi kali' (deferred for deferred), which is prohibited. (2) Ensuring equality to prevent riba, since cash is superior to credit. Also, since both countervalues are prices, neither has priority, so both must be possessed immediately.
The principle 'al-naqd khayr min al-nasi'ah' is invoked.
4
Define separation (ifttiraq) and its exceptions
Separation means physical departure of the parties' bodies. If they walk together, sleep, or faint, it is not considered separation. But if one leaves to fetch an item, that is separation.
This is contrasted with khiyar al-mukhayyara where i'rad invalidates.
5
Determine the practical application and consequence
If parties separate before full possession, the contract is batil (void). The ruling applies to all forms of gold and silver, whether coined or uncoined.
No internal ikhtilaf among the three Hanafi imams.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصرف

اشرف الہدایہ جلد نہم کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری شرط ہے اور دوسری حدیث یہ ہے کہ اموال ربویہ میں کھرا اور کھوٹا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ یعنی اگر ایک عوض کھرا اور ایک کھوٹا ہو تو بھی مساوات ضروری ہے۔ اور کمی زیادتی حرام ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ شریعت اسلام نے کھرے اور کھوٹے کے فرق کا اعتبار نہیں کیا ہے۔ بلکہ دونوں کو مساوی درجہ دیا ہے۔

بیع الصرف میں عوضین پر قبضہ ضروری ہے

قال ولا بد من قبض العوضين قبل الافتراق لما روينا ولقول عمر وان استنظرك ان يدخل بيته فلا تنظره ولانه لا بد من قبض احدهما ليخرج العقد عن الكالئى بالكالتى ثم لا بد من قبض الآخر تحقيقا للمساواة فلا يتحقق الربوا ولان احدهما ليس باولى من الآخر فوجب قبضهما سواء كانا يتعينان كالمصوغ اولا يتعينان كالمضروب اويتعين احدهما ولا يتعين الأخر لا طلاق ماروينا ولا نه ان كان يتعين ففيه شبهة عدم التعيين لكونه ثمنا خلقة فيشترط قبضه اعتباراً للشبهة فى الربوا والمراد منه الافتراق بالابدان حتى لو ذهبا عن المجلس يمشيان معافى جهة واحدة اونا مافى المجلس او اغمى عليهما لا يبطل الصرف لقول ابن عمر وان وثب من سطح فشب معه وكذا المعتبر ما ذكرناه فى قبض رأس مال السلم بخلاف خيار المخيرة لانه يبطل بالاعراض

ترجمہ: اور جدا ہونے سے پہلے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے اس حدیث کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے روایت کی ہے اور اس لئے کہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر وہ تجھ سے اپنے گھر میں داخل ہونے کی مہلت مانگے تو ، تو اس کو مہلت مت دے اور اس لئے کہ دونوں عوضوں میں سے ایک پر قبضہ کرنا اسلئے ضروری ہے تا کہ عقد کالی با لکائی ہونے سے خارج ہو جائے۔ پھر مسادات ثابت کرنے کیلئے دوسرے عوض پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے تا کہ ربوا متحقق نہ ہو۔ اور اس لئے کہ دونوں عوضوں میں سے ایک دوسرے سے اولیٰ نہیں ہے۔ پس دونوں پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ برابر ہے کہ دونوں عوض متعین ہو جاتے ہوں جیسے ڈھلی ہوئی چیز ، یا متعین نہ ہوتے ہوں جیسے سکہ یا ان ہیں سے ایک متعین ہو اور دوسرا متعین نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ جو حدیث ہم نے روایت کی ہے وہ مطلق ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اگر وہ متعین ہو جا تا ہو مگر پھر بھی اس میں متعین نہ ہونے کا شبہ ہے کیونکہ وہ پیدائشی طور پر شمن ہے۔ پس شبت الربو کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے اس پر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور افتراق سے مراد بدن سے جدا ہونا ہے حتی کہ اگر دونوں عقد کرنے والے مجلس سے اٹھ کر ایک سمت میں ساتھ ساتھ چلتے رہے یا دونوں مجلس میں سو گئے یا دونوں پر بے ہوشی طاری ہوگئی تو عقد صرف باطل نہیں ہوا ۔ کیونکہ ابن عمرؓ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر وہ چھت سے کود گیا تو تو بھی اس کے ساتھ کو د جا۔ اور مسلم کے راس المال پر قبضہ کرنے میں بھی یہی معتبر ہے جس کو ہم نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ برخلاف خیار مخیرہ کے کیونکہ اعراض سے اس کا خیار باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔

تشریح: تمام علماء کا اتفاق ہے کہ عقد صرف کے دونوں عوضوں پر بدن کے اعتبار سے جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل منقول یعنی حدیث یدا بید پہلے گزر چکی ہے یدا بید کے معنی ہاتھ درہاتھ یا ہا تھوں ہاتھ یا نقد انقدی کے ہیں اسی کو نقابض کہا جاتا ہے یعنی با ہمی قبضہ کرنا ۔ بہر حال لفظ يداً بيد اس پر دلالت کرتا ہے کہ اگر سونے کی بیچ سونے کے عوض یا چاندی کی بیع چاندی کے عوض ہو یعنی عقد صرف ہو تو عوضین پر جدا ہونے سے پہلے قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اور بخاری شریف کی حدیث ہے لا تبيعوا منها غائبا بناجز لين اموال ربویہ میں سے غائب کو نا جز کے عوض مت فروخت کرو۔ یعنی اموال ربویہ کی بیچ اس طرح مت کرو کہ ایک عوض مجلس میں موجود ہو اور ایک عوض موجود نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مجلس کے اندر ایک عوض پر تو قبضہ ہو جائے لیکن دوسرے عوض ( غیر موجود ) پر قبضہ نہ ہو گا۔ حالانکہ دونوں عوضوں پر مجلس کے اندر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کا شرط ہونا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ حضرت عمر کا قول بھی اسی کی شہادت دیتا ہے۔ موطا امام مالک میں یہ قول ان الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے، قال لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب الأمثلاً بمثل ولا تبيعوا الورق بالذهب احدهما غائب والآخر ناجز و ان استنظرك ان يلج بيته فلا تنظره الا يدا بيدهات وهات انى اخشى عليكم الربوا حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا کہ سونا ، سونے کے عوض نہ فروخت کرو مگر برابر، برابر اور چاندی کو سونے کے عوض اس حال میں مت فروخت کرو کہ ایک عوض غیر موجود ہو اور دوسرا موجود ہو۔ اور اگر تجھ سے ( تیرا ساتھی) اس بات کی مہلت مانگے کہ وہ اپنے گی میں داخل ہو کر (غیر موجود عوض لے آئے ) تو اس کو اتنی مہات بھی نہ دو۔ ہاں اگر معاملہ نقد انقدی اور لا اور لے کے طور پر ہو تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ) ( اور اس مہلت نہ دینے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ) میں تم پر ربوا سے ڈرتا یہ ہے کہ بیع صرف میں دونوں عوض چونکہ شمن ہونے میں برابر ہیں اسلئے ایک عوض کو دوسرے عوض پر کوئی ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہے اور جب ایک عوض دوسرے عوض سے اولیٰ اور راج نہیں ہے تو ترجیح بلا مرجع کے اشکال کو ختم کرنے کیلئے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔

صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ بیع صرف میں دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنے کا حکم عام ہے خواہ دونوں عوض ایسے ہوں جو متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتے ہوں جیسے ڈھالی ہوئی چیز زیور برتن وغیرہ خواہ دونوں عوض ایسے ہوں جو متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوتے ہوں جیسے درہم و دینار، خواہ ان میں سے ایک عوض ایسا ہو جو متعین کرنے سے متعین ہو جاتا ہو ۔ اور ایک عوض ایسا ہو جو متعین کرنے سے متعین نہ ہوتا ہو۔ دلیل یہ ہے حدیث الذهب بالذهب الخ مطلق ہے جو مضروب اور مصوغ سب کو شامل ہے۔
Chapter of Sarf. Equality is a condition. The second hadith states that in ribawi goods, pure and impure are equal. That is, even if one exchange is pure and the other impure, equality is still required. Increase or decrease is forbidden. This hadith shows that Islamic law does not consider the difference between pure and impure; rather, it gives them equal status. In a sarf sale, possession of the countervalues is required. He said: Possession of both countervalues before separation is necessary, due to what we narrated, and due to the statement of Umar: 'And if he asks you for respite to enter his house, do not give him respite.' And because possession of one of them is necessary to remove the contract from being kali' bi kali', then possession of the other is necessary to establish equality so that riba is not realized. And because one is not more entitled than the other, so possession of both is obligatory, whether they are specific (like uncoined metal) or non-specific (like coined money), or one is specific and the other not, due to the absolute nature of what we narrated. And because if it is specific, there is a semblance of non-specificity due to its being inherently a price, so possession is stipulated considering the semblance of riba. Separation meant is by bodies, so even if they leave the session walking together in one direction, or sleep in the session, or both faint, the sarf is not invalidated, due to the statement of Ibn Umar: 'And if he jumps from a roof, jump with him.' Similarly, what we mentioned is considered in possession of the capital of salam, unlike the option of the exercised (khiyar al-mukhayyara) because it is invalidated by turning away. Commentary: All scholars agree that in a sarf contract, possession of both countervalues before physical separation is necessary. The transmitted proof is the hadith of yadan bi yad (hand to hand), which has passed. 'Yadan bi yad' means hand in hand or cash. It indicates that if gold is sold for gold or silver for silver (i.e., a sarf contract), possession before separation is a condition. In Sahih al-Bukhari, the hadith is: 'Do not sell absent among them for present', meaning do not sell ribawi goods in such a way that one countervalue is present in the session and the other is absent. Because in that case, one countervalue would be possessed in the session but the other would not, while possession of both in the session is a condition. This hadith also proves the condition of possession before separation. The statement of Umar also testifies to this. In Muwatta of Imam Malik, this statement is narrated: He said, 'Do not sell gold for gold except like for like, and do not sell silver for gold when one is absent and the other present. And if he asks you for respite to enter his house, do not give him respite, but hand to hand, take and give. I fear riba for you.' Umar said: Do not sell gold for gold except equal, and do not sell silver for gold when one is absent and the other present. And if your companion asks for respite to enter his house (to bring the absent countervalue), do not give him even that much respite. (Yes, if the transaction is cash and give-and-take, there is no harm) (And the reason for not giving respite is that) I fear riba for you. That is, I fear that the delay in giving possession due to going and coming from home would become riba and usury, so my opinion is that you should not give him even that much respite. This also shows that possession before separation is necessary. The rational proof is: in the case of a sarf contract, possession of one countervalue is necessary so that the sale does not become kali' bi kali' (deferred sale for deferred countervalue), which is prohibited. Possession of the other countervalue is necessary to establish equality and prevent riba, because the countervalue that has been taken possession of becomes cash, and the one not taken becomes deferred. The well-known principle 'al-naqd khayr min al-nasi'ah' (cash is better than credit) indicates that cash has a kind of superiority over credit. One countervalue being superior to another is riba. Therefore, since riba would occur if one is possessed and the other not, possession of the other is necessary to create equality. Another transmitted proof: in a sarf sale, since both countervalues are equal in being prices, one has no preference over the other. And when one is not more entitled, to eliminate the problem of preference without basis, possession of both is necessary. The author of Hidayah says: The ruling of possession of both countervalues in a sarf sale is general, whether both are specific (like ornaments, vessels) or both non-specific (like dirhams and dinars), or one is specific and the other non-specific. The proof is the hadith of gold for gold etc. is absolute, including both coined and uncoined.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the conditions of a valid sarf (currency exchange) transaction. The ruling is straightforward: both parties must physically exchange the countervalues (e.g., gold for gold or silver for silver) before they separate from the session of the contract. The passage provides multiple proofs to establish this requirement.

1. The primary proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Gold for gold, like for like, hand to hand.' This hadith explicitly requires both equivalence in quantity and hand-to-hand delivery. The term 'yadan bi yad' is interpreted as immediate exchange without delay.

2. A secondary proof is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with him), narrated in Muwatta Imam Malik. He prohibits selling gold for gold except like for like, and if one party asks for even a moment's respite to fetch the item from his home, Umar forbids it out of fear of riba. This shows that the exchange must be completely immediate.

3. The rational proof is based on preventing two prohibited situations:
   - First, the contract must not be a deferred sale (kali' bi kali'), which is prohibited regardless of the commodity.
   - Second, even if one side is immediate, the other side must also be immediate to prevent riba, because cash is considered superior to credit. If one countervalue is received immediately and the other later, the transaction would involve an imbalance (one side being better), which is exactly riba.
   - Also, since both countervalues are prices (thaman) inherently, neither has priority over the other. To avoid unjustified preference, both must be possessed before separation.

4. The ruling applies universally to all forms of gold and silver: whether coined (like dinars and dirhams), uncoined (like jewelry or ingots), or a mix of both. The absolute wording of the hadith covers all types.

5. Separation is defined as physical departure from the session. If the parties walk away together in the same direction, or sleep, or faint, the contract remains valid because they have not 'separated' in the legal sense. The act of turning away (i'rad) that invalidates an option (khiyar al-mukhayyara) is not applicable here.

6. This requirement is a condition (shart) for the validity of the sarf contract. If the parties part without possessing both countervalues, the contract is void (batil).

The commentary also clarifies that the condition of equality (musawat) in quantity and quality is separate; here the emphasis is on the timing of delivery.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): A type of sale where the countervalues are gold or silver, either of the same genus (like gold for gold) or different genera (like gold for silver).
قبض (qabd): Physical taking possession of the item; in sarf, it is a condition for validity.
افتراق (ifttiraq): The physical separation of the parties from the session of the contract.
ربوا (riba): Usury or interest; in this context, it is the prohibited increase in exchange of ribawi goods.
مساوات (musawat): Equality in quantity and quality of the countervalues when exchanging within the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if two parties in a sarf contract separate (leave the session) before taking possession of both gold and silver items?
A) The contract is still valid but they must complete the exchange later.
B) The contract becomes void (batil) because the condition of immediate possession was not fulfilled.
C) The contract is valid but one party has an option to cancel.
D) The contract becomes a loan.

Key Takeaway
Immediate possession of both countervalues before physical separation is an essential condition (shart) for the validity of a sarf contract; violation renders the contract void.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

The Requirement of Possession in Sarf and Its Proofs
Ruling and proofs for qabd in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on possession in sarf, explain the naqli proof from Umar (radiallahu anhu), and derive the rational proofs for the condition.

Core Idea
In sarf, possession of both countervalues must occur in the session before parting.

Currency exchange (sarf) is a special contract with strict conditions. The Hanafi school requires immediate physical possession of both gold/silver items in the same session. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proofs from the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab and from rational arguments that prevent riba and debt-for-debt sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states that selling an absent ribawi item for a present one is prohibited. Both countervalues must be possessed before the parties separate. This is a condition for validity; if not met, the contract is fasid (invalid).
2
Examine the Naqli Proof
The proof is the statement of Umar (ra) narrated in Muwatta Imam Malik, which explicitly forbids selling gold for gold or silver for gold unless it is hand-to-hand (yadan bi yad). Umar feared that any delay could lead to riba.
This is a qawl sahabi, which is a source of evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the First Rational Proof
If only one countervalue is possessed, the other becomes a debt. This leads to bai' al-kali' bi al-kali' (sale of debt for debt), which is prohibited. Additionally, cash is superior to credit, creating an inequality that constitutes riba.
This is based on the maxim 'al-naqd khayrun min al-nasi'ah' (cash is better than credit).
4
Understand the Second Rational Proof
Both countervalues are equal as prices (thaman). If one is preferred without cause, it is invalid (tarjeeh bilaa murajjih). Possession of both eliminates this imbalance.
5
Apply the Ruling
In any sarf transaction, ensure both parties take physical possession of the gold or silver before leaving the session. Even a short delay (e.g., going into a house) is not permitted.
This applies to modern currency exchange as well, as per the same principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصرف
۹۴
اشرف الهدایہ جلد نمیم
اموال ربویہ میں سے غائب کو نا جز کے عوض مت فروخت کرو۔ یعنی اموال ربویہ کی بیچ اس طرح مت کرو کہ ایک عوض مجلس میں موجود ہو اور ایک عوض موجود نہ ہو ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں مجلس کے اندر ایک عوض پر تو قبضہ ہو جائے لیکن دوسرے عوض ( غیر موجود ) پر قبضہ نہ ہو گا۔ حالانکہ دونوں عوضوں پر مجلس کے اندر قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اس حدیث سے بھی جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کا شرط ہونا
ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ حضرت عمر کا قول بھی اسی کی شہادت دیتا ہے۔ موطا امام مالک میں یہ قول ان الفاظ کے ساتھ مروی ہے، قال لا تبيعوا الذهب بالذهب الأمثلاً بمثل ولا تبيعوا الورق بالذهب احدهما غائب والآخر ناجز و ان استنظرك ان يلج بيته فلا تنظره الا يدا بيدهات وهات انى اخشى عليكم الربوا حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا کہ سونا ، سونے کے عوض نہ فروخت کرونگر برابر، برابر اور چاندی کو سونے کے عوض اس حال میں مت فروخت کرو کہ ایک عوض غیر موجود ہو اور دوسرا موجود ہو۔ اور اگر تجھ سے ( تیرا ساتھی) اس بات کی مہلت مانگے کہ وہ اپنے گی میں داخل ہو کر (غیر موجود عوض لے آئے ) تو اس کو اتنی مہات بھی نہ دو۔ ہاں اگر معاملہ نقد انقدی اور لا اور لے کے طور پر ہو تو کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے ) ( اور اس مہلت نہ دینے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ ) میں تم پر ربوا سے ڈرتا ہوں۔ یعنی مجھے یہ ڈر ہے کہ گھر تک آنے اور جانے کی تاخیر سے جو قبضہ دینے میں تاخیر ہوگی وہ ربوا اور سود نہ ہو جائے اسلئے میری رائے ہے کہ اس کو اتنی مہلت بھی نہ دو۔ اس سے بھی ظاہر ہوتا ہے کہ جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے عوضین پر قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ عقد صرف کی صورت میں ایک عوض پر قبضہ کرنا تو اسلئے ضروری ہے تا کہ کافی با کائی کی بیچ لاز م نہ آئے یعنی ادھار کی بیع ادھار کے عوض لازم نہ آئے حالانکہ بیع الکائی با لکائی ممنوع ہے اور دوسرے عوض پر قبضہ کرنا اسلئے ضروری ہے تا کہ دونوں کے درمیان مساوات اور برابری متحقق ہو اور ر بوالا زم نہ آئے کیونکہ جس عوض پر قبضہ کر لیا گیا وہ تو نقد ہو گیا اور جس پر قبضہ نہیں کیا گیا وہ ادھار ہو گیا اور النقد خير من النسبة کا قاعدہ مشہور ہے کہ نقد ادھار سے بہتر ہوتا ہے گویا نقد کو ادھار پر ایک گونہ فضیلت حاصل ہوتی ہے اور ایک عوض کا دوسرے عوض سے افضل ہونا اس کا نام ربوا ہے۔ پس چونکہ ایک عوض پر قبضہ کرنے اور ایک پر قبضہ نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ربوا لازم آتا ہے اسلئے مساوات اور برابری پیدا کرنے کیلئے دوسرے عوض پر بھی قبضہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ دوسری منقلی دلیل یہ ہے کہ بیع صرف میں دونوں عوض چونکہ شمن ہونے میں برابر ہیں اسلئے ایک عوض کو دوسرے عوض پر کوئی ترجیح حاصل نہیں ہے اور جب ایک عوض دوسرے عوض سے اولیٰ اور راج نہیں ہے تو ترجیح بلا مرجع کے اشکال کو ختم کرنے کیلئے دونوں عوضوں پر قبضہ کرنا بھی ضروری ہے۔
Book of Sarf. Do not sell the absent (non-present) for the present among ribawi wealth. That is, do not conduct the sale of ribawi wealth in such a way that one countervalue is present in the session and the other is not. Because in this case, possession of one countervalue would occur in the session but possession of the second (absent) countervalue would not occur, although possession of both countervalues in the session is a condition. From this hadith as well, the condition of possession of both countervalues before separation is established. The statement of Umar also testifies to this. In the Muwatta of Imam Malik, this statement is narrated with these words: He said, 'Do not sell gold for gold except like for like, and do not sell silver for gold with one absent and the other present. And if he asks you for respite until he enters his house, do not give him respite except hand to hand. Indeed, I fear for you riba.' Umar said: Do not sell gold for gold except equal for equal, and do not sell silver for gold in a state where one countervalue is absent and the other is present. And if your companion asks you for respite so that he may enter his house (and bring the absent countervalue), do not give him even that much respite. Yes, if the transaction is cash in hand, there is no harm. (And the reason for not giving respite is that) I fear riba upon you. That is, I fear that the delay in going and coming from the house will cause delay in giving possession, which would become riba and usury. Therefore, my opinion is that you should not give him even that much respite. This also indicates that it is necessary to take possession of the countervalues before separation. The rational proof is that in a sarf contract, possession of one countervalue is necessary to avoid bai' al-kali' bi al-kali' (sale of debt for debt), i.e., the sale of credit for credit, which is prohibited. And possession of the second countervalue is necessary to ensure equality and equivalence between them and to avoid riba, because the countervalue that has been taken possession of becomes cash, and the one that has not been taken possession of becomes credit, and the principle is that cash is better than credit. So cash has a kind of superiority over credit, and one countervalue being superior to another is riba. Therefore, since in the case of taking possession of one and not the other, riba would occur, it is necessary to take possession of the second countervalue to establish equality. The second rational proof is that in a sarf contract, since both countervalues are equal in being prices (thaman), one countervalue has no preference over the other. And when one countervalue is not superior or preferred over the other, it is necessary to take possession of both countervalues to eliminate the problem of preference without cause (tarjeeh bilaa murajjih).
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs. It begins with the prohibition of selling an absent ribawi item for a present one, explaining that both countervalues must be taken into possession within the session. It then provides the proof from the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab (رضي الله عنه) in the Muwatta of Imam Malik, which explicitly forbids such transactions and emphasizes immediate hand-to-hand exchange. This is followed by a rational proof: if possession of only one countervalue occurs, it leads to bai' al-kali' bi al-kali' (sale of debt for debt), which is prohibited. Additionally, failing to possess both creates an imbalance where one becomes cash and the other credit, resulting in riba. A second rational proof is that since both countervalues are equal as prices, preferring one over the other without cause is invalid, so possession of both is essential.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange, specifically the exchange of gold and silver for gold and silver.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the countervalue.
ربوا (riba): Usury or unlawful increase in exchange transactions.
افتراق (iftiraq): Separation of the contracting parties from the session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if in a sarf contract, one countervalue is handed over but the other is promised to be delivered after the parties separate?
A) The contract is valid if the delayed item is of equal value.
B) The contract is fasid (invalid) because possession of both countervalues is a condition.
C) The contract is valid but the delayed party owes compensation.
D) The contract is suspended until the second item is possessed.

Key Takeaway
In a sarf contract, both parties must physically take possession of the gold or silver before they part; any delay invalidates the contract.

Generality of Possession Requirement and Definition of Separation
Addresses objection about musawwagh items and defines iftiraq as bodily separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule of possession in sarf for all gold/silver items, explain why wrought items are not exempt due to shubhat al-riba, and define iftiraq as bodily separation, applying it to examples.

Core Idea
All gold/silver in sarf require possession before bodily separation.

In sarf, the requirement of possession is not limited to coined money but extends to all gold and silver items, including jewellery. Some might think that because wrought items are individually specified, possession might not be necessary. The Hanafi school addresses this by invoking the concept of shubhat al-riba, and clarifies that separation means physical parting, not just abandonment of the session.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule of possession
State the ruling that both countervalues must be taken into possession in sarf, and note that it applies to all types of gold/silver items: coined, wrought, or one of each.
The ruling is based on the absolute hadith 'gold for gold...' covering everything.
2
Understand the objection regarding musawwagh items
Recognize the argument that wrought items, being determinate by specification, should not require possession because they do not entail bai' al-kali' bi al-kali'.
This objection would limit the general rule.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response using shubhat al-riba
Explain that even though wrought items are determinate, they retain their nature as thaman (price), so delaying possession resembles riba (shubhat al-riba), which is equally prohibited.
The semblance of riba is treated like actual riba in preventing delayed exchange.
4
Define iftiraq as bodily separation
State that 'separation' in the context of sarf means bodily departure (iftiraq bil-abdan) of the contracting parties, not merely leaving the session mentally.
Examples: walking away together, sleeping, fainting do not constitute separation.
5
Apply the definition to scenarios
Use the incident from Ibn Umar: if one party jumps off a roof to create separation, the other must jump with him to preserve the contract.
This illustrates that bodily separation is the criterion.

The author of al-Hidayah says: The ruling that both countervalues must be taken into possession in a sarf transaction is general, whether both countervalues are such that they become determinate by specification (like coined items, jewellery, vessels, etc.) or both are such that they do not become determinate by specification (like dirhams and dinars), or one of them is of the first type and the other of the second. The proof is that the hadith 'gold for gold...' is absolute, encompassing both coined and wrought articles. And the phrase 'because if it becomes determinate (yata'ayyan)...' is an answer to an objection. The objection is that the sale of coined (mudrib) for coined without possession is invalid because it entails bai' al-kali' bi al-kali' (sale of debt for debt), but selling wrought (musawwagh) items for wrought items without possession does not entail this defect, because wrought items become determinate by specification. So for coined-for-coined, possession is necessary to remove the defect of kali' bi kali' and to establish equality, but for wrought-for-wrought, since this defect does not occur, possession should not be necessary. The answer: Even though wrought items become determinate by specification, they still have the semblance (shubha) of being non-determinate because they are by nature thaman (price), i.e., they are originally gold and silver. Therefore, possession is still a condition, because just as actual riba is unlawful, so also the semblance of riba (shubhat al-riba) is unlawful. The author of al-Hidayah said that in the text's phrase 'before separation' (qabl al-iftiraq), 'separation' means bodily separation (iftiraq bil-abdan). That is, the parting of the contracting parties with their bodies. So if the two parties get up from the session and walk away together, or both fall asleep in the session, or both become unconscious, in these cases bodily separation has not occurred, so the sarf contract is not invalid. This is supported by the statement of Abdullah ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him). Allamah Ibn al-Humam narrated the full incident from al-Mabsut: Abi Jablah said: I asked Abdullah ibn Umar: We go to the land of Syria, and we have with us heavy silver coins that are current, and they have light silver coins that are not current. So we buy their ten coins for nine and a half? He said: Do not do that, but sell your silver for gold, and buy their silver with gold, and do not separate from him until you receive (your due). And if he jumps off a roof, jump with him. From this incident, several things are learned: first, that when silver is sold for silver, increase or decrease is not permitted, but when silver and gold are exchanged, increase/decrease is permitted. Second, that one should not separate without possessing the countervalues. Third, that separation means bodily separation, because Ibn Umar said that if your companion jumps off the roof to cause bodily separation and thus invalidate the sarf contract, then you should also jump with him to avoid separation.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of sarf, first stating the generality of the possession requirement for all gold/silver items, whether coined (mudrib) or wrought (musawwagh), citing the absolute hadith. It then addresses an objection that wrought items, being determinate, might not require possession. The response uses the concept of shubhat al-riba (resemblance of riba): even though wrought items are individually specified, they retain their nature as thaman (price), so the semblance of riba exists if possession is delayed. Therefore, possession remains necessary. The passage then defines 'separation' (iftiraq) as bodily separation (iftiraq bil-abdan), providing examples: if both parties walk away together, sleep, or faint, the contract remains valid. This is supported by an incident from Ibn Umar (رضي الله عنه) in which he instructs that if the other party jumps off a roof to cause bodily separation, you should jump with him to prevent separation. The commentary clarifies that the condition of possession is comprehensive and that the definition of separation is physical departure.

Key Terms
مضروب (mudrib): Coined gold or silver (e.g., dinars and dirhams).
مصوغ (musawwagh): Wrought gold or silver (e.g., jewellery, vessels).
شبہ الرھوا (shubhat al-riba): Semblance of riba; a situation that closely resembles prohibited usury.
افتراق بالا بدان (iftiraq bil-abdan): Bodily separation; physical departure of the contracting parties from the session.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does 'separation' (iftiraq) in sarf mean?
A) Separation of one countervalue from the other.
B) Bodily separation of the contracting parties.
C) Separation of the contract from the session.
D) Separation of the goods from the price.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, possession of both countervalues is required before the parties separate bodily; this applies to all gold/silver items, including wrought ones, to avoid the semblance of riba.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Ruling on Sarf: Excess and Hand-to-Hand Exchange
States ruling on sarf with hadith proof and condition of immediate exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling gold for silver with excess, identify the condition of immediate possession, and explain the effect of stipulating an option or term, including the intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
In sarf, excess is allowed between different genera, but immediate hand-to-hand exchange is required; options and terms invalidate unless dropped in session.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the core rules of the sarf contract—the exchange of gold and silver. You already know that riba is prohibited. Here, the author establishes the conditions under which such an exchange is permissible: although excess in quantity is allowed because gold and silver are different genera, the exchange must be hand-to-hand before the parties separate. The passage also tackles a subtle issue: what if the contract includes a condition like an option or a deferred term? And what if that condition is later dropped? The answers reveal a fascinating intra-Hanafi dispute between the majority and Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its components
The author states that excess is permissible but immediate possession is obligatory. Distinguish between two aspects: the permissibility of tafadul and the condition of taqabud.
Excess (tafadul) is allowed because gold and silver are not the same genus.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The hadith 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand' establishes the rule. Note the phrase 'illa ha wa ha' (except hand to hand) which makes possession a condition.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi and an-Nasa'i.
3
Understand the condition of taqabud
The contract is invalid if the parties separate before taking possession of both or even one countervalue. This is because the condition of possession is lost.
Possession must occur in the same session before separation.
4
Analyze the prohibition of option and term
Stipulating an option (khiyar al-shart) or a deferred term (ajal) is invalid in sarf because each prevents or delays the required immediate possession. Option means possession is not obligatory; term means obligatory possession is lost.
Other options like khiyar al-ayb are valid.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute with Zufar
If an option is stipulated but dropped in the session, the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the contract becomes valid because the invalidating factor is removed before it is established. Imam Zufar maintains that the contract was fasid from inception and remains so. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
The practical difference: under the majority, the contract can be saved; under Zufar, a new contract is needed.

ہوئی تو اس کے لیے اس عوض پر قبضہ کرنا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال خیار شرط کی صورت میں قبضہ مستحق یعنی واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے اور میعاد کی شرط لگانے سے واجب شدہ قبضہ فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس خیار شرط کے ساتھ قبضہ لگانا درست ہے۔ ہاں عقد صرف میں خیار عیب اور خیار روئیت دونوں ثابت ہوتے ہیں لیکن خیار روئیت معین عوض میں ثابت ہو گا دین میں ثابت نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عقد صرف میں خیار کی شرط لگائی مگر مجلس عقد ہی میں من لہ الخیار نے اس کو ساقط کر دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ عقد جائز ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ مفسد یعنی شرط خیار جب مستحکم اور ثابت ہونے سے پہلے پہلے مرتفع ہو گیا تو فساد دور ہو کر عقد جائز ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام زفر فرماتے ہیں کہ خیار شرط کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہو گیا ہے اور جو چیز فاسد ہو کر منعقد ہوتی ہے وہ جائز ہو کر عود نہیں کرتی بلکہ فاسد ہی رہتی ہے، اس لیے خیار ساقط کرنے کے باوجود یہ عقد جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
And if he sells gold for silver, excess is permissible due to lack of homogeneity, and hand-to-hand delivery is obligatory due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand.' Then if they separate in sarf before the two countervalues or one of them, the contract becomes invalid due to the loss of the condition, which is possession. For this reason, it is not valid to stipulate an option therein nor a term, because by the one, possession does not remain obligatory, and by the second, the obligatory possession is lost. Except if the option is dropped in the session, then it returns to permissibility because the corruption is removed before it becomes established. And regarding this there is a difference with Zufar. Translation: And if gold is sold in exchange for silver, excess (i.e., one being less and the other more) is permissible because they are not of the same genus. And mutual possession in the session is obligatory because the Holy Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Gold in exchange for silver is riba except hand to hand.' Then if the contracting parties separate in the sarf contract before taking possession of both countervalues or one of them, the contract becomes invalid because the condition, i.e., possession, has been lost. Therefore, it is not valid to stipulate an option in the sarf contract nor to stipulate a term. Because by one of them, the right to possession does not remain, and by the second, the right to possession is lost. But if the option is dropped in the session, the contract becomes valid and returns to permissibility because the corruption is removed before it becomes established. And Imam Zufar differs on this. Commentary: The example of the ruling is that if gold is sold in exchange for silver, then excess (tafadul) is permissible, and the reason for permissibility is the absence of homogeneity of genus. Because when homogeneity of genus is absent, selling with excess is permissible. However, mutual possession of both countervalues in the session is obligatory because the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Selling gold in exchange for silver is forbidden except with take and give, i.e., hand to hand.' And if the contracting parties separate in the sarf contract before taking possession of both countervalues or one of them, the sarf contract becomes invalid. Because the condition for the validity of the sarf contract, i.e., possession of the countervalues, has been lost. And since separation from the session without possession invalidates the sarf contract, therefore in the sarf contract it is not valid to stipulate an option nor a term. The case of option is that one of the contracting parties says: 'I have bought these dinars in exchange for these dirhams on the condition that I have a three-day option.' And the case of term is that he says: 'I have bought these dinars in exchange for these dirhams on the condition that I will give the said dirhams after one month.' The reason for invalidity in both cases is that the stipulated option prevents the establishment of ownership for the one without option. Thus, ownership of one countervalue is not established for the one without option, and when ownership is not established, it is not obligatory for him to take possession. Hence, in the case of stipulated option, possession is not obligatory; and in the case of term, the obligatory possession is lost. Whereas in the sarf contract, possession before separation is a condition, therefore it is not valid to stipulate an option nor a term. However, in the sarf contract, option of defect and option of sight are both established, but option of sight is established for specific countervalue, not for debt. The author of Hidaya says: If in a sarf contract an option is stipulated, but the one having the option drops it in the very session, then according to us the contract becomes valid, but according to Imam Zufar it does not become valid. Our proof is that when the invalidating factor, i.e., the option condition, is removed before it becomes firmly established, the corruption is removed and the contract becomes valid. Imam Zufar says that due to the option condition the contract became fasid, and a thing that becomes fasid by contract does not return to being valid, but remains fasid. Therefore, even after dropping the option, this contract is not valid.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling states that in a sarf contract (exchange of gold and silver), it is permissible to sell with an excess (tafadul) because gold and silver are not the same genus (jins). However, the contract requires immediate hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) before the parties separate from the session. The proof is the hadith: 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand.' If the parties separate before taking possession of either or both countervalues, the contract becomes invalid. Therefore, no option (khiyar) condition or deferment (ajal) is valid in a sarf contract because these would prevent or delay the required possession. An exception: if an option is stipulated but dropped in the session before the contract becomes final, the contract becomes valid because the corruption is removed before it is established. Imam Zufar differs, holding that the contract remains fasid even after dropping the option because it was initially concluded with a corrupt condition. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and his disciples) is that the contract becomes valid upon dropping the option in the session. This difference has practical consequences: under the Hanafi view, the parties can still execute the exchange, while under Zufar's view, a new contract would be needed.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): A contract for the exchange of gold and silver, or currency, where immediate hand-to-hand delivery is required.
تقابض (taqabud): Mutual physical possession or delivery of both countervalues in the contract session.
تفاضل (tafadul): Excess in quantity between the two items exchanged, e.g., selling one dinar for ten dirhams.
خیار (khiyar): A stipulated option to rescind the contract within a specified period.
اجل (ajal): A deferred term for payment or delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sarf contract (gold for silver), what happens if the parties stipulate a three-day option but then drop it in the same session?
A) The contract remains invalid according to all Hanafi scholars.
B) The contract becomes valid according to Abu Hanifa and the majority, but remains invalid according to Imam Zufar.
C) The contract is automatically valid because the option was dropped.
D) The contract is valid only if they also exchange the items in that session.

Key Takeaway
In a sarf contract, excess between different genera is allowed, but immediate hand-to-hand exchange is a condition; options and terms invalidate unless the option is dropped in the session before the contract becomes final.

Prohibition of Disposing of the Sarf Price Before Possession
Ruling with qiyas proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that the price in sarf is treated as mabee' and state the consequence of disposing of it before possession, while distinguishing the majority view from Imam Zufar's position.

Core Idea
In sarf, the price is an object of sale; disposing before possession invalidates the second transaction.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a crucial ruling in sarf (currency exchange): one cannot use the dirhams or dinars received in a sarf contract before physically taking possession. The author provides a qiyas (analogy) to the general rule of not selling what one does not possess, and addresses an objection from Imam Zufar. Understanding this ruling is essential for ensuring that the Shariah condition of hand-to-hand exchange (taqabud) is respected in modern currency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its practical example
Read the passage and note the explicit ruling: it is not permissible to dispose of the price in sarf before possession. Then examine the example given: selling a dinar for ten dirhams, then using those dirhams to buy a garment before taking possession of the dirhams. The garment purchase is ruled fasid (invalid).
The ruling applies to the second transaction, not the sarf contract itself.
2
Extract the reasoning (qiyas) behind the ruling
The author argues that the price in sarf is considered a mabee' (object of sale) because a sale contract requires an object, and there are only two countervalues. Therefore, each countervalue is treated as mabee'. Then the general rule applies: selling a mabee' before possession is prohibited.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) to the prohibition of selling what one does not possess.
3
Analyze the counterargument from Imam Zufar
Imam Zufar argues that the dirhams are not specified (ghayr muta'ayyin); when used to buy a garment, the contract refers to absolute dirhams, not the specific ones from the sarf. Thus, the prohibition does not apply because one does possess absolute dirhams in a general sense.
Zufar's view would make the garment purchase valid.
4
Understand the Hanafi response and the salam analogy
The Hanafi response maintains that even unspecified items can be mabee', citing the salam contract where the object (muslim fih) is unspecified yet treated as mabee'. Therefore, specification is not necessary for the prohibition.
This reinforces that in sarf, the price is mabee' regardless of specification.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and practical application
The majority view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) is that the second transaction is fasid. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa. In practice, one must take physical possession of the sarf countervalue before using it for any other transaction.
Imam Zufar's view is considered a minority opinion within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال ولا يجوز التصرف في ثمن الصرف قبل قبضه حتى لو باع دينارا بعشرة دراهم ولم يقبض العشرة حتى اشترى بها ثوبا فالبيع في الثوب فاسد لان القبض مستحق بالعقد حقا لله تعالى وفي تجويزه فواته وكان ينبغي ان يجوز العقد في الثوب كما نقل عن زفر لان الدراهم لا تتعين فينصرف العقد الى مطلقها ولكنا نقول الثمن في باب الصرف مبيع لان البيع لا بد له من مبيع ولا شيء سوى الثمنين فيجعل كل واحد منهما مبيعا لعدم الاولوية وبيع المبيع قبل القبض لا يجوز وليس من ضرورة كونه مبيعا ان يكون متعينا كما في المسلم فيه. ترجمہ: اور بیع صرف کے ثمن میں قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر ایک دینار دس درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا اور دس درہم پر قبضہ نہیں کیا، حتی کہ ان دس درہم کے عوض ایک کپڑا خرید لیا تو کپڑے کی بیع فاسد ہے۔ اس لیے کہ عقد صرف کی وجہ سے قبضہ اللہ تعالیٰ کا حق بن کر واجب ہے حالانکہ ایسا تصرف جائز قرار دینے میں اس کا فوت ہونا لازم آتا ہے اور مناسب تھا کہ کپڑے کی بیع بھی جائز ہو جیسا کہ امام زفر سے منقول ہے کیونکہ دراہم متعین نہیں ہوتے پس کپڑے کی بیع مطلق دراہم کی طرف لوٹے گی۔ لیکن ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ثمن، باب صرف میں مبیع ہوتا ہے کیونکہ بیع کے لیے مبیع ہونا ضروری ہے حالانکہ (یہاں) دو ثمنوں کے علاوہ کوئی چیز نہیں ہے۔ پس عدم اولویت کی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کو مبیع قرار دیا جائے گا اور مبیع کی بیع قبضہ سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کے مبیع ہونے سے متعین ہونا لازم نہیں آتا جیسے مسلم فیہ میں ہے۔
He said: It is not permissible to dispose of the price in sarf before taking possession of it. For example, if he sells a dinar for ten dirhams but does not take possession of the ten dirhams, and then with those dirhams buys a garment, then the sale of the garment is fasid (invalid). Because possession is an obligation (haqq Allah) due to the contract, and in allowing such disposal, the obligation would be lost. It would have been appropriate that the sale of the garment be valid, as narrated from Zufar, because dirhams are not specified ('ayn), so the contract would refer to absolute dirhams. But we say: The price in the context of sarf is an object of sale (mabee'), because a sale must have an object of sale, and there is nothing except the two prices. Due to lack of priority, each of them is made an object of sale. And selling the object of sale before taking possession is not permissible. And it is not necessary for it being an object of sale that it be specified, just as in the case of salam (Muslim fih).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof based on qiyas (analogy) and contains an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar. The ruling is that one cannot dispose of the price (thaman) in a sarf contract before taking possession of it. The example: if someone sells a dinar for ten dirhams (sarf contract) but does not yet take possession of the dirhams, and then uses those dirhams to buy a garment, the purchase of the garment is invalid (fasid). The reason is that the possession of the dirhams is an obligation established by the sarf contract (as a right of Allah), and using the dirhams before possession would cause this obligation to be lost. Imam Zufar reportedly held a different view: he considered the second transaction valid because the dirhams are not specific (ghayr muta'ayyin); the contract of buying the garment would refer to absolute dirhams (not the specific ones owed from the sarf). The Hanafi response is that in sarf, the price (thaman) is treated as an object of sale (mabee'), because a sale necessarily has an object, and here there are only two countervalues (the dinar and the dirhams). Since neither has priority, both are considered objects of sale. Selling an object of sale (mabee') before taking possession is prohibited by the Shariah rule that 'one cannot sell what one does not possess.' This analogy is supported by the case of salam (advance payment for future delivery), where the object (muslim fih) is not necessarily specified at the time of contract, yet it is treated as mabee'. Therefore, even though the dirhams are unspecified, they are considered mabee' in the context of sarf, and selling them before possession is invalid. This difference has practical application: under the Hanafi view, the buyer of the dinar cannot use the dirhams for another purchase until he takes possession; under Zufar's view, he could.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): Price or one of the two countervalues in a sarf contract, which is considered an object of sale (mabee') in the context of the ruling.
مبيع (mabee'): Object of sale. In sarf, both countervalues are treated as mabee' because the contract requires an object and there is nothing else.
مسلم فيه (muslim fih): The object of a salam contract (advance sale with deferred delivery), which is unspecified at the time of contract.
قبض (qabd): Possession, specifically physical taking of the object. In sarf, it is a condition for validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone buys a dinar with dirhams in a sarf contract and then uses those dirhams to purchase a separate item before taking possession of the dirhams?
A) The purchase is valid because the dirhams are not specified.
B) The purchase is fasid (invalid) because the dirhams are considered mabee' and cannot be disposed of before possession.
C) The purchase is valid only if the seller agrees to accept the dirhams as payment.
D) The purchase is automatically valid because the sarf contract is complete upon offer and acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In sarf, the price is legally considered an object of sale; thus, disposing of it before physical possession invalidates any subsequent transaction using that price.

Curing a Defective Sarf Contract: Dropping Khiyar al-Shart in the Session
Explaining prohibition of khiyar al-shart in sarf and its nullification in the session

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a sarf contract with a khiyar al-shart condition that is dropped in the same session, and distinguish Abu Hanifa's position from Imam Zufar's.

Core Idea
In sarf, if khiyar al-shart is dropped before it becomes established, the contract returns to validity.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical nuance in sarf (currency exchange): what happens when a prohibited option is inserted but immediately removed? The text explains why such a condition corrupts the contract and then presents the intra-Hanafi dispute over the remedy. Understanding this nuance is crucial for correctly applying the rules of sarf in contemporary currency transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the corrupting element
Recognize that stipulating khiyar al-shart or a term in a sarf contract corrupts it because it prevents immediate possession, which is a condition for validity.
2
Note the general Hanafi ruling
Both khiyar al-shart and a deferred term invalidate the sarf contract because possession is not immediate.
Exceptions: khiyar al-ayb and khiyar al-ru'yah are valid in sarf.
3
Identify the dispute scenario
The dispute arises when the khiyar al-shart condition is dropped in the same session.
4
State the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position and proof
The contract becomes valid. Proof: the corrupting factor was removed before becoming established, so the contract returns to validity.
5
State Imam Zufar's position and proof
The contract remains invalid. Proof: the contract was initially invalid and cannot become valid later.
The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصرف
اشرف الہدایہ جلد نم عوض اس شرط پر خریدا کہ میں مذکورہ در اہم ایک ماہ بعد دوں گا۔ ان دونوں صورتوں میں عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ خیار شرط چونکہ من لا خیار لہ کیلئے ملک ثابت ہونے کو روکتا ہے۔ اسلئے احد العوضین پر من لا خیارلہ کی ملک ثابت نہ ہوگی اور جب اس کی ملک ثابت نہ ہوئی تو اس کیلئے اس عوض پر قبضہ کرنا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ بہر حال خیار شرط کی صورت میں قبضہ مستحق یعنی واجب نہیں ہوتا ہے اور میعاد کی شرط لگانے سے واجب شدہ قبضہ فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس خیار شرط کے ساتھ قبضہ واجب نہیں ہوتا اور میعاد کی شرط کے ساتھ واجب شدہ قبضہ فوت ہو جاتا ہے۔ حالانکہ عقد صرف میں جدا ہونے سے پہلے پہلے قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اسلئے عقد صرف میں نہ خیار کی شرط لگانا درست ہے اور نہ میعاد کی شرط لگانا درست ہے۔ ہاں عقد صرف میں خیار عیب اور خیار رویت دونوں ثابت ہوتے ہیں لیکن خیار رویت معین عوض میں ثابت ہو گا دین میں ثابت نہ ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر عقد صرف میں خیار کی شرط لگائی مگر مجلس عقدہی میں من لہ الخیار نے اس کو ساقط کر دیا تو ہمارے نزدیک یہ عقد جائز ہو جائے گا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک جائز نہ ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل تو یہ ہے کہ مفسد یعنی شرط خیار جب مستحکم اور ثابت ہونے سے پہلے پہلے مرتفع ہو گیا تو فساد دور ہو کر عقد جائز ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ خیار شرط کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہو گیا ہے اور جو چیز فاسد ہو کر منعقد ہوتی ہے وہ جائز ہو کر عود نہیں کرتی بلکہ فاسد ہی رہتی ہے۔ اسلئے ” خیار ساقط کرنے کے باوجود یہ عقد جائز نہیں ہو گا۔
Book of Sarf. Ashraf al-Hidayah volume... Purchased on the condition that I will give the mentioned dirhams after one month. In both cases, the reason for impermissibility is that khiyar al-shart prevents ownership from being established for the one who has no option. Therefore, ownership of one of the counter-values will not be established for the one with no option, and when his ownership is not established, taking possession of that counter-value is not obligatory for him. Anyway, in the case of khiyar al-shart, possession is not due (obligatory), and stipulating a term causes the obligatory possession to be lost. Thus, with khiyar al-shart, possession is not obligatory, and with a term condition, the already obligatory possession is lost. However, in a sarf contract, possession before separation is a condition. Therefore, in a sarf contract, neither stipulating an option nor stipulating a term is valid. Yes, in sarf, options of defect and inspection are both established, but the option of inspection will be established in a specific counter-value, not in a debt. The author of Hidayah says: If a condition of option is stipulated in a sarf contract, but the one who has the option drops it in the same session of the contract, then in our view the contract becomes valid, and in Imam Zufar's view it will not be valid. Our proof is that when the corrupting factor (the condition of option) is removed before it becomes firm and established, the corruption disappears and the contract becomes valid. Imam Zufar says: The contract became invalid due to the option condition, and something that is contracted as invalid does not return to validity but remains invalid. Therefore, despite dropping the option, this contract will not be valid.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of khiyar al-shart (option to rescind) in a sarf (currency exchange) contract. The Hidayah commentator explains that stipulating either an option period or a deferred term invalidates the contract because possession is a necessary condition in sarf, and such conditions prevent immediate possession. He notes that options of defect and inspection are still valid. The core dispute arises when the option condition is dropped in the same session: the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) holds that the contract becomes valid because the corrupting factor ceased before it became established. Imam Zufar argues that the contract was initially invalid and cannot become valid later. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that temporary corruption that is removed before it becomes firm does not leave a permanent defect. This follows the general Hanafi approach of prioritizing the removal of impediments when possible.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyar al-shart): An option to rescind a contract stipulated as a condition for a specified period.
عقد صرف (aqd al-sarf): A contract of exchanging two types of ribawi items (gold/silver or currencies) on the spot.
خیار عیب (khiyar al-'ayb): The option to annul a sale due to a defect in the commodity.

Checkpoint

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Disposal of Price in Sarf Before Possession: Invalid
Ruling and rebuttal of Imam Zufar's qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prohibits disposing of the price in a sarf contract before possession and evaluate Imam Zufar's contrary qiyas.

Core Idea
In sarf, both items are subject matter — disposing before possession invalidates the sale, even if fungible.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical issue in sarf (currency exchange): may one use the price received in a sarf contract to purchase another item before taking possession? The author rules it invalid, and then engages with a contrary view from Imam Zufar. We will explore the legal reasoning and the underlying analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and the hypothetical
State the ruling: disposing of the price in sarf before possession is not permissible. The hypothetical: selling a dinar for ten dirhams, then buying a cloth with those dirhams before possessing them.
The cloth sale is the focus of the dispute.
2
Understand the Hanafi proof
The proof: possession is a right of Allah (due to riba prevention). In sarf, both items are considered subject matter (mabi') because there is no preference between them. Selling subject matter before possession is invalid.
The key concept: 'la uluwiyya' (no preference).
3
Examine Imam Zufar's qiyas
Imam Zufar argues: dirhams are fungible (not determinate), so the cloth sale refers to absolute dirhams, making it valid. This is a qiyas to a regular sale with an unspecified price.
The effective cause (illa) is the non-specification of dirhams.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The response: In sarf, the dirhams are not just price; they are also subject matter because there is no other subject matter. Thus, they are treated like mabi', and selling mabi' before possession is impermissible regardless of specification.
The Hanafi response overrides the qiyas by identifying a special characteristic of sarf.
5
Recognize the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if one buys cloth with sarf price before possession, the sale is invalid per Hanafi, valid per Zufar. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is invalidity.
This difference has real-world implications for currency exchange transactions.

وليس من ضرورة كونه...... الخ - سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب بیچ صرف کے دونوں بدل من وجہ مبیع میں تو ان کو متعین ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مبیع متعین ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ آپ ان
Disposing of the price in sarf before possession is not permissible. He said: It is not permissible to dispose of the price in sarf before taking possession; even if he sold a dinar for ten dirhams and did not take possession of the ten until he bought a cloth with them, then the sale of the cloth is invalid because possession is due by the contract as a right of Allah, and in allowing it there is a loss of that right. It would have been appropriate that the sale of the cloth be permissible as transmitted from Zufar, because dirhams are not specified, so the contract refers to absolute dirhams. But we say: The price in the chapter of sarf is a subject matter, because a sale cannot be without a subject matter, and there is nothing besides the two prices, so each of them is made a subject matter due to lack of preference, and selling the subject matter before possession is not permissible. It is not necessary for it to be a subject matter that it be specified, as in salam. [Translation continues in Urdu...]
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of disposing of the price in a sarf contract before taking possession. The author presents a hypothetical: if someone sells a dinar for ten dirhams and, before taking possession of the dirhams, uses those dirhams to buy a cloth, the purchase of the cloth is invalid. The reason is that in a sarf contract, possession is a right of Allah (due to the prohibition of riba), and disposing of the price before possession would lead to losing that right. The author then discusses Imam Zufar's opposing view, who argues that since dirhams are fungible (not specified), the contract for the cloth should be valid as it refers to absolute dirhams. The Hanafi response is that in a sarf contract, both items of exchange are considered subject matter (mabi') because a sale requires a subject matter, and since there is no preference to treat one as price and the other as commodity, each is considered a subject matter in some respect. Therefore, disposing of the subject matter before possession is invalid, regardless of specification. The text further elaborates that possession cannot be dropped by the parties because it is Allah's right, and it is obligatory to prevent riba. The argument between the Hanafi position and Imam Zufar revolves around the nature of dirhams as specified or unspecified, but the Hanafi position treats them as subject matter in the context of sarf. The passage concludes by addressing a potential objection regarding the dual nature of both items as price and subject matter, and the Hanafi response that the doubt between permissibility and non-permissibility results in non-permissibility.

Key Terms
ثمن (thaman): The price or one of the two counter-values in a sale; in sarf, both items are considered thaman.
مبیع (mabi'): The subject matter of sale; that which is sold.
قبض (qabd): Physical possession or taking delivery of the item.
بیع مقایضہ (bay' muqayyadah): A barter sale where goods are exchanged for goods (not money).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling if someone sells a dinar for ten dirhams in a sarf contract and then, before taking possession of the dirhams, uses them to buy a cloth?
A) The purchase of the cloth is valid because dirhams are fungible.
B) The purchase of the cloth is invalid because the dirhams are considered subject matter in sarf.
C) The purchase of the cloth is valid only if both parties agree.
D) The purchase of the cloth is valid if the dirhams are unspecified.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers both countervalues in sarf as subject matter, making disposal before possession invalid even if fungible; Imam Zufar's contrary view is not relied upon.

Disposal Before Possession in Sarf: Divine Right and the Doubt Principle
Explains prohibition of disposing sarf counter-values before possession and a sub-case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that disposal before possession in sarf is impermissible, explain the reason (haqq Allah and riba prevention), and evaluate the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding disposal of unspecified dirhams.

Core Idea
Disposal before possession in sarf is haram because it violates a divine right; doubt about legal description triggers impermissibility.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a core rule in sarf (exchange of gold/silver): neither counter-value may be disposed of before possession. The author explains that the obligation to take possession is a divine right (haqq Allah) that cannot be waived, as its purpose is to prevent riba. A practical sub-case illustrates the rule, and an intra-Hanafi difference with Imam Zufar is presented and refuted using the principle of doubt (shakk) when legal descriptions conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Locate the statement that disposal before possession in sarf is impermissible. Note that it applies to both counter-values because each is considered a price (thaman).
The ruling is from Al-Quduri's matn.
2
Understand the reason: possession is a divine right
Explain why possession is wajib: it is Allah's right to prevent riba. The parties cannot waive it because it is haqq Allah, not haqq al-'abd. This makes the prohibition binding regardless of agreement.
Compare with waivable rights in contracts (haqq al-'abd).
3
Examine the sub-case: buying cloth with dirhams before possession
Apply the ruling to the scenario: sell dinar for dirhams (sarf), then use dirhams to buy cloth before possession. The cloth sale is fasid because it nullifies Allah's right.
The dirhams are still a counter-value in the sarf, even if used for another purchase.
4
Analyze Imam Zufar's qiyas objection and the Hanafi response
Imam Zufar argued that since the dirhams are not actually specified (they are a debt), the cloth purchase should be permissible like buying with absolute dirhams. The Hanafi response: each counter-value is both mabi' and thaman min wajh, creating doubt that tips the scale to impermissibility.
The response uses the principle of mabi' min wajh to block qiyas.
5
Apply the doubt principle (shakk) to reconcile dual legal descriptions
When a counter-value is simultaneously mabi' (prevents disposal) and thaman (permits disposal), doubt arises. In Hanafi usul, when permissible and impermissible conflict, impermissibility prevails to avoid risk of sin.
This is a maxim: 'al-khuruj min al-khilaf mustahabb' but here it becomes wajib due to divine right.
