ثابت ہو گیا کہ عقد صرف میں قبضہ کا واجب ہونا اللہ کا حق ہے اور دس در اہم پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے ان کے عوض کپڑے کا تھان خریدنے میں اللہ کے اس حق کو فوت کرنا لازم آتا ہے۔ اور اللہ کے حق کو فوت کرنا قطعا نا جائز ہے۔ اسلئے قبضہ کئے بغیر دس درہم کے عوض کپڑے کا تھان خرید مانا جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قیاس کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے مذکورہ دس دراہم کے عوض کپڑا خریدنا جائز ہو۔ جیسا کہ یہ امام زفر سے بھی منقول ہے۔ کیونکہ دراہم متعین کرنے کے باوجود متعین نہیں ہوتے ۔ پس کپڑے کی بیع مطلق دراہم کی طرف لوٹے گی ۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے کپڑا خریدا اور اس کو بیع صرف کے بدل کی طرف منسوب نہیں کیا بلکہ مطلق دراہم کی طرف منسوب کیا تو یہ جائز ہے۔ پس اسی طرح جب بیچ صرف کے بدل کی طرف منسوب کیا ہو تو بھی جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا کیونکہ در اہم متعین نہیں ہوتے اگر چہ ان کی طرف اشارہ ہی کیوں نہ کیا گیا ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ کپڑے کی بیع کو بیع صرف کے بدل دس در اہم ) کی طرف منسوب کرنا اور مطلق رکھنا دونوں برابر ہیں۔ ہماری طرف سے اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عقد صرف ، عقد بیع ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد صرف میں مبادلہ مال بالمال ہوتا ہے۔ اور چونکہ مبادلہ مال بالمال کا نام بیج ہے اسلئے عقد صرف بھی عقد بیع ہوگا اور بیع بیع اور شمن دونوں پر مشتمل ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ یہاں دونوں عوض شمن ہیں۔ اسلئے کہ دینار بھی از قبیلہ ثمن ہے۔ اور دراہم بھی از قبیلۂ شمن ہیں اور کسی عوض کو چونکہ مبیع بنانے پر کوئی مرجح موجود نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے دونوں میں سے ہر ایک من وجہ مبیع اور من وجہ شمن ہوگا ۔ جیسا کہ بیع مقایضہ یعنی بیع العرض بالعرض میں ہر ایک من وجہ مبیع اور من وجہ تمن ہوتا ہے اور مبیع پر قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے اس میں تصرف کرنا چونکہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے عقد صرف کے عوض یعنی دس دراہم میں قبضہ کرنے سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔ اگر کوئی یہ اعتراض کرے کہ عقد صرف کا عوض اگر من وجہ مبیع ہے تو من وجہ شمن بھی ہے اور قبضہ سے پہلے شمن میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہے۔ لہذا عقد صرف کے عوض یعنی دس دراہم میں بھی قبضہ سے پہلے تصرف کرنا جائز ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ ثمن ہونے کا تقاضہ تو یہ ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے بیع صرف کے عوض میں تصرف کرنا جائز ہوا اور مبیع ہونے کا تقاضہ یہ ہے کہ قبضہ سے پہلے تصرف جائز نہ ہو۔ پس جب جوا او اور عدم جواز میں شک پیدا ہو گیا تو شک کی وجہ سے تصرف کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
وليس من ضرورة كونه...... الخ - سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔
سوال یہ ہے کہ جب بیچ صرف کے دونوں بدل من وجہ مبیع میں تو ان کو متعین ہونا چاہئے کیونکہ مبیع متعین ہوتی ہے۔ حالانکہ آپ ان کے متعین ہونے کے قائل نہیں ہیں؟
جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کسی چیز کا مبیع ہونا اس کے متعین ہونے کو ستلزم نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلا مسلم فیہ بالاتفاق مبیع ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن متعین نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ واجب ہوتی ہے۔
Book of Sarf. Explanation: The ruling is that in a sarf contract, it is not permissible to dispose of either counter-value before taking possession. Al-Quduri said that it is not permissible to dispose of the price (thaman) in a sarf contract before possession. And since each of its two counter-values is a price (thaman), therefore disposal before possession will not be permitted in either. Deriving a sub-case from this, it is said: If someone sold one dinar for ten dirhams, and without taking possession of the ten dirhams, bought a cloth with them, then the sale of the cloth is invalid. Because the sale of one dinar for ten dirhams is a sarf contract. And in a sarf contract, possession is obligatory due to the right of Allah. This is why possession is not waived by the contractors' waiver — meaning if both contractors agree to waive possession of the sarf counter-values, possession is not waived by their agreement; rather it remains obligatory as before. Because the obligation of possession is not their right but Allah's right. And Allah's right is because without possession, riba necessarily occurs, and riba is haram, and being haram is Allah's right, not the servant's. In any case, it is established that the obligation of possession in a sarf contract is Allah's right, and buying a cloth with the ten dirhams before taking possession necessarily entails nullifying Allah's right. And nullifying Allah's right is absolutely impermissible. Therefore, buying a cloth with the ten dirhams without possession is not permissible. The author of Al-Hidayah says: Qiyas requires that buying a cloth with the mentioned ten dirhams before possession should be permissible, as is also transmitted from Imam Zufar. Because dirhams, despite being specified, are not actually specified (mut'ayyan). So the sale of cloth will refer to absolute dirhams. Thus if someone bought a cloth and did not attribute it to the counter-value of the sarf contract but attributed it to absolute dirhams, it is permissible. Similarly, when attributed to the counter-value of the sarf contract, it should also be permissible because dirhams are not specified even if they are referred to. So it becomes clear that attributing the sale of cloth to the counter-value of the sarf (ten dirhams) and leaving it absolute are equal. Our response to this is: The sarf contract is a sale contract because in a sarf contract there is an exchange of property for property. And since the name of exchange of property for property is sale, the sarf contract is also a sale contract, and a sale consists of both a sold item (mabi') and a price (thaman). However, here both counter-values are prices (thaman) because the dinar is of the category of price and the dirhams are also of the category of price. And since there is no preference (murajjih) to make either counter-value the sold item (mabi'), each of them is, from one aspect, a sold item (mabi' min wajh) and from another aspect, a price (thaman min wajh), just as in a barter sale (bay' muqayada) i.e., sale of commodity for commodity, each is from one aspect a sold item and from another aspect a price. And since it is not permissible to dispose of the sold item before taking possession, therefore it will not be permissible to dispose of the sarf counter-value (ten dirhams) before taking possession. If someone objects: If the sarf counter-value is from one aspect a sold item (mabi'), it is also from one aspect a price (thaman), and it is permissible to dispose of the price before possession; therefore it should also be permissible to dispose of the sarf counter-value (ten dirhams) before possession. The answer is: The requirement of being a price is that it is permissible to dispose of the sarf counter-value before possession, and the requirement of being a sold item is that disposal before possession is not permissible. So when doubt arises between permissibility and impermissibility, disposal is not permissible due to the doubt. 'And it is not necessary that it be specified...' etc. — this is the answer to a question. The question is: When both counter-values in a sarf contract are from one aspect sold items (mabi' min wajh), they should be specified (mut'ayyan) because a sold item is specified, whereas you are not of the opinion that they are specified. The answer is: That something being a sold item does not necessitate its being specified. For example, 'muslam fih' (the subject matter of salam) is by consensus a sold item, but it is not specified; rather it is obligatory as a debt in the liability of the seller.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion on a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah. It opens by stating the foundational ruling: in a sarf (exchange of gold and silver) contract, neither counter-value can be disposed of before possession. The author explains that this is because each counter-value is considered a price (thaman), and the obligation to take possession is a divine right (haqq Allah), not something the parties can waive. The reasoning is that failure to take possession leads to riba, which is prohibited by Allah. A sub-case illustrates the point: if someone sells a dinar for ten dirhams (a sarf contract) and then uses those dirhams to buy a cloth before taking possession of the dirhams, the cloth purchase is invalid (fasid). This is because it would involve nullifying Allah's right to have possession taken in the original sarf. The text then presents a qiyas-based objection attributed to Imam Zufar: since the dirhams are not actually specified (they are a payment obligation, not a specific coin), the cloth purchase should be permissible—just as buying a cloth with absolute (unspecified) dirhams is permissible. The Hanafi response (from the author of Al-Hidayah) refutes this: the sarf contract is a type of sale, and in a sale each item is both a sold item (mabi') and a price (thaman) from different aspects. Since the sold item cannot be disposed of before possession, and there is doubt (shakk) as to whether the dirhams are mabi' or thaman, disposal is impermissible due to the doubt. Finally, an objection is raised: if they are mabi' min wajh, they should be specified, but the Hanafis do not consider them specified. The answer: being a sold item does not require specification, as exemplified by salam contracts where the subject matter (muslam fih) is a mabi' but is not specified—it is a debt in the liability.

Key Terms
بيع الصرف (bay' al-sarf): A contract exchanging gold or silver (or both) for gold or silver, such as dinar for dirhams.
قبض (qabd): Physical or constructive possession of the counter-value in a contract.
ثمن (thaman): Price; the counter-value given in exchange for the sold item.
مبيع (mabi'): The sold item; the object of sale.
ربوا (riba): Unlawful increase in exchange of certain types of property, especially gold and silver.
من وجہ (min wajh): From one aspect; used to indicate that something has multiple legal considerations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a sarf contract, why is buying a cloth with the dirhams (before taking possession of them) invalid?
A) Because the dirhams are specified and cannot be used until weighed.
B) Because it violates a divine right (haqq Allah) to take possession first to avoid riba.
C) Because the cloth is not a permissible item in sarf.
D) Because the seller did not consent to the cloth purchase.

Key Takeaway
Disposal before possession in sarf is impermissible because possession is a divine right to prevent riba, and doubt about legal description (mabi' vs thaman) triggers impermissibility to avoid sin.

Selling Gold for Silver by Estimation and a Mixed Sale Case
Ruling with proof followed by case application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the sarf rule that different-type transactions require immediate possession to a mixed sale, and determine which portion of payment corresponds to which item.

Core Idea
Gold for silver may be sold by estimation; in mixed sales, cash payment is for the ribawi item to satisfy the sarf condition.

The Hanafi school permits selling gold for silver by estimation because equality of weight is not required when types differ. The only condition is possession in the session, based on the hadith of Ubadah bin Samit. In a mixed sale combining a non-ribawi item (slave girl) with a ribawi item (silver necklace), the same principle applies: the payment for the necklace must be immediate, and any cash payment is presumed to cover that portion.

Guided Path
1
State the permissibility and condition
Identify the ruling: selling gold for silver by estimation is permissible. Recognize the condition: possession must occur in the session before separation.
This applies only when the types differ (gold vs silver).
2
Identify the dalil
Locate the proof: the hadith of Ubadah bin Samit: 'When these types differ, then sell as you wish as long as it is hand to hand.' This is the textual evidence for the ruling.
The hadith is a sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati dalala on this point.
3
Contrast with same-type sale
Note that selling gold for gold or silver for silver by estimation is haram due to the possibility of riba. Equality of weight and immediate possession are required there.
Even the possibility of riba is treated as actual riba in Hanafi law.
4
Analyze the mixed sale case
Examine the scenario: a slave girl (value 1000) with a silver necklace (value 1000) sold for 2000 total, with only 1000 paid in cash. Determine that the cash payment must be allocated to the necklace because its sale is a sarf transaction requiring immediate possession.
The default assumption is that the parties fulfilled the wajib of possession for the necklace.
5
Confirm allocation
Alternatively, if the sale was 1000 cash and 1000 credit, the cash is for the necklace because deferment (nasi'ah) is void in sarf but valid for the slave girl. The transaction is presumed valid.
This shows how sarf rules interact with mixed sales.

ترجمہ اور سونے کو چاندی کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ خلاف جنس میں برابری شرط نہیں ہے لیکن مجلس میں قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اس کے برخلاف اندازے سے اس کی بیع اس کی جنس کے عوض کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، سونے کی بیچ چاندی کے عوض اور چاندی کی بیچ سونے کے عوض اندازے سے جائز ہے خواہ وزن میں دونوں عوض برابر ہوں یا ایک کم اور ایک زائد ہو۔ کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں برابری شرط نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ عبادہ بن صامت کی حدیث:۔ اذا اختلفت هذه الاصناف فبيعوا كيف شتم اذا كان يداً بيد شاہد ہے۔ پس جب اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں دونوں عوضوں کا برابر ہونا شرط نہیں ہے تو اندازے اور انکل سے بیچنا بھی حرام نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ افتراق بالا بد ان سے پہلے پہلے قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور اس کی نقلی اور عقلی دلیلیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں۔ نقلی دلیل سے مراد حديث الذهب بالورق ربوا لاهاء وهاء ہے یعنی سونے کو چاندی کے عوض بچنار ہوا ہے مگر لے اور لا کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ یعنی اگر با ہم قبضہ ہو جائے تو جائز ہے اور اگر سونے کو اس کی جنس یعنی سونے کے عوض یا چاندی کو چاندی کے عوض اندازے اور انکل سے بیچا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے یعنی ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک عوض کم اور ایک عوض زائد ہو۔ اور پہلے بار بار گزر چکا ہے کہ احتمال ربوا بھی حقیقت ربوا کی طرح حرام ہے۔ اسلئے سونے یا چاندی کی بیع بجنسہ اندازے سے حرام اور نا جائز ہے۔
قال و من باع جارية قيمتها الف مثقال فضة وفى عنقها طوق فضة قميته الف مثقال بالفى مثقال فضة ونقدمن الثمن الف مثقال ثم افترقا فالذى نقد ثمن الفضة لان قبض حصة الطوق واجب في المجلس لكونه بدل الصرف والظاهر منه الاتيان بالواجب وكذا لواشتراهما بالفى مثقال الف نسيئة والف نقد فالنقد ثمن الطوق لان الاجل باطل فى الصرف جائز فى بيع الجارية والمباشرة على وجه الجواز هو الظاهر منهما
And it is permissible to sell gold for silver by estimation because equality is not a condition in it, but possession in the session is required for the reason we mentioned, unlike selling it for its own kind by estimation because of the possibility of riba. Translation: And selling gold for silver by estimation is permissible because in different types equality is not a condition, but possession in the session is a condition, for the reason we mentioned. Unlike selling it for its own kind by estimation because there is a possibility of riba. Explanation: The issue: Selling gold for silver and silver for gold by estimation is permissible whether the two counter-values are equal in weight or one is less and the other more. Because in case of difference of type, equality is not a condition, as the hadith of Ubadah bin Samit witnesses: 'When these types differ, then sell as you wish as long as it is hand to hand.' So when in case of difference of type equality of the two counter-values is not a condition, selling by estimation and measurement is also not haram. However, possession before separation (afraqa) is a condition, and its textual and rational proofs have passed earlier. The textual proof refers to the hadith 'Gold for silver is riba except hand to hand', i.e., selling gold for silver is riba except with take and give (i.e., hand to hand). That is, if possession occurs, it is permissible. And if gold is sold for its own kind (gold) or silver for its own kind by estimation, it is not permissible because there is a possibility of riba, i.e., it is possible that one counter-value is less and the other more. And it has been repeatedly mentioned earlier that the possibility of riba is also haram like actual riba. Therefore, selling gold or silver for its own kind by estimation is haram and impermissible. He (the author) said: And whoever sells a slave girl whose value is one thousand mithqals of silver, and around her neck is a silver necklace whose value is one thousand mithqals, for two thousand mithqals of silver, and he pays one thousand mithqals of the price in cash, then they separate, then what was paid in cash is the price of the silver (the necklace), because possession of the portion of the necklace is obligatory in the session as it is a counter-value of sarf, and the apparent (default) is that they performed the obligatory. Similarly, if he bought both (the slave girl and necklace) for two thousand mithqals, one thousand on credit and one thousand cash, then the cash payment is the price of the necklace, because deferment is void in sarf but allowed in the sale of the slave girl, and the default in the transaction is that it was done in a permissible manner.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First, it addresses selling gold for silver by estimation (jazaf). The author states it is permissible because equality of weight is not required when the types differ; the only condition is possession in the session. This is supported by the hadith of Ubadah bin Samit: 'When types differ, sell as you wish as long as it is hand to hand.' The text contrasts this with selling gold for gold or silver for silver by estimation, which is impermissible due to the risk of riba (even the possibility of riba is haram). Then a case is presented: a person sells a slave girl (whose value is 1000 dirhams) together with a silver necklace around her neck (value 1000 dirhams) for a total of 2000 dirhams. The buyer pays 1000 dirhams in cash and then they separate. The ruling: the 1000 dirhams paid are for the necklace (silver), not the slave girl. Why? Because the necklace portion involves a sarf exchange (silver for silver), and possession of that portion must occur in the session. The default assumption is that the parties fulfilled this obligatory possession. Similarly, if the sale was for 2000 dirhams with 1000 cash and 1000 credit, the cash payment is for the necklace because credit (nasi'ah) is invalid in sarf but valid in the sale of the slave girl, and the transaction is presumed valid.

Key Terms
مجازفة (mujāzafah): Selling by estimation, without measuring or weighing, based on approximation.
يداً بيد (yadan bi-yad): Hand to hand; immediate possession in the session of contract.
طوق (tawq): Necklace; here a silver necklace worn by the slave girl.

B) Because the hadith permits it as long as possession is hand to hand.
C) Because estimation eliminates the risk of riba.
D) Because the buyer and seller can agree to waive weighing.

Key Takeaway
Selling gold for silver by estimation is permissible as long as possession is immediate; in mixed sales, the cash payment is allocated to the ribawi item to satisfy the sarf condition.

The Sold Item Does Not Require Specification
Q&A on specification of sold item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that a sold item need not be specifically determined and apply it to the salam contract.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a sold item can be a liability not physically present—specification is not required for validity.

This brief passage addresses a common question in sales transactions: must the sold item be specifically identified at the time of contract? The Hanafi school answers no, using the salam contract as evidence. Understanding this principle is crucial for distinguishing valid deferred sales from invalid uncertain ones.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question and answer
Note that the question asks whether the sold item must be specific; the answer is negative.
The passage begins with a question (implied by 'کے متعین ہونے کے قائل نہیں ہیں؟') and provides a direct answer.
2
Extract the legal principle
The principle: 'کسی چیز کا مبیع ہونا اس کے متعین ہونے کو ستلزم نہیں ہوتا' (something being sold does not necessitate it being specific).
This is the core ruling.
3
Analyze the given example
The example is the muslam fihi (commodity in salam) which is sold by consensus but is not specific; it is a liability (dhimmah).
Salam is a deferred sale where the commodity is described but not physically present.
4
Understand the implication for liability
The sold item can be a debt or liability in the seller's dhimmah, not necessarily a concrete object.
This allows contracts like salam and istisna.
5
Distinguish from other schools
Note that other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) often require specification; the Hanafi position is unique and more flexible.
The passage does not mention the comparison, but it is useful context.

کے متعین ہونے کے قائل نہیں ہیں؟ جواب اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ کسی چیز کا مبیع ہونا اس کے متعین ہونے کو ستلزم نہیں ہوتا۔ مثلا مسلم فیہ بالاتفاق مبیع ہوتی ہے۔ لیکن متعین نہیں ہوتی بلکہ مسلم الیہ کے ذمہ واجب ہوتی ہے۔
They are not of the opinion that it is specific? Answer: The answer is that something being sold does not necessitate it being specific. For example, the muslam fihi (commodity in salam) is sold by consensus, but it is not specific; rather it is owed as a liability in the debtor's responsibility.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement: a question and answer about whether a sold item must be specifically determined at the time of contract. The answer clarifies that being sold does not require specification. The example given is the salam contract, where the commodity (muslam fihi) is a liability on the seller's dhimmah and not a specific identified item. This is a unique Hanafi position, as other schools may require specification for some contracts. The ruling is taken from the general principles of sales in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
متعین (muta'ayyin): Specified or determined (concrete) item as opposed to a liability in the dhimmah.
مسلم فیہ (muslam fihi): The commodity to be delivered in a salam contract.
ذمہ (dhimmah): Liability or responsibility of a person; here the seller's obligation to deliver a described commodity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

In the Hanafi school, is it necessary for the sold item to be specifically determined at the time of contract?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, it can be a liability in the dhimmah.
C) Only for gold and silver.
D) Only for salam contracts.

Key Takeaway
The sale of a non-specific item is valid under Hanafi law when the item is a clearly described liability on the seller, as exemplified by the salam contract.

Selling Gold for Silver by Estimation
Ruling with proof for selling gold for silver by estimation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling gold for silver by estimation and identify the conditions required for its validity.

Core Idea
Gold can be sold for silver by estimation because equality is not required across different species; only hand-to-hand delivery matters.

In this lesson, we examine a key Hanafi ruling on currency exchange contracts. The core principle is that riba prohibition applies strictly within the same genus, but when species differ, estimation is permitted as long as immediate delivery takes place. We will analyze the textual proof from the hadith of Ubada ibn Samit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is selling gold for silver by estimation (mujāzafah). The ruling is permissible (jā'iz) in the Hanafi school.
Contrast with same-species: that is prohibited by estimation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ubada ibn Samit: 'When these types differ, sell as you wish as long as it is hand-to-hand.'
The hadith is from Sunan Ibn Majah and is considered authentic.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'sell as you wish' indicates broad permission, and 'hand-to-hand' specifies the only condition. Since equality is not mentioned, it is not required.
Hanafi usul: the command is permissive (ibaha) unless restricted.
4
Note the condition
The hadith requires delivery (qabd) in the session before the parties separate. This prevents riba al-nasi'ah.
Delivery must be actual possession.
5
Contrast with same-species
If gold were sold for gold by estimation, it would be haram due to the possibility of riba. Equality is required within the same species.
The Hanafi rule: probability of riba is like actual riba in prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز بيع الذهب بالفضة مجازفة لان المساواة غير مشروطة فيه ولكن يشترط القبض في المجلس لما ذكرنا بخلاف بيعه بجنسه مجازفة لما فيه من احتمال الربوا ترجمہ اور سونے کو چاندی کے عوض اندازے سے بیچنا جائز ہے کیونکہ خلاف جنس میں برابری شرط نہیں ہے لیکن مجلس میں قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے اس کے برخلاف اندازے سے اس کی بیع اس کی جنس کے عوض کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، سونے کی بیچ چاندی کے عوض اور چاندی کی بیچ سونے کے عوض اندازے سے جائز ہے خواہ وزن میں دونوں عوض برابر ہوں یا ایک کم اور ایک زائد ہو۔ کیونکہ اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں برابری شرط نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ عبادہ بن صامت کی حدیث:۔ اذا اختلفت هذه الاصناف فبيعوا كيف شتم اذا كان يداً بيد شاہد ہے۔ پس جب اختلاف جنس کی صورت میں دونوں عوضوں کا برابر ہونا شرط نہیں ہے تو اندازے اور انکل سے بیچنا بھی حرام نہ ہوگا۔ البتہ افتراق بالا بد ان سے پہلے پہلے قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے اور اس کی نقلی اور عقلی دلیلیں سابق میں گذر چکی ہیں۔ نقلی دلیل سے مراد حديث الذهب بالورق ربوا لاهاء وهاء ہے یعنی سونے کو چاندی کے عوض بچنار [؟] ہوا ہے مگر لے اور لا کے ساتھ جائز ہے۔ یعنی اگر با ہم قبضہ ہو جائے تو جائز ہے اور اگر سونے کو اس کی جنس یعنی سونے کے عوض یا چاندی کو چاندی کے عوض اندازے اور انکل سے بیچا تو جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ اس میں ربوا کا احتمال ہے یعنی ہو سکتا ہے کہ ایک عوض کم اور ایک عوض زائد ہو۔ اور پہلے بار بار گزر چکا ہے کہ احتمال ربوا بھی حقیقت ربوا کی طرح حرام ہے۔ اسلئے سونے یا چاندی کی بیع بجنسہ اندازے سے حرام اور نا جائز ہے۔
And it is permissible to sell gold for silver by estimation because equality is not required therein, but delivery (qabd) in the session is required due to what we mentioned, unlike selling it for its own kind by estimation because of the possibility of riba. Translation: And selling gold for silver by estimation is permissible because in different species equality is not a condition, but delivery in the session is a condition. Contrary to selling it for its own kind by estimation because of the possibility of riba. Clarification: Selling gold for silver and silver for gold by estimation is permissible, whether the weights are equal or one is less and the other more. Because in different species equality is not a condition, as indicated by the hadith of Ubada ibn Samit: 'When these types differ, sell as you wish as long as it is hand-to-hand.' So when equality is not required in different species, selling by estimation is not haram. However, delivery before separation is required, and its textual and rational proofs have preceded. The textual proof refers to the hadith 'Gold for silver is riba except hand-to-hand.' Meaning gold for silver becomes a usurious sale unless delivery is taken. So if both take delivery, it is permissible. If gold is sold for its own kind or silver for its own kind by estimation, it is not permissible because of the possibility of riba, i.e., one may be less and the other more. And it has been repeatedly stated that the possibility of riba is like actual riba in prohibition. Therefore, selling gold or silver for its own kind by estimation is haram and impermissible.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that selling gold for silver by estimation is permissible because equality of weight is not required when the two items are of different species (jins). However, hand-to-hand delivery in the same session is required. The proof is the hadith of Ubada ibn Samit, which explicitly allows selling different types as long as it is hand-to-hand. The text then contrasts this with selling gold for gold or silver for silver: that is not permissible by estimation because of the possibility of riba (usury). The Hanafi principle that the mere possibility of riba is as prohibited as actual riba is invoked. The commentary clarifies that estimation is allowed across species, but not within the same species, and that delivery must take place before the parties separate.

Key Terms
مجازفة (mujāzafah): Selling by estimation without exact measurement or weighing.
ربوا (ribā): Usury or prohibited increase in exchange of certain items.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for selling gold for silver by estimation to be valid in the Hanafi school?
A) The weights must be equal.
B) The transaction must be documented by two witnesses.
C) Delivery must take place before the parties separate.
D) The gold must be in coin form.

Key Takeaway
Selling different species of ribawi items by estimation is permissible in the Hanafi school, provided hand-to-hand delivery occurs.

Allocating Cash Payment in a Mixed Sale with Sarf
Ruling with proof via qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on allocation of cash in a mixed sale involving a sarf component and apply the principle of prioritizing the wajib.

Core Idea
Cash payment is allocated to the sarf item (silver necklace) because immediate possession is wajib.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi case: a slave girl and a silver necklace sold together for a lump sum, with partial cash payment. The question is which item the cash is allocated to. The ruling relies on the principle of sarf—exchange of silver for silver—which requires immediate possession in the session. The Hanafi school applies a presumption that Muslims fulfill obligations first, leading to the cash being allocated to the necklace to validate the entire sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mixed sale components
Recognize that the transaction involves a slave girl (non-ribawi) and a silver necklace (ribawi). The total price is 2000 mithqal silver, with 1000 mithqal paid in cash.
The price is also silver, creating a sarf exchange for the necklace portion.
2
Classify the two exchanges
The exchange of the necklace (silver) for part of the price (silver) is sarf. The exchange of the slave girl for the remainder is a normal sale. Sarf requires immediate delivery (qabd) in the session.
Hanafi: sarf is exchange of gold/silver, ribawi, wujub of qabd in majlis.
3
Apply the rule for sarf
Since delivering the necklace's price is wajib in the session, the seller is presumed to have fulfilled that obligation by allocating the cash payment to it.
The principle: al-ghalib min al-muslimin an yūfī bi al-wājib.
4
Understand the presumption
The default assumption is that a Muslim performs the obligatory act. Thus, the cash is considered payment for the necklace, not the slave girl.
This is a legal presumption (zāhir al-ḥāl) used in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Examine the analogies (qiyas)
Two analogies support this: (1) sajdah sahw redirects to missing fard sajdah; (2) Tawaf al-Sadr redirects to Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Both show that a wajib act can substitute for a rukn to fulfill the obligation.
The common illa is fulfilling the obligatory to validate the act.

اسی طرح اگر باندی اور طوق کو دو ہزار مثقال چاندی کے عوض اس طور پر خریدا کہ ایک ہزار مثقال ادھار ہیں اور ایک ہزار نقد ہیں تو ایک ہزار نقد طوق کا ثمن شمار کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ بیع صرف میں میعاد مقرر کرنا یعنی ادھار معاملہ کرنا باطل ہے اور باندی کی بیع میں ادھار جائز
A slave girl whose value is one thousand mithqal of silver and on her neck is a silver necklace whose value is one thousand mithqal, sold for two thousand mithqal of silver, and he took one thousand mithqal as cash payment, then they separated after dissolving the session; what is the payment for? And he said: Whoever sells a slave girl worth one thousand mithqal of silver and on her neck is a silver necklace worth one thousand mithqal for two thousand mithqal of silver, and he pays one thousand mithqal of the price in cash, then they separate, then what he paid in cash is the price of the silver, because taking possession of the share of the necklace is obligatory in the session as it is the exchange of sarf, and the apparent situation is that he fulfilled the obligation. Similarly, if he buys both for two thousand mithqal, one thousand on credit and one thousand in cash, then the cash is the price of the necklace because the term is invalid in sarf and permissible in the sale of the slave girl, and the apparent situation of the parties is that they concluded it in a permissible manner. Translation: A person sold a slave girl worth one thousand mithqal of silver, on whose neck was a silver necklace also worth one thousand mithqal, for two thousand mithqal of silver. The buyer paid one thousand mithqal in cash, then they separated. The cash payment is considered for the silver necklace. Because possession of the necklace's share is obligatory in the session, since it is the exchange of sarf. The apparent situation of the seller is that he fulfilled the obligatory. Similarly, if he bought both for two thousand mithqal with one thousand on credit and one thousand cash, then the cash is for the necklace. Because specifying a term is invalid in sarf and valid in the sale of the slave girl, and the apparent situation of the contracting parties is that they concluded the contract in a permissible manner. Clarification: The case is that a person sold a slave girl worth one thousand mithqal of silver, on whose neck was a silver necklace also worth one thousand mithqal, for two thousand mithqal of silver. The buyer paid one thousand mithqal of the price in cash, then both parties separated. The cash paid is considered for the silver necklace. The evidence is that in this contract, one thousand mithqal of silver is the price of the slave girl and one thousand mithqal is the price of the necklace. The exchange between the necklace and one thousand mithqal is a sale of sarf, and the exchange between the slave girl and one thousand mithqal is not sarf. It has preceded that in a sarf contract, taking possession of the two items in the session is obligatory due to a legal right. Therefore, taking possession of the price of the necklace in the session is obligatory, while taking possession of the price of the slave girl is not obligatory. The apparent situation of Muslims is that they first fulfill the obligatory to clear their responsibility. Since the seller here is also a Muslim, his apparent situation is that he fulfilled the obligatory. Thus, the one thousand mithqal of silver is considered the share of the necklace, because only the payment for the necklace is obligatory in the session, not the payment for the slave girl. An analogy: A person missed one sajdah of prayer and also committed forgetfulness (sahw). He then performed two sajdahs of sahw and said salam. One of the two sajdahs of sahw is redirected to the sajdah of prayer, even if he did not intend it, so that his prayer becomes correct and the obligation of prayer is fulfilled. Because the sajdah of prayer is a rukn and fard without which prayer is not valid, while sajdah sahw is wajib without which the prayer is still valid although deficient. Another analogy: A person left Tawaf al-Ziyarah and performed Tawaf al-Sadr; this Tawaf al-Sadr is redirected to Tawaf al-Ziyarah so that his Hajj becomes correct. Because Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn of Hajj without which Hajj is not valid, while Tawaf al-Sadr is wajib without which the obligatory Hajj is still fulfilled. Similarly, the one thousand mithqal of silver will be considered the price of the necklace so that both the sale of the necklace and the slave girl become valid. Similarly, if he bought the slave girl and the necklace for two thousand mithqal, with one thousand on credit and one thousand cash, then the cash is the price of the necklace. Because fixing a term is invalid in sarf and valid in the sale of the slave girl.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting a case where a slave girl and a silver necklace are sold together for a lump sum. The buyer pays part cash and part credit, or all cash but only partial payment in cash. The question is which item the cash payment is allocated to. The ruling is that the cash payment is allocated to the necklace because the exchange of silver for silver (the price of the necklace) is a sarf contract, which requires immediate possession in the session. Since the seller is a Muslim, it is assumed he first fulfills the obligatory duty. The commentary then provides two analogies: one from prayer (sajdah sahw redirection) and one from Hajj (Tawaf al-Sadr redirection) to illustrate that when a wajib and a fard conflict, the wajib is redirected to fulfill the fard. The legal principle is that the obligatory (wajib) in sarf is given precedence to ensure the contract is valid. The second scenario confirms that even when mixing credit and cash, the cash payment is for the necklace because credit is invalid in sarf.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Exchange of gold and silver (ribawi items) with specific conditions.
طوق (tawq): Necklace made of silver.
ثمن (thaman): Price or payment in a sale.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mixed sale of a slave girl and a silver necklace, if the buyer pays part cash and they separate, to which item is the cash allocated?
A) Slave girl, because she is the main item.
B) Necklace, because its exchange is sarf requiring immediate payment.
C) Both equally.
D) It is invalid and the sale is void.

Key Takeaway
When a mixed sale includes a sarf component, the mandatory immediate delivery (qabd) in the session dictates that any cash payment is first allocated to the sarf item to ensure the contract's validity.

Sale of a Silver-Inlaid Sword: Allocation and Conditions
Rulings on sale of a silver-inlaid sword with partial payment and separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of a composite item (sword with silver ornamentation) when partial payment is made without specification, and apply the conditions of sarf (qabd, separability, and riba avoidance) to determine validity.

Core Idea
Payment defaults to the silver portion; failure to exchange hands voids the sarf sub-sale and possibly the whole.

This passage addresses a common scenario in composite sales: an item containing both ribawi (silver) and non-ribawi (sword) components. The Hanafi school applies rigorous principles to ensure compliance with sarf and avoid riba. Through the example of a silver-inlaid sword, the author demonstrates how allocation, possession, and separability determine validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the composite sale
The sale involves a sword with silver ornamentation (hilyah). The total price is 100 dirhams, ornamentation worth 50. The buyer pays 50 dirhams without specifying allocation.
2
Apply default allocation rule
When payment is not specified, it is allocated to the silver ornamentation because sarf rules require immediate possession of the price for the ribawi component. The Quranic verse (55:22) is cited as a precedent for interpreting mention of two as intended for one.
This is based on the principle of 'zahir al-hal' (apparent condition).
3
Examine effect of separation before qabd
If the parties separate before mutual possession of the silver price and ornamentation, the sarf contract becomes void. If the ornamentation cannot be removed without harming the sword, the sword sale also becomes void (like the necklace case).
If the ornamentation can be removed without damage, the sword contract remains valid.
4
Consider the riba condition on amounts
The sale is valid only if the silver paid is greater than the silver in the ornamentation. If equal, less, or unknown, the sale is invalid due to potential riba al-fadl.
This condition applies to the sarf portion; the ruling has one valid aspect and two invalid aspects, leading to preponderance of invalidity.
5
Derive the final ruling
The sale is initially valid if payment is allocated and qabd occurs. Upon separation without qabd, the sarf part is void; if the sword cannot be delivered without the ornamentation, the entire sale is fasid. Additionally, if the silver amounts are not clearly greater, the sale is invalid due to riba.
The Hanafi position weighs the invalid aspects over the valid, making the contract void in ambiguous cases.

Source Text

ایک تلوار چاندی سے آراستہ ایک سو درہم کے عوض فروخت کی اس کا حلیہ پچاس درہم ہے اور ثمن پچاس درہم ادا کئے تو یہ ثمن اس حلیہ کے بدلے ہوگا۔ و کذلک لو باع سیفا محلى بمائة درهم وحليته خمسون ودفع من الثمن خمسين جاز البيع فكان المقبوض حصة الفضة وان لم يبين ذلك لما بينا وكذلك ان قال خذ هذه الخمسين من ثمنهما لان الاثنين قد يراد بذكرهما الواحد قال الله تعالى " يخرج منهما اللؤلؤ والمرجان " والمراد احدهما فيحمل عليه بظاهر حاله فان لم يتقابضا حتى افترقا بطل العقد في الحلية لانه صرف فيها وكذا في السيف ان كان لا يتخلص إلا بضرر لانه لا يمكن تسليمه بدون الضرر. ولهذا لايجوز افراده بالبيع فصار كالطوق الجارية وهذا اذا كانت الفضة المفردة ازيد مما فيه فان كانت مثله او اقل منه اولا يدرى لا يجوز البيع للربوا اولا اله وجهة الصحة من وجه وجهة الفساد من وجهين فتـــرجـــــحــت. تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے چاندی کے زیور سے آراستہ ایک تلوار ایک سو درہم کے عوض فروخت کی درانحالیکہ اس کا حلیہ اور زیور پچاس درہم ہے۔ پھر مشتری نے ثمن میں پچاس درہم ادا کئے اور یہ صراحت نہیں کی کہ یہ پچاس درہم حلیہ کا عوض ہیں یا تلوار کا عوض ہیں یا دونوں کا عوض ہیں تو یہ بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور وہ پچاس درہم جن پر بائع نے قبضہ کیا ہے حلیہ کا ثمن شمار ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ حلیہ ہی کے ثمن پر قبضہ کرنا واجب تھا اسلئے ظاہر حال کا تقاضہ یہی ہے کہ پہلے وہی ادا کیا گیا ہوگا۔
A sword adorned with silver was sold for one hundred dirhams; its ornamentation is fifty dirhams, and fifty dirhams of the price were paid. So this price will be for the ornamentation. Similarly, if someone sells a sword adorned with silver for one hundred dirhams, its ornamentation being fifty dirhams, and he pays fifty from the price, the sale is valid, and what was taken is the portion of the silver, even if he did not specify that, for the reason we stated. Similarly, if he said, 'Take this fifty from the price of both,' because sometimes mentioning two intends one. Allah Almighty said, 'From both of them emerge pearls and coral,' and the intention is one of them. So it is interpreted according to its apparent condition. Then if they do not take possession until they separate, the contract becomes void for the ornamentation because it involves sarf, and likewise for the sword if it cannot be separated except with harm, because it is not possible to deliver it without harm. For this reason, its separate sale is not permissible, so it becomes like the necklace of the slave-girl. This is when the separate silver is more than what is in it. But if it is equal to it or less, or it is not known, the sale is not permissible due to riba. There is one aspect of validity and two aspects of invalidity, so the aspect of invalidity is preponderant. Explanation: A person sold a sword adorned with silver ornamentation for one hundred dirhams, its ornamentation being fifty dirhams. Then the buyer paid fifty dirhams from the price without specifying whether this fifty is for the ornamentation, the sword, or both. Then this sale is valid, and those fifty dirhams which the seller took possession of will be considered the price of the ornamentation, because possession of the price of the ornamentation was obligatory, so the apparent condition requires that it was paid first.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage continues the topic of bay' al-sarf in a composite sale, now involving a sword with silver ornamentation (hilyah). The ruling establishes that when payment is made without explicit allocation, it is presumed to be for the silver ornamentation because sarf rules require immediate possession. The author cites the Quranic verse (55:22) as an instance where mentioning two can intend one, supporting the principle of interpreting by the apparent condition (zahir al-hal). The passage then addresses a scenario where the parties separate before mutual possession: the sarf part (ornamentation) becomes void. If the ornamentation cannot be separated from the sword without damage (ghair mutakhallis illa bi-darar), then the sale of the sword also becomes void because it cannot be delivered independently, analogous to the necklace and slave-girl case. However, if the ornamentation can be removed without harm, the contract for the sword remains valid. Finally, the passage discusses riba: if the silver paid is equal to or less than the silver in the ornamentation, or unknown, the sale is invalid due to potential riba al-fadl. The principle 'one aspect of validity vs two of invalidity' leads to preponderance of invalidity. This is a classic Hanafi method of weighing probabilities in ambiguous contracts. Authority weight: The ruling is from the Hanafi madhhab as expounded in Ashraf al-Hidayah, based on al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
حلیہ (hilyah): Silver ornamentation or inlay on the sword.
سیف محلی (sayf muhalla): A sword that is plated or ornamented with silver.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A sword with silver ornamentation (value 40 dirhams) is sold for 120 dirhams. The buyer pays 50 dirhams without specification, and they separate before the seller receives the full price. The ornamentation can be removed without damage. What is the status of the contract?
A) The entire sale is valid because payment exceeds ornamentation value.
B) The sale of the ornamentation is void, but the sword sale remains valid.
C) The entire sale is void because they separated before qabd.
D) The sale is postposed until the remaining price is paid.

Key Takeaway
When selling a composite item containing a ribawi component, the Hanafi school requires default allocation of payment to the ribawi part, hand-to-hand exchange in the session, and clear excess of paid silver over content to avoid riba; failure in any one can void part or all of the contract.

Sale of a Sword Adorned with Silver: Allocation of Payment and Conditions of Validity
Ruling with proof on composite item sale and partial payment in sarf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on allocation of partial payment in a composite sale (sword with silver ornament), explain the Quranic proof using dual pronouns, and identify the conditions (sarf possession, separability, and riba) that affect validity.

Core Idea
When ambiguity exists, a Muslim's words are interpreted to validate the contract, using Quranic precedent where dual pronouns refer to one.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling from the Book of Sarf concerning the sale of a sword adorned with silver. When a buyer pays only part of the price without specifying allocation, Hanafi fiqh uses the principle of zahir al-hal (apparent state) to attribute the payment to the silver ornament, thereby validating the transaction. This ruling is supported by a unique proof from the Quran and Sunnah where dual pronouns are used to refer to a single entity, and it comes with important conditions regarding riba and hand-to-hand delivery.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
A sword with a silver ornament is sold for a total price, and the buyer pays only a portion (equal to the ornament's value) without specifying allocation for the sword or the ornament.
The ambiguity arises because the payment could be for the whole item or just part.
2
Locate the core ruling
The Hanafi ruling states that the payment is attributed solely to the silver ornament, not the sword, based on the principle of zahir al-hal (apparent state of a Muslim to do what is valid).
This allocation ensures the sale of the ornament (a sarf exchange) is valid on the spot, and the sword sale remains valid as a separate item.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is taken from Quranic and Prophetic usage where dual pronouns (like 'minhuma') are used but refer to one entity, e.g., Quran 55:22 about pearls and coral coming from one sea.
This supports interpreting the buyer's phrase 'from the price of both' as 'from the price of the ornament'.
4
Apply the condition of sarf possession
If the parties separate without taking possession of the silver payment, the contract for the ornament becomes void (since it's sarf). The sword's sale remains valid only if the ornament can be separated without harm.
If separation causes harm, the entire contract becomes void due to impossibility of delivery.
5
Evaluate the riba condition
Compare the amount of silver paid separately to the silver in the ornament. If the paid silver is more, the sale is valid; if equal, less, or unknown, the sale is invalid due to riba (usury).
This is because two aspects of invalidity outweigh one aspect of validity.

مالک بن الحویرث اور ان کے چچا زاد بھائی کے قصہ میں فرمایا ہے۔ اذا سافرتما فاذنا واقيما يعنی جب تم سفر کرو تو اذان دو اور اقامت کہو ۔ یہاں بھی اذانا اور اقیما میں تثنیہ بول کر واحد مراد لیا گیا ہے کیونکہ اذان واقامت ایک آدمی کہتا ہے اور جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول ہے يا معشر الجن والانس الم بأنكم رسل منکم، حالانکہ اہل حق کے نزدیک رسل فقط معشر انس سے ہوتے ہیں ۔ معشر جن سے نہیں ہوتے پس یہاں بھی منکم یعنی معشر جن اور معشر انس بول کر فقط معشر انس مرادلیا گیا ہے۔ پس جب تثنیہ بول کر واحد مراد لینا شائع ذائع ہے تو مشتری کے مسلمان ہونے کی حالت کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے اسکے قول مـن ثـمـنـهـمـا كومن ثمن الحلیہ پرمحمول کیا جائے گا کیونکہ مسلمان کا ظاہر حال یہ ہے کہ وہ جائز کام کرتا ہے اور نا جائز کا ارتکاب نہیں کرتا۔ اور بیع کا جواز اسی صورت میں ہو سکتا ہے جبکہ مذکورہ پچاس درہم حلیہ کا ثمن قرار دئیے جائیں۔ اسلئے خذ هذه الخمسين من ثمنهما کہنے کی صورت میں بھی یہ پچاس درہم ، حلیہ کا ثمن شمار ہوں گے اور حلیہ اور تلوار دونوں کا شمار نہ ہوں گے۔
صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ مذکورہ دونوں صورتوں میں یعنی جاریہ اور طوق کی صورت میں اور تلوار اور حلیہ کی صورت میں اگر مجلس میں باہم قبضہ نہ ہوا اور عاقدین دونوں جدا ہو گئے تو طوق اور حلیہ کے حصہ میں عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ حصہ طوق اور حصہ حلیہ میں دونوں عوضوں کے ثمن یعنی چاندی ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ عقد صرف ہے اور بغیر قبضہ کئے جدا ہونے سے چونکہ عقد صرف باطل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے حصہ طوق اور حصہ حلیہ میں یہ عقد باطل ہو جائے گا۔ اور باندی کے اندر درست ہو جائے گا۔ اور رہا تلوار کا معاملہ تو حلیہ اگر تلوار کے ساتھ ایسے طریقہ سے پیوستہ اور وابستہ ہے کہ حلیہ کو تلوار سے جدا کرنا بغیر ضرر کے ممکن نہ ہو تو تلوار کی بیع بھی باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں بغیر ضرر کے تلوار کا سپرد کر ناممکن نہ رہا اور جس صورت میں بغیر ضرر کے مبیع سپرد کرنا ممکن نہ ہو ۔ اس صورت میں بیع باطل ہو جاتی ہے اسلئے مذکورہ صورت میں تلوار کی بیع بھی باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جب حلیہ کا تلوار سے جدا کرنا بغیر ضرر کے ممکن نہ ہو تو تنہا تلوار کی بیع جائز نہیں ہوتی جیسے چھت میں لگے ہوئے شہتیر کا سپرد کرنا چونکہ بغیر ضرر کے ممکن نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے چھت میں لگے ہوئے شہتیر کا بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر حلیہ کا تلوار سے جدا کرنا بغیر ضرر کے ممکن ہو تو تلوار کی بیع جائز ہو جائے گی اور حلیہ کی بیع باطل ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں تلوار یعنی مبیع کو بغیر ضرر کے سپرد کرناممکن ہے اور جس صورت میں مبیع کو بغیر ضرر کے سپرد کرنا
Book of Sarf. It is. And from the apparent state of the contracting parties, it is that the sale is valid. So considering the apparent state, it is appropriate to make the one thousand cash the share of the necklace in the price so that the sale of both the necklace and the slave girl becomes valid. A sword adorned with silver was sold for one hundred dirhams, its ornament is fifty dirhams, and fifty dirhams of the price were paid. This price will be for the ornament. And likewise, if he sold a sword adorned with silver for one hundred dirhams, and its ornament is fifty, and he paid fifty of the price, the sale is valid. So what was taken possession of is the share of the silver, even if he did not specify that, due to what we have stated. And likewise if he said: 'Take these fifty from the price of both' because sometimes by mentioning two, one is intended. Allah the Exalted said: 'From both of them come forth pearls and coral' but what is intended is one of them. So it is attributed to it based on its apparent state. If they did not take possession until they separated, the contract becomes void regarding the ornament because it is sarf in it, and likewise in the sword if it cannot be separated except with harm, because it is not possible to deliver it without harm. And for this reason, selling it alone is not permissible, so it becomes like the necklace of the slave girl. And this is when the separate silver is more than what is in it. If it is equal to it or less than it or unknown, the sale is not permissible due to riba, because it has one aspect of validity and two aspects of invalidity, so the aspect of invalidity preponderates. Translation: And likewise, if a sword adorned with silver was sold for one hundred dirhams, and its ornament is fifty dirhams, and he paid fifty dirhams of the price, the sale becomes valid. So what was taken possession of is the share of the silver (ornament) even if he did not specify it, due to the evidence we have stated. And likewise if he said: 'Take these fifty from the price of both' because sometimes by mentioning two, one is intended. Thus Allah the Exalted said: 'From both of them come forth pearls and coral' and what is intended is one of them. So based on the apparent state, it is attributed to that. If mutual possession did not occur until they separated, the contract becomes void regarding the ornament because it is a sale of sarf in it, and likewise in the sword if the ornament cannot be separated without harm, because it is not possible to deliver the sword without harm. And for this reason, selling it alone is not permissible, like the sale of a beam in a roof is not permissible. And if the ornament can be separated from the sword without harm, then the sale of the sword becomes valid, and the sale of the ornament becomes void, because the sale of the sword alone is possible. So it becomes like the slave girl and the necklace. And this ruling applies when the separate silver is more than that which is in the sold item. If it is less or equal to it, or its amount is unknown, then due to riba or the possibility of riba, the sale is not permissible. And the aspect of validity is one, and the aspect of invalidity is two, so the aspect of invalidity preponderates. Explanation: The scenario is that a person sold a sword adorned with silver ornamentation for one hundred dirhams, while its ornament and decoration are fifty dirhams. Then the buyer paid fifty dirhams of the price and did not specify whether these fifty dirhams are the price of the ornament, or the price of the sword, or the price of both. So this sale becomes valid, and those fifty dirhams that the seller took possession of will be counted as the price of the ornament, because it was obligatory to take possession of the price of the ornament only. Therefore, the requirement of the apparent state is that it was paid first. And if the buyer explicitly [?] said: 'These fifty dirhams are the price of both the sword and the ornament,' then in this case too it will be counted as the price of the ornament only. It is as if the buyer said: 'Take from the price of both that which it is obligatory to take possession of,' because the affairs of Muslims are to be attributed to validity and correctness as much as possible, and here it is possible to attribute it to validity, in that the pronoun of duality in 'min thamanihima' (from the price of both) is intended to refer to one, and it is said that although the buyer said 'min thamanihima', he meant 'min thaman al-hilyah' (from the price of the ornament), and using the dual to refer to one is permissible. As in the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'From both of them come forth pearls and coral,' the referent of the pronoun 'huma' (both) is the salt sea and the sweet sea, but pearls and coral only come from the salt sea and the [?] sea, not from the sweet sea. From this it is known that in 'minhuma' the dual is used to refer to one. And like in the story of Musa and Khidr (peace be upon them), Allah the Exalted said: 'They forgot their fish' – 'nasiya' is a dual form, whereas the one who forgot the fish at the meeting of the two seas was only the servant of Musa (peace be upon him). Here also the dual is used to refer to one. And like Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed, your supplication has been answered' – 'du'a'ukumaa' is dual, while what is intended is only the supplication of Musa (peace be upon him). Here also the dual is used to refer to one. And like the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said in the story of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith and his cousin: 'When you travel, give the adhan and iqamah' – 'adhinaa wa aqimaa' is dual, but what is intended is one, because one person gives the adhan and iqamah. And like the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'O assembly of jinn and humans, did there not come to you messengers from among you?' – 'minkum' is dual referent, whereas according to Ahl al-Haqq, messengers are only from humans, not from jinn. So here too, by saying 'jinn and humans' only humans are intended. So when using the dual to refer to one is widespread and common, then considering the state of the buyer being a Muslim, his saying 'min thamanihima' will be attributed to 'min thaman al-hilyah' because the apparent state of a Muslim is that he does a valid act and does not commit an invalid one. And the validity of the sale can only be in this case when the mentioned fifty dirhams are considered the price of the ornament. Therefore, even in the case of saying 'take these fifty from the price of both,' these fifty dirhams will be counted as the price of the ornament, and not as the price of both the ornament and the sword. Sahib al-Quduri says: In both mentioned cases, i.e., the case of the slave girl and the necklace and the case of the sword and the ornament, if they did not take mutual possession in the session and the two contracting parties separated, then the contract regarding the share of the necklace and the share of the ornament becomes void. Because in the share of the necklace and the share of the ornament, since the price of both counterparts is silver, this contract is sarf, and due to separation without possession, the contract of sarf becomes void. Therefore, the contract regarding the share of the necklace and the share of the ornament becomes void, and regarding the slave girl it remains valid. As for the matter of the sword: if the ornament is attached to the sword in such a way that separating the ornament from the sword is not possible without harm, then the sale of the sword also becomes void. Because in this case, delivering the sword without harm becomes impossible, and when delivering the sold item without harm is not possible, the sale becomes void. Therefore, in the mentioned case, the sale of the sword also becomes void. This is why, when separating the ornament from the sword is not possible without harm, selling the sword alone is not permissible, just as selling a beam installed in a roof is not permissible because delivering it without harm is not possible. And if separating the ornament from the sword is possible without harm, then the sale of the sword becomes valid and the sale of the ornament becomes void, because in this case delivering the sword (i.e., the sold item) without harm is possible.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Sarf (currency exchange) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, expanding on the sale of composite items containing silver. The core issue is: when a person sells a sword adorned with silver ornamentation for a total price, and the buyer pays only part of the price (equivalent to the silver ornament), how is the payment allocated? The ruling states that the sale is valid, and the partial payment is attributed to the silver ornament, not the sword, even if the buyer does not specify or says 'from the price of both.' This is based on the principle that the apparent state (zahir al-hal) is given consideration, and contracts are interpreted in a way that validates them as much as possible. The proof comes from Quranic usage where dual pronouns sometimes refer to a single entity, such as in Surah ar-Rahman (55:22) 'From both of them come forth pearls and coral,' where 'both' refers to the two seas but the pearls and coral only come from one. Similarly, in other Quranic and Prophetic texts, dual forms are used to mean one. Thus, the buyer's statement 'from the price of both' is understood to mean 'from the price of the ornament' to preserve the validity of the sale. The passage then discusses conditions: if the parties separate without mutual possession, the contract for the silver part (the ornament or necklace) becomes void because it constitutes a sarf transaction (exchange of silver for silver) which requires hand-to-hand receipt. For the sword or slave girl (the non-silver part), the sale remains valid if the silver can be separated without harm; if not, the entire contract becomes void due to impossibility of delivery. Additionally, a comparison of silver amounts is crucial: if the separately paid silver is more than the silver in the sold item, the sale is valid; if equal or less, or unknown, the sale is invalid due to riba (usury) because it resembles an unequal exchange of silver. The preponderance of the aspect of invalidity over validity is established (tarjih). The passage concludes with a quotation from Sahib al-Quduri summarizing the rules.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): A contract of exchange where the consideration is gold or silver (or currency) and requires hand-to-hand delivery in the same sitting.
حلیہ (hilyah): The silver ornamentation on the sword, considered as a separate entity in the contract.
ظاہر حال (zahir al-hal): The apparent state or presumption about a person's actions, especially a Muslim, that they intend a valid act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the buyer's statement 'take these fifty from the price of both' interpreted as referring only to the price of the ornament?
A) Because the buyer explicitly said so.
B) Because it is the only way to avoid riba in the transaction.
C) Because the Quran and Sunnah use dual pronouns to sometimes mean one.
D) Because the sword cannot be sold without the ornament.

Key Takeaway
When ambiguity arises in a composite sale involving silver, Hanafi fiqh attributes partial payment to the silver portion to validate the transaction, using the principle of zahir al-hal and Quranic precedent, subject to strict conditions of sarf possession, separability, and riba avoidance.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
12 min
Selling a Sword with Silver Ornament for Silver Dirhams: Conditions and Proofs
Explanation of the ruling for selling a sword with silver ornament for silver dirhams, including conditions on quantity and possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a sale involving a composite object with silver for silver dirhams is valid, and explain the Hanafi interpretation of the buyer's ambiguous statement using the principle of dual-to-singular.

Core Idea
A sale of a sword with silver ornament for silver dirhams is valid only if the price exceeds the attached silver and immediate possession occurs.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah unpacks a nuanced sarf transaction: when a buyer says 'take these fifty dirhams from the price of both' (sword and ornament), the Hanafi school interprets it in the most favorable light to maintain validity. The text then details the crucial conditions of quantity and possession, supported by Quranic and hadith examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous statement
The buyer says 'khudh hadhihi al-khamsina min thamanihima' – take these fifty dirhams from the price of both (the sword and ornament). This creates ambiguity: does the price cover both items or only one?
The dual pronoun 'thamanihima' indicates two items.
2
Apply the principle favorable to Muslims
The Hanafi school presumes a Muslim intends a valid contract. Since interpreting the statement as covering both would lead to riba (because silver is exchanged for silver without equality), it is interpreted as referring only to the ornament's price, making the sale valid.
This principle applies 'umur al-muslimin 'ala al-salah' (affairs of Muslims are assumed valid).
3
Analyze the linguistic proof
The author cites Quranic verses and hadith where the dual form is used to mean singular. For example, 'yakhruju minhuma al-lu'lu' wa al-marjan' – pearls and coral come only from salt water, so 'minhuma' refers to one sea. This proves that dual-to-singular is acceptable in Arabic, legitimizing the interpretation.
Quran 55:22, story of Musa, hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwairith, and others are mentioned.
4
Evaluate the sarf condition of immediate possession
Since the exchange involves silver for silver (sarf), the contract requires immediate hand-to-hand possession (qabd) in the session. If the parties separate without qabd, the contract becomes batil (void) for the silver portion (the ornament) but remains valid for the non-silver item (the sword if separable).
This is based on the ruling of Sahib al-Quduri.
5
Apply the quantity condition
Sahib al-Hidayah states that the ruling applies only when the price silver exceeds the silver attached to the sold item. If the price is equal or less, riba occurs because silver is exchanged for silver without an additional non-silver element. If the quantity is unknown, the sale is fasid due to the preponderance of corruption.
The text gives an example: price 10 tolas, attached silver 12 tolas – riba results from 2 tolas unpaid.
