Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Refuting the Objection of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i on Currency Exchange
Response to objections against Hanafi ruling on ambiguous currency exchange

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of istihsan to validate an ambiguous currency exchange contract and respond to objections based on change in contract description.

Core Idea
An ambiguous currency exchange is valid by interpreting it as individual-for-individual across types; this changes only the description, not the essence.

Currency exchange (sarf) is governed by strict rules against riba. When parties exchange a mix of dirhams and dinars without specifying the pairing, the contract is ambiguous. Imam Abu Hanifa holds the contract valid via istihsan, while Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i object that such an interpretation changes the contract. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi proof and its refutation of the objections, focusing on the critical distinction between the essence of a contract (asl) and its description (wasf).

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
State the exact scenario: two dirhams and one dinar are exchanged for one dirham and two dinars, without specifying how the items match. Determine the legal problem: ambiguity can lead to riba.
2
List the three possible interpretations
Identify the three probabilities: total-for-total, individual-for-individual within same type, individual-for-individual across types. Note which lead to invalidity and which one yields a valid exchange.
Individual-for-individual across types avoids riba because quantities match appropriately.
3
Apply istihsan to choose the valid interpretation
Since a sane adult's transaction should be upheld when possible, the contract is carried to the valid interpretation (individual-for-individual across types). This is istihsan.
This selection changes only the description (wasf), not the essence (asl).
4
Distinguish essence from description
The essence of a sarf contract is ownership of the whole for the whole. The description is how the exchange is matched (general vs. specific). The valid interpretation preserves the essence; only the matching method changes.
Changing description is permissible; changing essence is not.
5
Respond to the opponents' objections
Address the claim that interpretation changes the contract. Show that the change is only in description, as in the slave sale analogy. Then briefly note why the murabaha and other analogies fail (they change essence, not description).
Focus on the slave sale parallel as the core qiyas.

كتاب الصرف 
اشرف البدایہ جلد - نم مقابلہ پرمحمول کرنے میں عقد کا وصف متغیر ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی اصل متغیر نہیں ہوتی ۔ کیونکہ اس کا موجب اصلی باقی رہتا ہے۔ اور حکم اصلی کل کے مقابلہ میں کل کے اندر ملک کا ثابت ہونا ہے اور یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کسی نے ایسے غلام کا آدھا فروخت کیا جو اس کے اور اس کے غیر کے در میان مشترک ہے تو یہ بیع اس کے تصرف کو صحیح کرنے کیلئے اس کے حصہ کی طرف پھرے گی ۔
تشریح مسئلہ مذکورہ میں ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دو درہم اور ایک دینار کا مقابلہ ، ایک درہم اور دو دینار کے ساتھ مطلق ہے۔ اس میں یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ مجموعہ کا مقابلہ مجموعہ کے ساتھ ہو اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ فرد کا مقابلہ فرد کے ساتھ ہو ۔ مقابلہ فرد بالفرد میں بھی دو احتمال ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من جنسہ ہو۔ یعنی دو درہم، ایک درہم کے مقابلہ میں ہوں اور ایک دینار، دود بینار کے مقابلہ میں ہو۔ دوم یہ کہ مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من غیر جنسہ ہو یعنی دو درہم، دو دینار کے مقابلہ میں ہوں اور ایک دینار ایک درہم کے مقابلہ میں ہو۔ حاصل یہ کہ مقابلہ مطلقہ جس طرح مقابلہ کل بالکل کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اسی طرح مقابلہ نفرد بالفرد کا احتمال رکھتا ہے جیسا کہ مقابلہ جنس با جنس میں مقابلہ فرد بالفرد کا احتمال ہے۔ اس طور پر کہ اگر دود بینار، دو دینار کے عوض فروخت کئے گئے تو بالاتفاق ایک دینار، ایک دینار کے مقابلہ میں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح یہاں مقابلہ مطلقہ میں بھی، مقابلہ فرد بالفرد کا احتمال موجود ہے۔ پس احتمالات ثلاثہ میں سے دو احتمال یعنی مقابله کل بالکل اور مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من جنسہ کی صورت میں عاقدین کا تصرف باطل ہو جاتا ہے اور مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من غیر جنسہ کی صورت میں تصرف درست رہتا ہے تو گویا مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من غیر جنسہ اس کے تصرف کو صحیح بنانے کا ایک متعین طریقہ ہے اور یہ بات چونکہ مسلم ہے کہ عاقل بالغ آدمی کے تصرف کو صحیح کرنے کی حتی الامکان کوشش کرنی چاہئے ۔ اسلئے عاقد کے تصرف کو صحیح کرنے کیلئے اس کے عقد کو اس احتمال یعنی مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من غیر جنسہ پر محمول کیا جائے گا۔
ر با امام زفر اور امام شافعی کا یہ کہنا کہ مقابلہ فرد بالفرد میں عقد کو غیر متغیر کرنالازم آتا ہے تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ اصل عقد کو متغیر کر نالازم نہیں آتا بلکہ وصف عقد کو متغیر کرنا لازم آتا ہے عقد کا وصف تو اسلئے متغیر ہو جاتا ہے کہ مقابلہ کل بالکل کے احتمال میں بنوارہ بطور شیوع کے تھا اس کو ترک کر دیا گیا اور مقابلہ فرد بالفرد من غیر جنسہ جس میں بٹوارہ متعین طور پر الگ الگ ہوتا ہے اس کو مراد لیا گیا ہے تو گویا عقد کے ایک وصف یعنی شیوع کے طریقہ کو چھوڑ کر دوسرا وصف یعنی تعیین کا طریقہ مراد یا گیا ہے اور اصل عقد اسلئے متغیر نہیں ہوا کہ عقد کا حکم اصلی یہ ہے کہ کل کے مقابلہ میں کل کے اندر ملکیت ثابت ہو جائے یعنی دو درہم اور ایک دینار کا مالک ایک عاقد ہو جائے اور ایک درہم اور دو دینار کا مالک دوسرا عاقد ہو جائے اور یہ بات مقابلہ کل بالکل اور مقابلہ فرد بالفرد دونوں صورتوں میں متحقق ہو جاتی ہے اور جب دونوں صورتوں میں کل کے مقابلہ میں کل کے اندر ملکیت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے تو معلوم ہوا کہ اصل عقد متغیر نہیں ہوا بلکہ وصف عقد متغیر ہوا ہے اور اصل عقد کو متغیر کرنا اگر چہ جائز نہیں ہے لیکن وصف عقد کو متغیر کرنا جائز ہے اور جب وصف عقد کو متغیر کرنا جائز ہے تو متن میں مذکور بیع کی صورت بھی جائز ہو گی۔ اس کی مثال ایسی ہے جیسے ایک غلام دو آدمیوں کے درمیان مشترک ہو ان میں سے ایک نے نصف غلام فروخت کر دیا ہو تو یہ نصف مطلق ہے۔ یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ اس نے اپنا نصف حصہ مراد لیا ہو۔ اور یہ بھی احتمال ہے کہ دوسرے ساتھی کا نصف حصہ مراد لیا ہو۔ اور اس طرح بیع نا جائز ہوتی ہے۔ مگر بائع کے تصرف عقد کو صحیح کرنے کیلئے اس کے حصہ کی طرف عقد کو پھیرا جاتا ہے اور اس میں زیادہ سے زیادہ وصف متغیر ہوتا ہے بایں طور کہ مطلقاً نصف غلام مراد لینے کی صورت میں شیوع تھا اور بائع کا حصہ مراد لینے کی صورت میں تعیین ہے پس جس طرح عقد کو صحیح کرنے کیلئے اس مسئلہ میں تغیر وصف کے باوجود عقد کو بائع کے حصہ کی طرف پھیرا گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح

كتاب الصرف 
متن کے مسئلہ میں بھی تغیر وصف کے باوجود عقد کو صیح کرنے کیلئے ہر ایک عوض کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرا جائے گا۔
اشرف البدایہ جلد - محمد
بخلاف ماعُد من المسائل أما المسألة المرابحة لانه يصير تولية فى القلب بصرف الربح كله الى الثوب والطريق في المسألة الثانية غير متعين لانه يمكن صرف الزيادة على الالف الى المشترى وفي الثالثة اضيف البيع الى المنكر وهو ليس بمحل للبيع والمعين ضده وفى الاخيرة انعقد العقد صحيحا والفساد في حالة البقاء وكلامنا في الابتداء
ترجمه بر خلاف ان مسائل کے جن کو شمار کیا گیا ہے۔ بہر حال مسئلہ مرابحہ تو اسلئے کہ تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے سے کنگن میں عقد مرابحہ بدل کر تو لیہ ہو جائے گا اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں جواز کا طریقہ غیر متعین ہے کیونکہ ایک ہزار سے زائد کو بھی خریدے ہوئے غلام کی طرف پھیر نا ممکن ہے اور تیسرے مسئلہ میں بیج کو غیر معین غلام کی طرف منسوب کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ وہ بیع کا محل نہیں ہے اور معین اس کی ضد ہے اور آخری مسئلہ میں عقد صحیح ہو کر منعقد ہوا اور فساد حالت بقاء میں ہے اور ہمارا کلام ابتدائے عقد میں ہے۔ تشریح حضرت امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے تغیر تصرف کے عدم جواز پر جن مسائل کو بطور نظیر پیش فرمایا تھا یہاں سے انہیں مسائل کا جواب ہے ۔ چنانچہ مسئلہ مرابحہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر پورا نفع کپڑے کی طرف پھیر دیا گیا تو نگن میں بیع تولیہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جب پورا نفع یعنی پانچ درہم کپڑے کی طرف پھیر دیئے گئے تو کنگن جس کا وزن دس درہم تھا۔ دس درہم کے عوض خرید کر دس ہی درہم کے عوض فروخت کر دیا اور بغیر نفع اور بغیر خسارہ کے فروخت کرنے کو بیع تولیہ کہا جاتا ہے تو کنگن میں بیع تولیہ ہوئی اور تولیہ چونکہ مرابحہ کی ضد ہے اور شی اپنی ضد کو شامل نہیں ہوتی ۔ اسلئے تولیہ مرابحہ کو شامل نہ ہو گا۔ پس تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اگر چہ عقد صحیح ہو جاتا ہے لیکن اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے یعنی مرابحہ سے بدل کر تو لیہ ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے کہ کپڑے اور کنگن کے خریدار نے بصراحت یہ کہا تھا کہ میں نے کنگن اور کپڑے کو مرابحہ فروخت کیا یعنی ہیں درہم میں خرید کر پچیس درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا ہے۔ بہر حال اس مسئلہ میں تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ متن کے مسئلہ میں عوضین میں سے ہر عوض کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرنے میں عقد کا وصف متغیر ہوتا ہے۔ اصل ند متغیر نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اس قدر فرق کے ساتھ متن کے مسئلہ کو اس مسئلہ پر قیاس کرنا اور متن کے مسئلہ کی اس مسئلہ کو نظیر قرار دینا کس طرح درست ہو سکتا ہے۔
دوسرے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ نے شراء ماباع باقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن کی خرابی سے بچنے کیلئے اور بیع کو جائز کرنے کیلئے یہ کہا کہ جس غلام کو ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خریدا تھا جب اس کو اور دوسرے غلام کو ادائے شمن سے پہلے بائع کے ہاتھ پندرہ سو برہم کے عوض فروخت کرنا چاہا۔ تو خریدے ہوئے غلام کا شمن ایک ہزار درہم قرار دیا اور دوسرے کا پانچ سو درہم ثمن قرار دیا لیکن اس کے با وجود ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خریدے ہوئے غلام میں بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ آپ تو یہ سمجھتے ہیں کہ عقد متغیر ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع نا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں جواز کا طریقہ متعین نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد جائز کرنے کیلئے جس طرح
Chapter of Currency Exchange
Ashraf al-Bidaya - Volume: In carrying over to the exchange, the description of the contract changes; its essence does not change. Because its original cause remains. And the original ruling is the establishment of ownership within the whole in exchange for the whole. And this becomes like someone who sold half of a slave who is shared between him and another—this sale is turned towards his share to correct his transaction.
Explanation: In the mentioned issue, our proof is that the exchange of two dirhams and one dinar for one dirham and two dinars is absolute. In this, there is a possibility that the total is exchanged for the total, and also a possibility that each individual is exchanged for an individual. In the individual exchange, there are two possibilities: one that the individual exchange is within the same type, i.e., two dirhams for one dirham and one dinar for two dinars; second, that the individual exchange is across different types, i.e., two dirhams for two dinars and one dinar for one dirham. In summary, the absolute exchange bears the possibility of total-for-total exchange as well as individual-for-individual exchange, just as in exchange of one type for another, there is a possibility of individual exchange. For example, if two dinars are sold for two dinars, by consensus one dinar can be exchanged for one dinar. Similarly, here in the absolute exchange, the possibility of individual exchange exists. So among the three possibilities, in two possibilities—total-for-total and individual-for-individual within the same type—the transaction of the parties becomes invalid; and in the possibility of individual-for-individual across types, the transaction remains valid. Thus the individual-for-individual across types is a definite way to make his transaction valid. And since it is established that every effort should be made to validate the transaction of a sane adult, to validate the party's transaction, his contract will be carried to that possibility, i.e., individual-for-individual across types.
As for the statement of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i that individual exchange necessarily changes the contract, we say: It does not necessitate changing the essence of the contract; rather it necessitates changing the description of the contract. The description of the contract changes because in the possibility of total-for-total the division was general (shuyu'), and that was abandoned, and the individual-for-individual across types, where division is specific, was intended. So one description of the contract, i.e., the method of generality, was left and another description, i.e., the method of specification, was intended. The essence of the contract did not change because the original ruling of the contract is that ownership is established within the whole in exchange for the whole—i.e., one party becomes owner of two dirhams and one dinar, and the other party becomes owner of one dirham and two dinars—and this is realized in both the total-for-total and individual-for-individual forms. Since ownership of the whole in exchange for the whole is established in both forms, it is known that the essence of the contract did not change, only its description changed. And while changing the essence is not permissible, changing the description is permissible. Since changing the description is permissible, the form of sale mentioned in the text is also permissible. An example of this is a slave shared between two persons; one of them sold half of the slave. This half is absolute: there is a possibility that he intended his own half-share, and a possibility that he intended the other partner's half-share. In that case the sale would be invalid. But to validate the seller's transaction, the contract is turned towards his share. At most, the description changes: if the absolute half of the slave was intended, it was general (shuyu'); if the seller's share was intended, it is specific (ta'yin). So just as in that case, to validate the contract, despite the change in description, the contract was turned towards the seller's share, similarly

Chapter of Currency Exchange
In the issue of the text, despite the change in description, to validate the contract, each consideration will be turned towards its opposite type.
Ashraf al-Bidaya - Volume - Muhammad
Contrary to the cases that were enumerated: As for the case of murabaha, it becomes tawliya in essence by directing all profit to the cloth, and the path in the second case is not definite because it is possible to direct the excess over one thousand to the buyer, and in the third case, the sale was attributed to an unknown entity which is not a subject of sale, and the known is its opposite, and in the last case, the contract was concluded validly and the corruption is in the state of continuation, and our discussion is about the beginning.
Translation: Contrary to the cases that were enumerated. However, regarding the case of murabaha, because directing all profit to the cloth turns the bangle into a tawliya contract. And in the second case, the way of validity is not definite because it is possible to direct the excess over one thousand to the purchased slave. And in the third case, the sale was attributed to an unspecified slave, while he is not a subject of sale, and the specified is its opposite. And in the last case, the contract was concluded validly and the corruption is in the state of continuation, while our discussion is about the inception. Explanation: This is the answer to the cases that Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i presented as analogies for the impermissibility of changing the transaction. So, the answer to the murabaha case: If all profit is directed to the cloth, then the bangle becomes a tawliya sale. Because when all profit, i.e., five dirhams, was directed to the cloth, the bangle, whose weight was ten dirhams, was bought for ten dirhams and sold for ten dirhams, and selling without profit or loss is called tawliya. So the bangle was a tawliya sale, and since tawliya is the opposite of murabaha, and a thing does not include its opposite, tawliya does not include murabaha. So directing all profit to the cloth, although it makes the contract valid, changes the essence of the contract—that is, it changes from murabaha to tawliya. Because the buyer of the cloth and bangle explicitly said: I sold the bangle and cloth as murabaha—i.e., bought for twenty dirhams and sold for twenty-five dirhams. In any case, in this case directing all profit to the cloth changes the essence of the contract. And it was previously established that in the issue of the text, directing each consideration to its opposite type changes the description of the contract, not its essence. Therefore, with such a difference, how can it be correct to analogize the issue of the text to this case and consider this case as a parallel for the issue of the text?
The answer to the second case: You said that to avoid the defect of buying what one sold before payment of the price and to validate the sale, when the slave bought for one thousand dirhams and another slave are sold to the seller before payment for fifteen hundred dirhams, the price of the bought slave was set as one thousand dirhams and the price of the other as five hundred dirhams. But despite this, the sale of the slave bought for one thousand dirhams is not valid. You think that the sale is invalid because the contract changed. However, that is not the case; rather the reason for invalidity is that the way of validity is not definite in this situation. Because to validate the contract, as...

Commentary
This passage is a detailed Hanafi rejoinder to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i in a currency exchange dispute. The core issue is whether a contract exchanging two dirhams and one dinar for one dirham and two dinars is valid when the parties did not specify whether the exchange is total-for-total or individual-for-individual. The Hanafi position, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, is that the contract is valid. The reasoning is that the contract is absolute and can be interpreted in three ways: total-for-total, individual-for-individual within the same type, or individual-for-individual across types. The first two interpretations lead to invalidity due to riba (usury) or lack of specification, but the third—individual-for-individual across types—yields a valid exchange. Since a sane adult's transaction should be upheld as much as possible (istihsan), the contract is carried to the valid interpretation. This does not change the essence of the contract (ownership of the whole against each other) but only its description (from general division to specific division). The commentator then responds to the opponents' analogies. The murabaha case is distinguished because directing all profit to one item changes the contract type entirely (murabaha to tawliya), which is a change in essence, not mere description. The second case fails because there is no single definite way to make it valid. The third and fourth cases are similarly distinguished: one involves a non-existent subject of sale, the other a defect arising after the contract, not at inception. Thus the Hanafi position stands on the principle of preserving the contract by minimal interpretative adjustment.

Key Terms
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange; the chapter dealing with trade of gold, silver, and other currencies with specific rules against riba.
مقابلہ (muqabala): Exchange or matching of items in a contract; here it refers to how items are paired in the exchange.
شیوع (shuyu'): Generality or common division; in the contract, it means the items are exchanged as a whole without specific pairing.
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification; in the contract, it means each item is individually matched with a specific counterpart.
محمل (mahmal): The interpretation or carrying over of a term; here 'mahmūl' means the contract is carried to a certain interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school in this passage, why is the exchange of two dirhams and one dinar for one dirham and two dinars considered valid?
A) Because it is a total-for-total exchange of identical value.
B) Because it is interpreted as individual-for-individual across types, which preserves ownership of the whole for each party.
C) Because Imam Shafi'i also agrees to its validity.
D) Because changing the description of a contract is impermissible.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates ambiguous currency exchange contracts by interpreting them in a way that avoids riba and preserves the essence of the transaction, changing only its description.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
advanced
12 min
Response to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i on Change of Description in Contracts
Refuting objections against contracts where description changes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits contracts where the description changes due to apportioning countervalues to different genera, and refute the opposing analogies by identifying the actual cause of invalidity in each case.

Core Idea
A change of description (wasf) does not invalidate a contract; only a change of essence (asl) does.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hadaya presents the Hanafi response to two objections from Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, who argued that altering the description of a contract (e.g., from murābaḥa to ṭawliya by reallocating profit) invalidates it. The Hanafis maintain that such a change is permissible as long as the essence remains intact. The commentator refutes four analogies by showing that each has a distinct cause of invalidity—change of contract type, indeterminate method, unknown subject matter, or post-contractual defect—none of which apply to the original issue.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Clearly articulate the Hanafi ruling: a contract remains valid even if the description changes due to apportioning countervalues to different genera.
The key distinction is between change of description (wasf) and change of essence (asl).
2
Identify the four analogies presented by Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i
List the four cases they used to argue that change of description invalidates: (1) murābaḥa with profit turned to one item, (2) selling a purchased slave before payment with multiple price possibilities, (3) selling an unspecified slave, (4) a contract that becomes invalid after separation without possession.
These are presented as naẓā'ir (analogies).
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each analogy
For each analogy, identify the specific defect that actually causes invalidity according to Hanafi reasoning: (1) change of contract type (murābaḥa to ṭawliya), (2) indeterminate method of validation (unknown price), (3) unknown subject matter (indefinite slave), (4) lack of possession causing invalidity after conclusion.
The Hanafi response shows that the cause of invalidity differs in each case.
4
Compare the cause of invalidity with the original issue
In the original matn issue, the only change is in description (wasf), not essence (asl). The opponents' analogies involve defects such as change of contract type, uncertainty, or unknown subject matter, which are absent in the original.
Thus, the analogies are not valid qiyas because the cause (ʿilla) is different.
5
Conclude why the Hanafi position stands
Since the opponents failed to present a true analogy with identical cause, the Hanafi position that change of description does not invalidate remains robust.
This demonstrates the importance of precise ʿilla identification in Hanafi legal reasoning.

بخلاف ماعُد من المسائل أما المسألة المرابحة لانه يصير تولية فى القلب بصرف الربح كله الى الثوب والطريق في المسألة الثانية غير متعين لانه يمكن صرف الزيادة على الالف الى المشترى وفي الثالثة اضيف البيع الى المنكر وهو ليس بمحل للبيع والمعين ضده وفى الاخيرة انعقد العقد صحيحا والفساد في حالة البقاء وكلامنا في الابتداء
ترجمه بر خلاف ان مسائل کے جن کو شمار کیا گیا ہے۔ بہر حال مسئلہ مرابحہ تو اسلئے کہ تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے سے کنگن میں عقد مرابحہ بدل کر تو لیہ ہو جائے گا اور دوسرے مسئلہ میں جواز کا طریقہ غیر متعین ہے کیونکہ ایک ہزار سے زائد کو بھی خریدے ہوئے غلام کی طرف پھیر نا ممکن ہے اور تیسرے مسئلہ میں بیج کو غیر معین غلام کی طرف منسوب کیا گیا ہے حالانکہ وہ بیع کا محل نہیں ہے اور معین اس کی ضد ہے اور آخری مسئلہ میں عقد صحیح ہو کر منعقد ہوا اور فساد حالت بقاء میں ہے اور ہمارا کلام ابتدائے عقد میں ہے۔ تشریح حضرت امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے تغیر تصرف کے عدم جواز پر جن مسائل کو بطور نظیر پیش فرمایا تھا یہاں سے انہیں مسائل کا جواب ہے ۔ چنانچہ مسئلہ مرابحہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ اگر پورا نفع کپڑے کی طرف پھیر دیا گیا تو نگن میں بیع تولیہ ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ جب پورا نفع یعنی پانچ درہم کپڑے کی طرف پھیر دیئے گئے تو کنگن جس کا وزن دس درہم تھا۔ دس درہم کے عوض خرید کر دس ہی درہم کے عوض فروخت کر دیا اور بغیر نفع اور بغیر خسارہ کے فروخت کرنے کو بیع تولیہ کہا جاتا ہے تو کنگن میں بیع تولیہ ہوئی اور تولیہ چونکہ مرابحہ کی ضد ہے اور شی اپنی ضد کو شامل نہیں ہوتی ۔ اسلئے تولیہ مرابحہ کو شامل نہ ہو گا۔ پس تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اگر چہ عقد صحیح ہو جاتا ہے لیکن اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے یعنی مرابحہ سے بدل کر تو لیہ ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے کہ کپڑے اور کنگن کے خریدار نے بصراحت یہ کہا تھا کہ میں نے کنگن اور کپڑے کو مرابحہ فروخت کیا یعنی ہیں درہم میں خرید کر پچیس درہم کے عوض فروخت کیا ہے۔ بہر حال اس مسئلہ میں تمام نفع کو کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور کپڑے کی طرف پھیرنے میں اصل عقد متغیر ہو جاتا ہے اور سابق میں گذر چکا کہ متن کے مسئلہ میں عوضین میں سے ہر عوض کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرنے میں عقد کا وصف متغیر ہوتا ہے۔ اصل ند متغیر نہیں ہوتا۔ لہذا اس قدر فرق کے ساتھ متن کے مسئلہ کو اس مسئلہ پر قیاس کرنا اور متن کے مسئلہ کی اس مسئلہ کو نظیر قرار دینا کس طرح درست ہو سکتا ہے۔
دوسرے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ آپ نے شراء ماباع باقل مما باع قبل نقد الثمن کی خرابی سے بچنے کیلئے اور بیع کو جائز کرنے کیلئے یہ کہا کہ جس غلام کو ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خریدا تھا جب اس کو اور دوسرے غلام کو ادائے شمن سے پہلے بائع کے ہاتھ پندرہ سو برہم کے عوض فروخت کرنا چاہا۔ تو خریدے ہوئے غلام کا شمن ایک ہزار درہم قرار دیا اور دوسرے کا پانچ سو درہم ثمن قرار دیا لیکن اس کے با وجود ایک ہزار درہم کے عوض خریدے ہوئے غلام میں بیع جائز نہیں ہے۔ آپ تو یہ سمجھتے ہیں کہ عقد متغیر ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع نا جائز ہے۔ حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ عدم جواز کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اس صورت میں جواز کا طریقہ متعین نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ عقد جائز کرنے کیلئے جس طرح ایک ہزار کے عوض خریدے ہوئے غلام کی طرف ایک ہزار درہم پھیرا جا سکتا ہے اسی طرح ایک ہزار ایک درہم اور ایک ہزار دو درہم اور ایک ہزار تین درہم اور ایک ہزار چار درہم اور اس سے زائد کو بھی پھیرا جا سکتا ہے اور یہ تمام صورتیں برابر ہیں۔ کسی کو کسی پر کوئی ترجیح نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر کسی ایک صورت کو ترجیح دی گئی تو ترجیح بلا مرجح لازم آئے گا اور ترجیح نہ دی گئی تو شمن اور طریقہ بجواز مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ اور متن کے مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از متعین ہے یعنی ہر عوض کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرنا۔ پس جب متن کے مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از متعین ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از غیر متعین ہے تو ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا اور نظیر بنانا کیسے درست ہوگا ۔
تیسرے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب ایک آدمی نے اپنے اور دوسرے کے غلام کو ملا کر یہ کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ہاتھ ان دونوں میں سے ایک غلام کو فروخت کیا تو بیع کی نسبت منکر یعنی غیر معین غلام کی طرف کی گئی ہے حالانکہ غیر معین غلام مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع کا محل یعنی مبیع نہیں ہوسکتا اور معین چونکہ منکر اور غیر معین کی ضد ہے اور شی اپنی ضد کو شامل نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے غیر معین یعنی لفظ احد هما بول کر معین یعنی اس کا اپنا غلام بھی مراد نہیں لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ میں بیع کے ناجائز ہونے کی وجہ مبیع یعنی غلام کا مجہول ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عقد کا متغیر ہونا اسلئے تغیر عقد کی نظیر میں اس مسئلہ کو پیش کرنا بھی درست نہ ہو گا۔
چوتھے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب ایک درہم اور ایک کپڑے کو ایک درہم اور ایک کپڑے کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ عقد صحیح ہو کر واقع ہوا تھا۔ مگر جب بغیر قبضہ کئے عاقدین جدا ہو گئے تو دونوں درہموں میں عقد فاسد ہو گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس مسئلہ میں ابتداء عقد صحیح تھا۔ مگر حالت بقاء میں فاسد ہو گیا ہے اور متن کے مسئلہ میں ہمارا کلام ابتدائے عقد میں ہے۔ یعنی عوضین میں سے ہر عوض کو اگر خلاف جنس کی طرف نہ پھیرا گیا تو عقد ابتداء فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ پس جب خلاف جنس کی طرف نہ پھیرنے کی صورت میں متن کے مسئلہ میں ابتداء فساد پیدا ہو گیا اور اس مسئلہ میں قبضہ نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے بقاء عقد فاسد ہوا تو ان دونوں مسئلوں میں چونکہ بہت بڑا فرق ہے اسلئے ایک کو دوسرے کی نظیر قرار دینا درست نہ ہوگا۔
Contrary to those enumerated issues. As for the murābaḥa issue, because it becomes a ṭawliya in the heart by turning all the profit towards the cloth. And the way in the second issue is not determined, because it is possible to turn the excess over a thousand towards the buyer. In the third issue, the sale is attributed to the indefinite, which is not a place for sale, and the definite is its opposite. In the last issue, the contract was concluded validly, and the nullity is in the state of remaining, and our speech is about the beginning. Translation: Contrary to those issues that have been enumerated. Anyway, the murābaḥa issue is because by turning all the profit towards the cloth, the contract of murābaḥa in the bracelet changes to ṭawliya. In the second issue, the method of permissibility is not determined, because it is possible to turn the excess over a thousand towards the purchased slave. In the third issue, the sale was attributed to an indefinite slave, while it is not a place for sale, and the definite is its opposite. In the last issue, the contract was concluded validly, and the nullity is in the state of remaining, while our speech is about the beginning of the contract. Explanation: This is the response to the issues that Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i presented as analogies on the impermissibility of change in description. Thus, the response to the murābaḥa issue is that if the entire profit is turned towards the cloth, then in the bracelet the sale becomes ṭawliya. Because when the entire profit, i.e., five dirhams, is turned towards the cloth, the bracelet, which weighs ten dirhams, was bought for ten dirhams and sold for ten dirhams, and selling without profit or loss is called ṭawliya. So in the bracelet, the sale is ṭawliya, and since ṭawliya is the opposite of murābaḥa, and a thing does not include its opposite, ṭawliya does not include murābaḥa. Therefore, in turning all profit towards the cloth, although the contract becomes valid, the original contract changes from murābaḥa to ṭawliya. Because the buyer of the cloth and bracelet explicitly said, 'I sold the bracelet and cloth on murābaḥa,' meaning I bought for twenty dirhams and sold for twenty-five dirhams. In any case, in this issue, turning all profit towards the cloth changes the original contract. And it has already passed that in the issue of the matn, turning each of the two countervalues to a different genus changes the description of the contract, not the essence. Therefore, with such a difference, how can the matn's issue be analogized to this issue and this issue be made an analogy for the matn's issue? The response to the second issue is that you said, to avoid the defect of buying what one sold before paying the price and to validate the sale, that when the slave bought for a thousand dirhams, along with another slave, was sold before payment of the price to the seller for fifteen hundred dirhams, you set the price of the purchased slave as a thousand dirhams and the other as five hundred dirhams. Still, the sale of the slave bought for a thousand dirhams is not valid. You think it is invalid due to change in the contract, but this is not the case; rather, the reason for invalidity is that in this case, the method of permissibility is not determined. Because to validate the contract, just as you can turn a thousand dirhams towards the slave bought for a thousand, you can also turn a thousand and one, a thousand and two, a thousand and three, a thousand and four, and more, and all these possibilities are equal. None has preference over another. If one is preferred, it leads to preference without a preferrer; if not, the price and method of validity become unknown, causing the contract to be invalid. In the matn's issue, the method of validity is determined: turning each countervalue to a different genus. So when the matn's issue has a determined method and this issue has an undetermined method, how can one be analogized to the other and made an analogy? The response to the third issue is that when a man combined his own slave and another's slave and said, 'I have sold you one of these two slaves,' then the sale is attributed to the indefinite, i.e., an unspecified slave, while an unspecified slave, being unknown, cannot be the subject of sale. And since the definite is the opposite of the indefinite, and a thing does not include its opposite, by saying 'one of them' the definite, i.e., his own slave, cannot be intended. Therefore, in this issue, the cause of invalidity is the unknown subject matter, not the change in the contract. So presenting this issue as an analogy for change in contract is incorrect. The response to the fourth issue is that when a dirham and a cloth were sold for a dirham and a cloth, the contract was valid. But when the parties separated without possession, the contract became invalid regarding the two dirhams. The conclusion is that in this issue, the beginning of the contract was valid, but it became invalid in the state of remaining. In the matn's issue, our speech is about the beginning of the contract: if each countervalue is not turned to a different genus, the contract is invalid from the beginning. So when in the matn's issue, failure to turn to a different genus causes invalidity from the beginning, and in this issue, failure to take possession causes invalidity during continuation, there is a great difference, so one cannot be made an analogy for the other.
Source pages p. 111

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute where the Hanafi position is defended against objections raised by Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i. The issue concerns contracts in which the description changes due to apportioning countervalues to different genera. The opponents argued that such change invalidates the contract, citing four analogies. The Hanafi response, given by the commentator, refutes each analogy by showing that the actual cause of invalidity in those examples is not the change of description, but other factors. In the first analogy (murābaḥa), turning all profit to one item changes the contract from murābaḥa to ṭawliya (sale at cost), which is a change of type, not a mere description change, so it is not analogous. In the second, the method of validating the contract is indeterminate because multiple price allocations are possible, leading to uncertainty. In the third, the contract is invalid due to unknown subject matter (indefinite slave), not due to change in description. In the fourth, the contract was initially valid and became invalid later due to lack of possession before separation, which is a different issue. Thus, the Hanafi ruling that change in description (as in the original matn issue) does not invalidate the contract remains intact.

Key Terms
تغیر وصف (taghayyur waṣf): Change in the description of a contract, such as from murābaḥa to ṭawliya, considered permissible in the original matn issue.
مرابحہ (murābaḥa): A sale where the seller discloses the cost and adds a known profit.
تولیہ (ṭawliya): A sale at cost without profit or loss.
نظیر (naẓīr): An analogous case used as evidence in legal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why is the second analogy (selling a purchased slave before payment with multiple price possibilities) not valid as an objection?
A) Because the contract was invalid from the beginning due to change in description.
B) Because the method of validation is indeterminate, leading to uncertainty, not change in description.
C) Because the subject matter was unknown.
D) Because the contract was valid at inception and became invalid later.

Key Takeaway
A change of description (wasf) in a contract is permissible; only a change of essence (asl) or other defects invalidate it.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
6 min
Selling Eleven Dirhams for Ten Dirhams and One Dinar
Stating the ruling for a mixed currency exchange contract

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sale of eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, and explain the apportionment method used to satisfy the condition of tamāthul.

Core Idea
In mixed currency exchanges, tamāthul applies only to same-genus portions; the rest is treated as a separate different-genus exchange.

This lesson addresses a classic sarf scenario: selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar. At first glance, the transaction seems unequal, but the Hanafi school validates it by apportioning the eleven dirhams: ten dirhams exchange like-for-like with the ten dirhams, and the remaining one dirham exchanges for the dinar as a different currency, where equality is not required. Understanding this interpretation is key to applying the rules of ribā in currency exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the currencies and their types
List the items being exchanged: eleven dirhams (silver) for ten dirhams and one dinar (gold). Note that dirham and dinar are different genera.
2
Recall the condition for same-genus exchange
For exchanging dirham for dirham, Hanafi fiqh requires equality (tamāthul) in quantity. This is based on the hadith prohibiting excess in silver-for-silver sales.
This condition applies to the dirham-to-dirham portion.
3
Apportion the countervalues
Interpret the seller's intention: treat ten of the eleven dirhams as the price for the ten dirhams (like-for-like), and the remaining one dirham as the price for the dinar.
The seller's apparent intention supports this apportionment.
4
Apply the ruling for different genera
Since the remaining one dirham and the dinar are different genera (silver vs gold), equality is not required. The exchange is valid as a currency trade (sarf) with spot delivery.
5
Conclude the validity of the sale
The entire sale is permissible (jāʾiz) because each component fulfills the respective conditions: tamāthul for the dirham portion, and free agreement for the different-genus portion.

قال ومن باع أحد عشر درهما بعشرة دراهم ودينار جاز البيع ويكون العشرة بمثلها والدينار بدرهم لان شرط البيع في الدراهم التماثل على ماروينا فالظاهر انه ارادبه ذلك فبقى الدراهم بالدينار وهما جنسان ولا يعتبر التساوي فيهما
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے گیارہ درہم، دس درہم اور ایک دینار کے عوض فروخت کئے تو بیع جائز ہے اور دس درہم، دس درہم کے عوض ہوں گے۔ اور ایک دینار ایک درہم کے عوض ہوگا کیونکہ دراہم کے اندربیع کی شرط برابر ہونا ہے۔ اس حدیث کے مطابق جو ہم روایت کر چکے۔ پس ظاہر یہی ہے کہ اسنے اس بیع سے یہی ارادہ کیا ہوگا۔ اور ایک درہم ایک دینار کے مقابلہ میں باقی رہا درانحالیکہ یہ دونوں دو جنس ہیں اور دو جنس میں مساوات کا اعتبار نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے گیارہ درہم ، دس درہم اور ایک دینار کے عوض فروخت کئے تو یہ بیج جائز ہوگی اور یہ کہا جائے گا کہ گیارہ درہم میں سے دس درہم تو دس درہم کے مقابلہ میں ہیں اور باقی رہا ایک درہم تو وہ ایک دینار کے مقابلہ میں ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ
He said: And whoever sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, the sale is permissible. And the ten (dirhams) are for the like of them, and the dinar for a dirham, because the condition of sale in dirhams is equality, according to what we have narrated. So it is apparent that he intended that by it. Then the dirhams remain for the dinar, and they are two different types, and equality is not considered between them. Translation: And if someone sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, the sale is permissible. And the ten dirhams will be in exchange for ten dirhams, and the one dinar will be in exchange for one dirham, because the condition for sale of dirhams is equality, according to the hadith we have narrated. So it is apparent that he intended that by this sale. And one dirham remains in exchange for one dinar, while these two are different types, and equality is not considered between two different types. Explanation: The issue is that if a person sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, this sale will be permissible. And it will be said that out of the eleven dirhams, ten dirhams are in exchange for ten dirhams, and the remaining one dirham is in exchange for one dinar. The evidence is that...
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a direct ruling statement. It addresses a sarf (currency exchange) scenario: selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar. The Hanafi ruling is that the sale is valid by interpreting it as follows: ten of the eleven dirhams are exchanged for the ten dirhams on a like-for-like basis (required in sarf for the same currency), and the remaining one dirham is exchanged for the dinar as two different currencies, where equality is not required. The proof is the hadith requiring equality in exchanging dirhams for dirhams. The apparent intention of the seller is understood to be this apportionment. The ruling ensures that the ribawi condition of equality is maintained for the dirham-to-dirham portion, and the rest is treated as a separate exchange of different currencies.

Key Terms
تماثل (tamāthul): Equality in quantity and quality when exchanging the same type of currency (e.g., dirham for dirham).
صرف (ṣarf): The exchange of gold, silver, or currency; subject to specific rules of equality and hand-to-hand transfer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar, how are the countervalues apportioned according to the Hanafi ruling?
A) Ten dirhams for ten dirhams, and one dirham for one dinar.
B) Eleven dirhams for ten dirhams, and the dinar is extra.
C) Ten dirhams for one dinar, and one dirham for ten dirhams.
D) The entire eleven dirhams for the ten dirhams and dinar together.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates a mixed currency exchange by apportioning the countervalues to satisfy tamāthul for same-genus portions and allows difference for different genera.

Refuting Objections in Sarf: The Requirement of Specified Exchange
Commentator refutes four objections on sarf specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and refute common objections to the sarf ruling that each countervalue must be returned to the opposite type.

Core Idea
In sarf, analogy requires exact match of cause; differences in specification, timing, or object unknown break the analogy.

The commentator addresses four objections that attempt to analogize other transactions to the established sarf ruling. Each objection is refuted by showing that the underlying cause of invalidity differs. Understanding these refutations sharpens your ability to apply sarf rules correctly and avoid flawed analogies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
State the matn's ruling: a slave bought for 1000 dirhams can be redeemed by returning 1000 dirhams. The method must be specified (each countervalue returned to opposite type).
2
Extract each objection
List the four objections: (1) all amounts are equal, so any similar amount should work; (2) a case with unspecified method cannot be compared; (3) selling 'one of two slaves' is a case of unknown object; (4) a contract that becomes invalid later is not analogous to one invalid from inception.
The objections try to cast doubt on the original ruling by citing similar-looking cases.
3
Follow the commentator's refutation
For each objection, note the flaw: (1) preference without cause is arbitrary; (2) the method must be specified in the original but is not in the objection; (3) unknown object invalidates the sale completely; (4) later invalidity differs from initial invalidity.
The key is that the cause of invalidity must be the same for a valid analogy.
4
Distinguish types of invalidity
Recognize three distinct causes: unknown object (majhul), unspecified method, and later invalidation (e.g., separation without possession). Each leads to fasid but for different reasons.
Mixing these up leads to false analogies.
5
Apply the principle
Conclude that a valid analogy in sarf requires the precise illa (cause) to be shared. The commentator's refutations reinforce that the specification of method is essential for the original ruling.
This principle extends to other fiqh areas where qiyas is used.

كِتَابُ الصَّرْفِ اشرف الہدایہ جلد نم ایک ہزار کے عوض خریدے ہوئے غلام کی طرف ایک ہزار درہم پھیرا جا سکتا ہے اسی طرح ایک ہزار ایک درہم اور ایک ہزار دو درہم اور ایک ہزار تین درہم اور ایک ہزار چار درہم اور اس سے زائد کو بھی پھیرا جا سکتا ہے اور یہ تمام صورتیں برابر ہیں۔ کسی کو کسی پر کوئی ترجیح نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر کسی ایک صورت کو ترجیح دی گئی تو ترجیح بلا مرجح لازم آئے گا اور ترجیح نہ دی گئی تو شمن اور طریقہ بجواز مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد فاسد ہوگا۔ اور متن کے مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از متعین ہے یعنی ہر عوض کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرنا۔ پس جب متن کے مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از متعین ہے اور اس مسئلہ میں طریقہ جو از غیر متعین ہے تو ایک کو دوسرے پر قیاس کرنا اور نظیر بنانا کیسے درست ہوگا۔ تیسرے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب ایک آدمی نے اپنے اور دوسرے کے غلام کو ملا کر یہ کہا کہ میں نے تیرے ہاتھ ان دونوں میں سے ایک غلام کو فروخت کیا تو بیع کی نسبت منکر یعنی غیر معین غلام کی طرف کی گئی ہے حالانکہ غیر معین غلام مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے بیع کا محل یعنی مبیع نہیں ہوسکتا اور معین چونکہ منکر اور غیر معین کی ضد ہے اور شی اپنی ضد کو شامل نہیں ہوتی۔ اسلئے غیر معین یعنی لفظ احد هما بول کر معین یعنی اس کا اپنا غلام بھی مراد نہیں لیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس اس مسئلہ میں بیع کے ناجائز ہونے کی وجہ مبیع یعنی غلام کا مجہول ہوتا ہے نہ کہ عقد کا متغیر ہونا اسلئے تغیر عقد کی نظیر میں اس مسئلہ کو پیش کرنا بھی درست نہ ہو گا۔ چوتھے مسئلہ کا جواب یہ ہے کہ جب ایک درہم اور ایک کپڑے کو ایک درہم اور ایک کپڑے کے عوض فروخت کیا تو یہ عقد صحیح ہو کر واقع ہوا تھا۔ مگر جب بغیر قبضہ کئے عاقدین جدا ہو گئے تو دونوں درہموں میں عقد فاسد ہو گیا۔ حاصل یہ کہ اس مسئلہ میں ابتداء عقد صحیح تھا۔ مگر حالت بقاء میں فاسد ہو گیا ہے اور متن کے مسئلہ میں ہمارا کلام ابتدائے عقد میں ہے۔ یعنی عوضین میں سے ہر عوض کو اگر خلاف جنس کی طرف نہ پھیرا گیا تو عقد ابتداء فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ پس جب خلاف جنس کی طرف نہ پھیرنے کی صورت میں متن کے مسئلہ میں ابتداء فساد پیدا ہو گیا اور اس مسئلہ میں قبضہ نہ کرنے کی وجہ سے بقاء عقد فاسد ہوا تو ان دونوں مسئلوں میں چونکہ بہت بڑا فرق ہے اسلئے ایک کو دوسرے کی نظیر قرار دینا درست نہ ہوگا۔
Book of Sarf. Ashraf al-Hidayah, volume 9: A thousand dirhams can be returned towards a slave purchased in exchange for a thousand. Similarly, one thousand one dirhams, one thousand two dirhams, one thousand three dirhams, one thousand four dirhams, and more can also be returned. All these cases are equal; none has preference over another. If one case is preferred, it would be preference without a preponderant factor, and if not, then due to the price and method being unknown, the contract is invalid. In the original issue (matn), the method is specified, i.e., each countervalue is returned to the opposite type. So when the matn's method is specified and this issue's method is unspecified, how can one be analogized to the other? The answer to the third issue: When a man combined his own slave and another's and said, 'I sold you one of these two slaves,' the sale is attributed to an indefinite slave, whereas an indefinite slave cannot be the object of sale due to unknownness. The definite is the opposite of indefinite, and a thing does not include its opposite. Therefore, by saying 'one of them,' the definite (his own slave) cannot be intended. Thus, the invalidity here is due to the object (slave) being unknown, not due to the contract being altered. Hence, citing this as a case of altered contract is incorrect. The answer to the fourth issue: When one dirham and one cloth were sold for one dirham and one cloth, the contract was valid initially. But when the parties separated without possession, the contract became invalid in both dirhams. Thus, here the contract was valid initially but became invalid later, while our discussion in the matn is at the inception of the contract: if each countervalue is not returned to the opposite type, the contract is invalid from the start. Therefore, there is a great difference between the two cases, so one cannot be considered analogous to the other.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage is a commentary addressing four objections raised against an earlier ruling on sarf (exchange of currencies). The commentator refutes each objection by showing that the analogies proposed by the objector are invalid due to differences in conditions. The first objection concerns returning a thousand dirhams against a slave; the commentator argues that all amounts are equal, so preferring any one is arbitrary. The second objection compares a specified method to an unspecified one; the commentator states that the matn's method is determinate while the objector's case is not, so analogy fails. The third objection involves selling one of two slaves; the commentator explains that the indefinite slave cannot be the object of sale, so the invalidity is due to unknown object, not altered contract. The fourth objection involves a valid contract that later becomes invalid due to separation without possession; the commentator distinguishes this from the matn's case where invalidity is at inception. All four objections are thereby refuted, affirming the original ruling.

Key Terms
صَرْف (sarf): Exchange of gold, silver, or currencies; a specific type of sale with strict conditions.
ثَمَن (thaman): Price; one of the countervalues in a sale contract. In sarf, both commodities are thaman.
مَجْهُول (majhul): Unknown; an object whose identity or quantity is not specified, leading to contract invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the third objection, why is the sale of 'one of two slaves' invalid according to the commentator?
A) Because the slave is not owned by the seller
B) Because the slave is unknown (majhul) and cannot be the object of sale
C) Because the price is missing
D) Because the contract was not in sarf

Key Takeaway
The validity of sarf contracts depends on specification of the exchange method; any deviation or analogy that ignores this condition is invalid.

Selling Eleven Dirhams for Ten Dirhams and One Dinar
Ruling on a sarf transaction with a combination of same and different species.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of tamathul (equality) to a mixed sarf transaction and explain why the sale of eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar is valid.

Core Idea
In a sarf contract, excess over same species is riba, but excess allocated to a different species is valid.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling on a combined currency exchange. The matn from al-Quduri rules that selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams plus a dinar is valid. The commentator shows how the condition of equality (tamathul) for same species is satisfied by matching ten dirhams, and the remaining dirham is lawfully exchanged for the dinar as a different species.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and its apparent problem
The transaction involves eleven dirhams on one side and ten dirhams plus one dinar on the other. Prima facie, there is an excess of one dirham if both dirhams are considered same species. This could be riba.
Riba al-fadl is prohibited when exchanging same species with excess.
2
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation
The Hanafi school rules the sale valid by allocating the ten dirhams against each other (equal) and treating the remaining dirham as the price of the dinar. This avoids riba because the excess is matched with a different species.
This relies on the assumption that the parties intended a valid contract (since they are Muslims).
3
Examine the proof (dalil)
The hadith 'الفضة بالفضة مثلاً بمثل سواء بسواء' establishes that equality (tamathul) is required when exchanging silver for silver. This implies that when species differ, equality is not required. The Hanafis apply this by interpreting the contract accordingly.
The dalil is from Sunnah ahad, but its meaning is clear.
4
Distinguish between same and different species
Dirham and dinar are two different species (jins). Tamathul is a condition only for same species. Therefore, the one dirham may be exchanged for the dinar without requiring equal amount.
This distinction is central to the Hanafi ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ بَاعَ أَحَدَ عَشَرَ دِرْهَمًا بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَدِينَارٍ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ وَيَكُونُ الْعَشَرَةُ بِمِثْلِهَا وَالدِّينَارُ بِدِرْهَمٍ لِأَنَّ شَرْطَ الْبَيْعِ فِي الدَّرَاهِمِ التَّمَاثُلُ عَلَى مَا رَوَيْنَا فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ أَرَادَ بِذَلِكَ فَبِقِيَ الدِّرْهَمُ بِالدِّينَارِ وَهُمَا جِنْسَانِ وَلَا يُعْتَبَرُ التَّسَاوِي فِيهِمَا۔ حدیث مشهور الفضة بالفضة ... الخ سے ثابت ہے کہ دراہم کے اندر بیع جائز ہونے کی شرط دونوں موضوں کا برابر اور مساوی ہونا ہے اور عاقدین چونکہ مسلمان ہیں۔ اسلئے ان کا ظاہر حال اس بات کا مقتضی ہے کہ انہوں نے عقد جائز کا ارتکاب کیا ہوگا نہ کہ عقد فاسد کا اور عقد جائز کی وہی صورت ہے جس کو صاحب قدوری نے ذکر کیا ہے کہ دس درہم، دس درہم کے عوض ہو جائیں گے۔ اور باقی ایک درہم ، ایک دینار کے عوض ہو جائے گا۔ اور درہم اور دینار چونکہ دو مختلف جنس ہیں اسلئے ان میں مساوات اور برابری بھی معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ برابری کا ہونا اتحاد جنس کے وقت شرط ہوتا ہے اختلاف جنس کے وقت شرط نہیں ہوتا۔
He said: Whoever sells eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and a dinar, the sale is valid. The ten dirhams are for ten dirhams, and the dinar is for one dirham, because the condition for sale of dirhams is equality, as we have narrated. So it is apparent that he intended that; thus one dirham remains for the dinar, and they are two different species, and equality is not considered between them. The famous hadith 'Silver for silver...' establishes that the condition for a valid sale of dirhams is that both amounts are equal. Since the parties are Muslims, their apparent state requires that they intended a valid contract, not an invalid one. The valid form is as al-Quduri mentioned: ten dirhams are for ten dirhams, and the remaining dirham is for the dinar. Dirham and dinar are two different species, so equality is not required between them, because equality is a condition only when species are identical.
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a mixed sarf transaction. The matn (from al-Quduri) states that selling eleven dirhams for ten dirhams plus one dinar is valid. The commentator explains the reasoning: the condition for dirham-dirham exchange is equality (tamathul). Since the parties are Muslims, we assume they intended a valid contract, so we allocate the ten dirhams against each other (equal), and the remaining dirham is considered the price of the dinar. Because dirham and dinar are different species, equality is not required. The proof is the hadith on silver-for-silver exchange, which mandates equality for same species. The commentator also cites al-Quduri's formulation. This ruling allows combining same-species and cross-species exchange in a single contract by imputing the excess to the cross-species part.

Key Terms
تَمَاثُل (tamathul): Equality in amount and quality between two items of the same genus (jins) in a sarf contract.
جِنْس (jins): Genus; a category of items that share the same intrinsic nature (e.g., gold, silver, wheat). In sarf, different genera have different rules.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the sale of eleven dirhams for ten dirhams and one dinar valid?
A) Because the seller made a mistake in counting
B) Because the ten dirhams are equal and the excess dirham is for the dinar, which is a different species
C) Because the buyer agreed to pay more
D) Because the hadith allows any increase

Key Takeaway
In a sarf contract, equality (tamathul) is required only when trading within the same species; excess is permissible when traded for a different species.

Sarf with an Extra Item: Offsetting Riba in Exchange of Like Commodities
Ruling on a sarf transaction with an extra item to avoid riba.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings for a sarf transaction where the two amounts are unequal and an additional item is included, and apply the condition that the item must have adequate value to avoid riba.

Core Idea
In sarf, inequality can be offset by an item of real value; without value, the excess is riba.

This passage expands on the classical Hanafi rule for exchanging gold for gold or silver for silver (sarf). When the weights are unequal, the addition of another item may save the contract from riba — but only if the item has genuine monetary value that compensates the shortfall. Otherwise, the transaction falls into prohibition or disliked permissibility. The passage also hints at the legal trick (hilah) concern, which makes some cases disliked.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core rule for sarf equality
Recognize that in a direct exchange of gold for gold or silver for silver, the weights must be equal to avoid riba. The passage starts with the premise of an unequal exchange.
The hadith 'gold for gold, equal for equal' is the basis.
2
Isolate the variable: presence of an extra item
The matn introduces a third item added to the lesser amount. Determine its value (none, less than shortfall, equal to shortfall).
3
Apply the three categories
Work through each scenario: (1) item worthless → sale batil (clear riba). (2) item value covers shortfall → sale jai'z without karahah. (3) item value less than shortfall → sale jai'z with karahah.
The dislike is due to the appearance of circumventing riba via hilah.
4
Understand the ratio legis (illah)
The illah for prohibition is the increase without equivalent countervalue. When the extra item provides the equivalent (in value), the increase is no longer riba.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the definition of riba.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that the Shafi'i school generally does not allow mixing a different item in the same contract to offset sarf inequality; they require separate contracts.
The thamarah al-khilaf is practical: under Shafi'i, the transaction would be invalid if done in one contract.

وَلَوْ تَبَايَعَا فِضَّةً بِفِضَّةٍ أَوْ ذَهَبًا بِذَهَبٍ وَاحِدُهُمَا أَقَلُّ وَمَعَ أَقَلِّهِمَا شَيْءٌ آخَرُ يَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ بَاقِيَ الْفِضَّةِ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ غَيْرِ كَرَاهَةٍ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَبْلُغْ فَمَعَ الْكَرَاهَةِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ قِيمَةٌ كَالْتُّرَابِ لَا يَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ لِتَحَقُّقِ الرِّبَا إِذِ الزِّيَادَةُ لَا مُقَابَلَ لَهَا تَكُونُ رِبًا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک شخص نے چاندی ، چاندی کے عوض یا سونا سونے کے عوض فروخت کیا اور ان دونوں میں سے ایک عوض وزن کے اعتبار سے کم ہے اور کم عوض کے ساتھ کوئی چیز ہے مثلا کسی نے دس درہم اور ان کے ساتھ کسی چیز کو پندرہ دراہم کے عوض فروخت کیا۔ پس جو چیز دس دراہم کے ساتھ ملا کر دی گئی ہے اس کی کوئی قیمت ہوگی یا قیمت نہ ہوگی۔ اگر اس کی کوئی قیمت نہ ہو جیسے مٹی تو اس صورت میں بیع جائز نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ جس جانب میں پندرہ درہم ہیں اس جانب میں پانچ درہم اس طور پر زائد ہیں کہ دوسری جانب ان کے مقابلہ میں کوئی عوض نہیں ہے اور عقد بیع میں ایسی زیادتی جس کے مقابلہ میں عوض نہ ہو وہ ربوا اور سود کہلاتی ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں ربوا لازم آئے گا۔ اور بوا حرام ہے لہذا بیع کی یہ صورت حرام اور نا جائز ہوگی اور اگر اس چیز کی قیمت ہو تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں یا تو یہ قیمت باقی چاندی یعنی پانچ دراہم کو پہنچ جاتی ہے یا نہیں پہنچتی۔ اگر اس کی قیمت باقی چاندی یعنی پانچ دراہم کو پہنچ جاتی ہے تو یہ بیچ بلا کراہت جائز ہے اور اگر اس کی قیمت باقی چاندی یعنی پانچ دراہم کونہیں پہنچتی تو یہ بیچ مع الکراہت جائز ہے۔ اور یہ صورت مکر وہ اسلئے ہے کہ لوگ ایسا کر کے ربوا کو ساقط کرنے کا حیلہ کریں گے یعنی سود کا لین دین کریں گے اور اس کو جائز کرنے کیلئے یہ کریں گے کہ کم عوض کے ساتھ دو سو گرام گندم ملا لیا کریں گے اور جواز کے حیلہ کیساتھ کسی حرام کا ارتکاب اگر حرام نہیں ہوگا تو مکروہ ضرور ہوگا۔ اس لئے اس صورت کو مکروہ قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
If two persons exchange silver for silver or gold for gold, and one of the two is less, and with the lesser one there is another thing that reaches the value of the remaining silver, the sale is permissible without dislike. If it does not reach, then with dislike. If it has no value, like dust, the sale is not permissible because riba is established, since the increase that has no equivalent is riba. Explanation: If a person sells silver for silver or gold for gold, and one of the two is less in weight, and with the lesser there is something else, e.g., someone sells ten dirhams plus some other item for fifteen dirhams. The item given with the ten dirhams either has value or not. If it has no value, like soil, then the sale is invalid because the side with fifteen dirhams has an excess of five dirhams with no corresponding countervalue in the other side. Such an increase with no equivalent is called riba (usury), which is forbidden. If the item has value, then two cases: either its value reaches the remaining silver (i.e., five dirhams) or not. If it reaches, the sale is permissible without dislike. If it does not reach, it is permissible with dislike. This dislike is because people might use this as a trick (hilah) to eliminate riba, i.e., by adding a small item to the lesser amount to justify the excess. Even though the trick makes it permissible, it remains disliked because it resembles a device to circumvent a prohibition.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on a sarf transaction where the two amounts of the same species are unequal, but the smaller amount is accompanied by another item. The matn states the three possibilities: (1) If the accompanying item has no value (e.g., dust), the sale is invalid due to clear riba. (2) If it has value equal to the shortfall, the sale is permissible without dislike. (3) If it has value less than the shortfall, the sale is permissible but disliked (makruh). The commentator explains that the dislike is due to the potential for using this as a legal trick (hilah) to circumvent the riba prohibition. The example given: selling ten dirhams plus a worthless item for fifteen dirhams — the five dirham excess is pure riba. If the item is worth five dirhams, it offsets the excess, making the transaction valid. If it is worth less (e.g., two dirhams), the remaining three dirham excess is still riba, but by including the item, it becomes a borderline case, hence disliked.

Key Terms
رِبَا (riba): Usury or unjustified increase in a sale of same species; the excess that has no equivalent countervalue.
حِيلَة (hilah): Legal stratagem used to achieve a permissible result while avoiding a prohibition; here, adding an item to offset riba.
صَرْف (sarf): Sale of gold for gold, silver for silver, or the exchange of one for another of the same genus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person sells 10 grams of silver plus a piece of pottery worth 2 grams of silver for 15 grams of silver. What is the Hanafi ruling?
A) Valid without dislike
B) Valid but disliked
C) Invalid (batil)
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
In a sarf exchange, if the weights are unequal, the deficiency can be compensated by an extra item of real value; full compensation makes the sale permissible without dislike, partial compensation makes it permissible with dislike, and no value makes it haram.

Exchanging Ribawi Items with a Compensatory Item
Ruling on sarf with a compensatory item

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rulings for exchanging gold/silver for an unequal amount accompanied by another item, and identify the condition (value of the added item) that determines each ruling.

Core Idea
Adding a compensatory item to the lesser side can prevent riba, but only if the item has real value.

This lesson addresses a nuanced scenario in sarf (currency exchange): what happens when you exchange silver for silver, or gold for gold, and one side weighs less but is accompanied by another commodity? The Hanafi school, applying istihsan (juristic preference), allows this sale under certain conditions. We will unpack the three possible rulings based on the value of the added item.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a sarf transaction (same genus ribawi items). Normally, equality of weight is required. Here, one side is less, but a non-ribawi item is added. The ruling depends on the value of that added item.
The three rulings: permissible without dislike, permissible with dislike, invalid.
2
Locate the dalil and the basis
The foundational hadith 'الفضة بالفضة مثلا بمثل' (silver for silver like for like) requires equality. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to allow an exception when a compensatory item covers the shortfall.
The exception is based on the principle that riba is the increase without compensation; if compensation exists, riba is avoided.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith's imperative for equality implies that any excess without compensation is riba. However, when the excess is compensated by a separate item, the increase is not unrequited, so the prohibition of riba does not apply.
The compensatory item must have value (qimah). Valueless items like dirt do not count.
4
Analyze the grading: three conditions
If the value of the added item equals the shortfall: permissible without karahah. If it partially covers: permissible with karahah tanzihiyyah. If it has no value (e.g., dirt): sale is invalid because the excess remains unrequited riba.
Karahah tanzihiyyah means avoiding it is better but it is not sinful.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
This Hanafi ruling uses istihsan. Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may not allow such a compensatory mechanism, insisting on strict equality. The practical difference appears in fatwa.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ تَبَايَعَا فِضَّةً بِفِضَّةٍ أَوْ ذَهَبًا بِذَهَبٍ وَأَحَدُهُمَا أَقَلُّ وَمَعَ الْأَقَلِّ شَيْءٌ آخَرُ يَبْلُغُ قِيمَتُهُ بَاقِيَ الْفِضَّةِ جَازَ الْبَيْعُ مِنْ غَيْرِ كَرَاهِيَةٍ، وَإِنْ لَمْ تَبْلُغْ فَمَعَ الْكَرَاهَةِ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ قِيمَةٌ كَالتُّرَابِ لَا يَجُوزُ الْبَيْعُ لِتَحَقُّقِ الرِّبَا؛ إِذِ الزِّيَادَةُ الَّتِي لَا مُقَابِلَ لَهَا تَكُونُ رِبًا.
And if they buy and sell silver for silver or gold for gold, one of them being less, and with the less there is another thing whose value reaches the remainder of the silver, the sale is permissible without dislike; and if it does not reach, then with dislike; and if it has no value like dirt, the sale is not permissible due to the realization of riba, because the increase that has no equivalent is riba.
Source pages p. 113

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Sarf (currency exchange) states the Hanafi ruling on a specific scenario: when exchanging ribawi items of the same genus (silver for silver, gold for gold), equality in weight is required. If one item is less, but accompanied by a non-ribawi commodity (like wheat or cloth) that makes up the value difference, the sale is valid. The ruling is graded: if the accompanying item's value exactly covers the shortfall, the sale is permissible without dislike. If it covers partially, there is dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) because it may be a device (hilah) to circumvent riba. If the accompanying item is valueless (like dirt), the sale is invalid because the increase becomes pure riba. The hadith 'الفضة بالفضة مثلا بمثل' (silver for silver like for like) is the basis, requiring equality.

Key Terms
ربو (ribā): Usury or interest, specifically the prohibited increase in exchange of ribawi items without proper compensation.
صرف (ṣarf): Currency exchange, the sale of gold, silver, or money of the same or different types.
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike, a legal classification between permissible and prohibited. Here it is tanzihiyyah (avoidance recommended).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of silver for silver, if one side is less but accompanied by another item whose value does NOT cover the shortfall, what is the ruling according to the Hanafi school?
A) The sale is invalid (batil) due to riba
B) The sale is permissible without dislike
C) The sale is permissible with dislike (makruh)
D) The sale is valid only if the accompanying item is gold

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exchanging unequal amounts of the same ribawi genus when a valuable non-ribawi item compensates the deficiency; if compensation is partial, it is makruh, and if absent, the sale is invalid due to riba.

Selling a Dinar to Offset a Prior Debt: The Hanafi Reasoning
Explains the permissibility of selling a dinar to offset a prior debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits a debtor to sell a dinar to his creditor and then offset the debt, and identify the point of disagreement with Imam Zufar regarding the use of iqtida'.

Core Idea
Selling a dinar for dirhams then offsetting the debt is valid via rescission by necessity (iqtida').

This lesson examines a specific transaction where a debtor sells a dinar to his creditor and then both agree to offset the price against a pre-existing debt. The Hanafi school validates this through a sophisticated legal reasoning involving the rescission of the sale and the concept of iqtida' (legal implication). We will unpack the reasoning and see why Imam Zufar dissents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the transaction and the Hanafi ruling
Start by stating the scenario: a debtor owes 10 dirhams, sells a dinar to the creditor for 10 dirhams, delivers it, and they mutually set off the price against the debt. The ruling is jayiz (permissible).
2
Understand the reasoning: why direct set-off is not possible
The debts are of different genera (dinar gold vs. dirham silver), so muqasah (set-off) directly after the sale would require an exchange of currency (sarf) which needs immediate possession. Instead, the subsequent agreement implies rescission of the sale so that the price becomes attached to the prior debt, achieving set-off.
The rescission is not explicit but implied by necessity (iqtida').
3
Appreciate the concept of iqtida' (legal necessity)
Rescission is established by iqtida' because without it the transaction would be invalid. The text parallels this with the case where two parties sell for a thousand then for fifteen hundred, implying rescission of the first sale.
Iqtida' is a well-accepted Hanafi principle.
4
Locate the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) disagrees because he does not accept iqtida' as a valid mechanism. For him, the rescission would not be established, and thus the transaction would not be permissible.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad agree.
5
Determine the practical consequence and mufta bihi
According to Zufar, the transaction is not valid. The mufta bihi (operative position) is the majority view of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, which permits it.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a creditor cannot use this method to settle a debt if following Zufar's opinion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَن كَانَ لَهُ عَلَى آخَرَ عَشَرَةُ دَرَاهِمَ فَبَاعَهُ الَّذِي عَلَيْهِ الْعَشَرَةُ دِينَارًا بِعَشَرَةِ دَرَاهِمَ وَرَفَعَ الدِّينَارَ وَتَقَاصَّا الْعَشَرَةَ بِالْعَشَرَةِ فَهُوَ جَائِزٌ. وَمَعْنَى الْمَسْأَلَةِ إِذَا بَاعَ بِعَشَرَةٍ مُطْلَقَةٍ. وَوَجْهُهُ أَنَّهُ يَجِبُ بِهَذَا الْعَقْدِ ثَمَنٌ يَجِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعْيِينُهُ بِالْقَبْضِ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا. وَالدَّيْنُ بِهَذِهِ الصِّفَةِ لَا يَقَعُ الْمُقَاصَّةُ بِنَفْسِ الْبَيْعِ لِعَدَمِ الْمُجَانَسَةِ. فَإِذَا تَقَاصَّا يَتَضَمَّنُ ذَلِكَ فَسْخَ الْأَوَّلِ وَالْإِضَافَةَ إِلَى الدَّيْنِ إِذْ لَوْلَا ذَلِكَ يَكُونُ اسْتِبْدَالًا بِبَدَلِ الصَّرْفِ. وَفِي الْإِضَافَةِ إِلَى الدَّيْنِ يَقَعُ الْمُقَاصَّةُ بِنَفْسِ الْعَقْدِ عَلَى مَا نُبَيِّنُهُ. وَالْفَسْخُ قَدْ يَثْبُتُ بِطَرِيقِ الِاقْتِضَاءِ كَمَا إِذَا تَبَايَعَا بِأَلْفٍ ثُمَّ بِأَلْفٍ وَخَمْسِمِائَةٍ. وَزُفَرُ يُخَالِفُنَا فِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَقُولُ بِالِاقْتِضَاءِ. وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ الدَّيْنُ سَابِقًا فَإِنْ كَانَ لَاحِقًا فَكَذَلِكَ فِي أَصَحِّ الرِّوَايَتَيْنِ لِتَضَمُّنِهِ انْفِسَاخَ الْأَوَّلِ وَالْإِضَافَةَ إِلَى دَيْنٍ قَائِمٍ وَقْتَ تَحْوِيلِ الْعَقْدِ فَكَفَى ذَلِكَ لِلْجَوَازِ.
And if one has a debt of ten dirhams on another, and the debtor sells him a dinar for ten dirhams, and hands over the dinar, and they mutually set off the ten dirhams against the ten dirhams, it is permissible. The meaning of the case is when he sold it for absolute ten dirhams. The reason is that by this contract a price becomes obligatory that must be specified by delivery as we mentioned. And the debt in this description does not allow set-off by the sale itself due to lack of homogeneity. So when they settle, it entails the rescission of the first and the addition to the debt. Because otherwise it would be a substitution for the consideration in a currency exchange. And in the addition to the debt, the set-off occurs by the contract itself as we will explain. And rescission may be established by necessity, just as if they sold for a thousand then for a thousand and five hundred. And Zufar disagrees with us because he does not accept necessity. This is when the debt is prior. If it is subsequent, then likewise in the more correct of the two narrations, because it entails the rescission of the first and the addition to a debt existing at the time of the contract change, and that suffices for permissibility.
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on Sarf addresses a specific transaction: a debtor owes ten dirhams. He sells a dinar to the creditor for ten dirhams, delivers the dinar, and then both agree to offset the ten dirhams price against the debt of ten dirhams. The Hanafi ruling is that this is permissible. The reasoning: The sale is for absolute dirhams, not specifically the debt. After delivery, when they mutually agree to set off, it is valid because it effectively rescinds the original sale of the dinar and attaches the price to the pre-existing debt. This avoids an exchange of currency (sarf) where immediate possession is required. The rescission is established by necessity (bi tariq al-iqtida') similar to the case where they first sell for a thousand then later for fifteen hundred (which implies rescission of the first). Imam Zufar rejects this reasoning because he does not accept iqtida'. The ruling applies whether the debt existed before the sale (sabiq) or arises after (lahiq) according to the more sound narration.

Key Terms
مقاصة (muqāṣṣah): Mutual set-off or offsetting of debts, where two parties agree to cancel mutual obligations.
اقتضاء (iqtidā'): Legal implication or necessity; a presumption that a subsequent contract implies the rescission of a prior one.
دين (dayn): Debt; a liability owed by one person to another, here ten dirhams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school consider the transaction of selling a dinar for dirhams and then offsetting the debt as permissible?
A) Because the sale and the debt are of the same genus, allowing direct set-off
B) Because the subsequent mutual settlement implies rescission of the sale and attachment to the debt via iqtida'
C) Because Imam Zufar accepted it
D) Because the dinar and dirhams are both currency

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits a debtor to sell a different commodity to his creditor and offset the price against a prior debt through the legal mechanism of rescission by necessity (iqtida'), a point of disagreement with Imam Zufar.
