Dirham Ghallah and Equal-Weight Exchange of Silver
Defines a term and states a ruling with a hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging mixed dirhams of equal weight and identify the hadith proof that quality differences are disregarded.

Core Idea
Equality of weight is the sole condition for exchanging silver for silver; quality differences are ignored.

The Hanafi school addresses the sale of silver coins that vary in quality – such as fine dirhams versus broken ones that merchants accept but the treasury does not. The passage clarifies that as long as the total weight matches, the exchange is valid. This principle is grounded in the prophetic hadith that the good and bad of silver are equal in exchange.

Guided Path
1
Define dirham ghallah
Identify what a dirham ghallah is: a coin accepted in trade but not by the treasury due to being broken or small change, not because it is counterfeit.
This distinguishes it from a counterfeit coin, which would be subject to different rulings.
2
Identify the exchange scenario
The passage gives an example: selling one fine dirham and two broken dirhams for two fine dirhams and one broken dirham. Note that total weight on both sides is equal.
3
State the condition for permissibility
According to Hanafi fiqh, the exchange of silver for silver (a ribawi transaction) is permissible only when the weight is equal. Quality differences do not affect the ruling.
This is because the underlying cause (illah) for riba in silver is weight, not quality.
4
Cite the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Its good and its bad are equal' (جَيْدَهَا وَرَدَيهَا سَوَاءٌ). This directly establishes that quality is irrelevant.
The hadith is transmitted in various collections; its meaning is clear (dalala qat'iyya) for the Hanafi school.
5
Conclude the ruling
The sale described is permissible (jai'z) because the condition of weight equality is satisfied. The difference in quality does not create a forbidden excess.

صاحب ہدایہ نے فرمایا ہے کہ درہم غلہ وہ ہے جس کو شجار تو قبول کر لیتے ہیں مگر بیت المال قبول نہیں کرتا۔ لیکن بیت المال کا قبول نہ کرنا اس کے کھوٹا ہونے کی وجہ سے نہیں ہے بلکہ ریزگاری اور پھٹ گر ہونے کی وجہ سے ہے۔ اب مسئلہ یہ ہوا کہ اگر کسی نے ایک درہم صحیح اور دو درہم پھٹ گر کو دو درہم صحیح اور ایک درہم پھٹ گر کے کلاس فروخت کیا تو یہ بیع جائز ہے کیونکہ وزن کے اعتبار سے دونوں عوض برابر ہیں اور درہم کی بیع درہم کے عوض جائز ہونے کی یہی شرط ہے اور ربا در ہم صحیح کا ٹوٹا ہوانہ ہونا تو یہ اس کا ایک وصف ہے اور عمدہ وصف ہے اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ بجنہ مقابلہ کے وقت وصف جودت وغیرہ کا اعتبار نہیں ہوتا چنانچہ مدینہ کے آقا صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے جَيْدَهَا وَرَدَيهَا سَوَاءٌ
The author of Hidayah has said: Dirham ghallah is that which merchants accept but the treasury does not accept. However, the treasury's non-acceptance is not because it is counterfeit, but because it is loose change and broken. Now the issue is: if someone sells one fine dirham and two broken dirhams for two fine dirhams and one broken dirham, this sale is permissible because the two countervalues are equal in weight, and this is the condition for the permissibility of selling dirhams in exchange for dirhams. And the fact that one fine dirham is broken in exchange for a fine one is a quality—a good quality—and it has passed before that at the time of exchange, qualities like excellence are not considered. Hence the saying of the Master of Medina (peace and blessings be upon him): 'Its good and its bad are equal.'
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a proof from hadith. It first defines 'dirham ghallah' as a coin that is acceptable in trade but not in public treasury due to being broken or small change, not due to debasement. Then it presents a case: selling one fine (full weight) dirham and two broken dirhams for two fine dirhams and one broken dirham. According to Hanafi fiqh, this sale is valid because the total weight on both sides is equal. The condition for selling silver for silver (ribawi goods) is equality in weight, not quality. Any difference in quality (e.g., fine vs. broken) does not justify excess. The proof is the hadith: 'جيدها ورديها سواء' (its good and its bad are equal). This means that in the exchange of silver, good and bad grades are treated the same; only weight matters. Therefore, the ruling is that such an exchange is permissible when weight is equal.

Key Terms
درہم غلہ (dirham ghallah): A dirham that is accepted in trade but not by the public treasury due to being broken or small change, not because it is counterfeit.
جيدها ورديها سواء (jayyiduha wa radiyuha sawa'): Hadith: 'Its good and its bad are equal' – meaning in exchange of silver, quality differences are disregarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the sale of a mixed dirham for a fine dirham with equal weight, why is the sale permissible according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because the broken dirham is not considered money.
B) Because the total weight is equal, and quality is irrelevant.
C) Because the hadith allows excess for bad quality.
D) Because the treasury accepted the broken coins.

Key Takeaway
Exchange of silver dirhams of mixed quality is permissible as long as the weight is equal, based on the prophetic principle that good and bad are equal.

The Principle of Predominance in Mixed Coins
States the legal effect of predominance of precious metal in mixed coins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mixed coins and apply the rule of predominance (ghalib) to determine whether riba rules apply.

Core Idea
Predominance of silver or gold in a mixed coin gives it the legal status of the pure metal, prohibiting unequal exchange.

In this passage, Al-Marghinani states a key principle for applying riba rules to coinage. Since coins often contain alloy, the school looks to the predominant metal. This lesson unpacks how predominance is determined and its implications for sale and loan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Predominant Metal
Determine which metal constitutes the majority by weight in the coin: silver in dirhams, gold in dinars.
If neither predominates, the coin is not treated as ribawi silver/gold.
2
State the Legal Ruling
The coin is legally considered as that pure metal for all riba-related rules.
3
Apply Prohibition of Riba in Sale
When exchanging such coins against themselves or against pure metal, equality in weight is required; excess is prohibited.
The hadith 'جيدها ورديها سواء' supports equality.
4
Extend to Borrowing
Borrowing must be by weight, not count, because the coin's value is in its metal content.
5
Understand the Justification
Coins always contain a small amount of alloy due to minting; this is negligible and does not change the genus.
The good and the bad are equal.

قال وإذا كان الغالب على الدراهم الفضة فهى فضة وأذا كان الغالب على الدنانير الذهب فهى ذهب ويعتبر فيهما من تحريم التفاضل ما يعتبر فى الجياد حتى لا يجوز بيع الخالصة بها ولا بيع بعضها ببعض الامتساويا في الوزن وكذا لا يجوز الاستقراض بها الا وزنا لان النقود لا تخلو عن قليل غش عادة لانها لا تنطبع الامع الغش وقد يكون الغش خلقيا كما في الردى منه فيلحق القليل أو بالرداءة والجيد والردى سواء
He said: And when silver predominates in dirhams, they are silver; and when gold predominates in dinars, they are gold. And the prohibition of excess is considered in them as is considered in pure ones, so that it is not permissible to sell pure ones with them, nor to sell some of them for others unless equal in weight. Likewise, it is not permissible to borrow them except by weight, because coins are not devoid of a little adulteration usually, since they cannot be struck without adulteration. And sometimes adulteration is natural, as in the inferior kind, so a small amount is attached to inferiority, and the good and the bad are equal.
Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a proof based on reasoning and a hadith. It establishes a key principle of Hanafi fiqh for riba (usury) in sarf (currency exchange): when the precious metal (silver or gold) predominates in a coin, that coin is legally treated as that pure metal. This means that the same rules of riba apply: selling such coins against themselves or against pure metal requires equality in weight; excess is prohibited. The text then extends this to borrowing: such coins can only be borrowed by weight, not by count, because even pure coins are never free of some alloy (ghish) due to minting requirements. This alloy is considered negligible and attached to the inferior quality, per the hadith 'جيدها ورديها سواء' (the good and bad are equal). Therefore, all mixed coins with predominant silver/gold are equivalent to pure metal for riba purposes.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghalib): The predominant metal (silver or gold) in a mixed coin, which determines its legal ruling.
غش (ghish): Alloy or adulteration mixed with precious metal in coinage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is treated as copper, not subject to riba rules for silver.
B) It is still treated as silver because it is called a dirham.
C) It is treated as silver only if the copper is naturally occurring.
D) The ruling depends on the intention of the parties.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, predominance of the precious metal in a coin determines its ribawi status; the small amount of alloy is disregarded.

Ruling on Coins with Predominant Adulteration
States that if adulteration predominates, the coin is not in the ruling of dirhams/dinars; example with sword ornamentation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on coins where adulteration predominates and apply the analogy of hilyat al-sayf to determine exchange permissibility.

Core Idea
A coin's monetary ruling depends on the predominant metal; ghish ghalib removes it from riba.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue in exchange: when a coin contains more base metal than silver or gold, is it still considered dirham or dinar? The Hanafi school, using the principle of considering the predominant (al-ghalabah), rules that such a coin is no longer ribawi money. The ruling is analogized to the well-known case of sword ornaments (hilyat al-sayf), where the composition determines the applicability of riba rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
The condition is that ghish (adulteration) is ghalib (predominant) in the coin. If so, the coin is not in the ruling of dirham/dinar.
The principle 'اعتبارًا للغالب' is applied.
2
State the legal principle
The principle is 'اعتبارًا للغالب' (consideration is to the predominant). This is the basis for the ruling.
3
Trace the analogy to hilyat al-sayf
The coin case is analogous to sword ornament (hilyat al-sayf) made of gold/silver and base metal. In hilyat al-sayf, if the precious metal is not predominant, it is a commodity; riba rules are relaxed.
The detailed rulings of hilyat al-sayf are assumed known from earlier sections.
4
Derive the ruling for the coin
Since ghish predominates, the coin is a commodity. Therefore, exchanging it for pure silver is not subject to riba conditions (like equality of weight), and excess is generally permissible.
The exact ruling depends on the proportion of precious metal, as per the hilyat al-sayf scenarios.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
For example, a coin with 70% copper and 30% silver: buying pure silver with such a coin is permissible even if the silver weight is not equal.
This facilitates trade of debased or worn coins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان الغالب عليهما الغش فليسا فى حكم الدراهم والدنانير اعتبارًا للغالب فان اشترى بها فضة خالصة فهو على الوجوه التي ذكرناها في حلية السيف
And if adulteration predominates over them (dirhams/dinars), they are not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars, considering the predominant. So if one purchases pure silver with them, it is subject to the scenarios we mentioned in the ornament of the sword (hilyat al-sayf).
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling that establishes an exception to the previous rule. If the adulteration (copper or other base metal) is the predominant component in a coin, then that coin is no longer legally considered a dirham or dinar (i.e., silver or gold). The legal principle is: 'اعتبارًا للغالب' (consideration is given to the predominant). Therefore, such coins are treated as ordinary goods (commodities) that happen to contain some precious metal. The text references the example of a sword ornament (hilyat al-sayf), which is a known case in Hanafi fiqh where an object is made of both precious and base metals. The ruling for such items involves specific categories: if the predominant metal determines the permissibility of exchange with excess. Essentially, if adulteration predominates, the coin cannot be used in a ribawi transaction with pure silver/gold unless the exchange follows the rules for non-monetary items, i.e., any excess is allowed if the precious metal is a negligible part. The full discussion of hilyat al-sayf is assumed known.

Key Terms
حلية السيف (hilyat al-sayf): The ornamentation on a sword, often made of gold or silver; used as a legal analogy for items that combine precious and base metals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The exchange is prohibited because the dirham still contains silver.

D) The exchange is valid only if the buyer intends to melt the dirham.

Key Takeaway
When ghish predominates in a coin, the coin is treated as a commodity, not as ribawi money, and exchange rules for hilyat al-sayf apply.

Ruling on Coins Where Silver or Gold is Predominant
Ruling with proof on mixed coins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on exchanging and lending coins where silver or gold is predominant, and identify the proof based on the principle that the predominant metal determines the ruling.

Core Idea
A coin with predominantly silver or gold is treated as pure, making ribawi rules binding on its exchange and loan.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a practical issue: coins are rarely pure, often mixed with alloys. The Hanafi school establishes that as long as the precious metal (silver or gold) is predominant, the coin is legally treated as pure. Consequently, all ribawi rules apply—exchange must be equal by weight, and loans must be by weight, not count. The proof is rooted in the nature of coinage and a hadith on equality in exchange.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
What act is being ruled upon? Selling dirhams/dinars for their own kind, and lending such coins. The ruling is that any disparity (excess) in exchange is haram, and loans must be by weight.
This is a ribawi transaction involving same-kind exchange.
2
Determine When a Mixed Coin is Treated as Pure
If silver is predominant in dirhams, they are treated as pure silver; if gold is predominant in dinars, they are treated as pure gold. The alloy is ignored because coins cannot be minted without some alloy.
The key criterion is ghalabah (predominance) of the precious metal.
3
Apply the Ruling to Exchange and Loan
In exchange (sale) of such coins for their own kind, equality in weight is required—any excess is haram. In loans, repayment must be by weight, not by count or measure, because gold and silver are mawzunat (weighed items).
This applies whether the coins are pure or mixed, as long as the precious metal is predominant.
4
Locate the Proof and Understand Its Implication
The proof: (1) Coins are inevitably minted with some alloy, so the small amount of alloy is attached to low quality (radha'a). (2) The hadith 'Al-jayyid wa al-radhi sawa'' (good and bad are equal) indicates that quality difference does not permit disparity in same-kind exchange.
The hadith is ahad, but it is accepted in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دراہم میں اگر چاندی غالب ہو تو یہ دراہم ، خالص چاندی کے حکم میں ہیں اور اگر دنا نیر میں سونا غالب ہو تو یہ دنا تیر ، خالص سونے کے حکم میں ہیں اور ان میں بجنسہ بیع کرتے وقت کی ، زیادتی اسی طرح حرام ہوگی جیسے خالص سونے اور چاندی کی بجنسہ بیچ میں کمی زیادتی حرام ہوتی ہے چنانچہ اگر خالص دراہم کو کھوٹ اور میل ملے ہوئے درا ہم میں سے بعض کو بعض کے عوض بیچا گیا یا کھوٹ ملے ہوئے دنا نیر میں سے بعض کو بعض کے عوض بیچا گیا تو وزن کے اعتبار سے مساوات اور برابری ضروری ہوگی جیسا کہ خالص دراہم کو خالص در اہم کے عوض اور خالص د نا نیر کو خالص دنا نیر کے عوض فروخت کرنے کی صورت نہیں برابری شرط ہے اور اسی طرح اگر در اہم مغشوشہ یا دنا نیر مغشوشہ کو قرض کے طور پر لیا گیا تو وزن کے اعتبار سے قرض لینا جائز ہوگا عدد کے اعتبار سے جائز نہ ہوگا جیسے خالص در اہم اور دنا نیر کا قرضہ وزن کے ساتھ جائز ہے عدد کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ کھوٹ ملنے کے باوجود جب تک وہ دینار کہلاتا ہے، سونا ہے اور جب تک درہم کہلاتا ہے چاندی ہے اور سونا اور چاندی موزونات کے قبیلہ سے ہیں اور موزونات کا قرضہ وزن کے ساتھ جائز ہوتا ہے عدد یا کیل وغیرہ کے ساتھ جائز نہیں ہوتا اس لئے دراہم اور دنا نیر ، خالصہ ہوں یا مغشوشہ ان کو وزن کے ساتھ قرض لینا تو جائز ہے عدد یا کیل کے ساتھ لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ در اہم مغشوشہ اور دنا نیر مغشوشہ کو خالص در اہم اور دنا نیر کے مرتبہ میں رکھنے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نقود یعنی در اہم ودنا نیر کی ڈھلائی عادة اس وقت تک نہیں ہو سکتی جب تک کہ ان میں کھوٹ یعنی دوسری کسی دھات کی آمیزش نہ ہو۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ نفو تھوڑے بہت کھوٹ سے خالی نہیں ہوتے بلکہ کچھ نہ کچھ آمیزش اور ملاوٹ ضروری ہے اور کبھی سونے اور چاندی میں خلقی اور پیدائشی کھوٹ بھی ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ ردی سونے اور چاندی میں ۔ پس اگر کھوٹ کم ہو اور سونایا چاندی غالب ہو تو کھوٹ کی اس قلیل مقدار کو رداءۃ کیساتھ لاحق کیا جائے گا یعنی کھوٹ والے سونے اور چاندی کو پیدائشی ردی سونے اور چاندی کے ساتھ لاحق کیا جائے گا اور پہلے حدیث گذر چکی ہے کہ جید اور ردی دونوں برابر ہیں یعنی اگر جید کا مبادلہ، ردی کے ساتھ کیا گیا تو ان میں تفاضل اسی طرح حرام ہوگا جیسے فقط جید کا جید کے ساتھ مبادلہ کرنے میں تفاضل حرام ہوتا ہے۔
Explanation of the issue: If silver is predominant in dirhams, then these dirhams are in the ruling of pure silver. And if gold is predominant in dinars, then these dinars are in the ruling of pure gold. When selling them for their own kind, excess is forbidden just as excess is forbidden in selling pure gold and silver for their own kind. Thus, if pure dirhams are sold for mixed dirhams, or mixed dinars for mixed dinars, equality in weight is required, just as equality is a condition when selling pure dirhams for pure dirhams and pure dinars for pure dinars. Similarly, if mixed dirhams or mixed dinars are taken as a loan, it is permissible to take them by weight, not by count, just as a loan of pure dirhams and dinars is permissible by weight and not by count. Because even with alloy, as long as it is called a dinar, it is gold, and as long as it is called a dirham, it is silver. And gold and silver belong to the category of weighed items (mawzunat). A loan of weighed items is permissible by weight, not by count or measure. Therefore, dirhams and dinars, whether pure or mixed, are permissible to be lent by weight, not by count or measure. The proof for placing mixed dirhams and dinars in the same status as pure is that currency (dirhams and dinars) cannot normally be minted without some alloy (i.e., mixture of another metal). So it is known that currencies are not free from a little alloy; some amount of mixture is necessary. And sometimes gold and silver have a natural alloy, as in low-quality gold and silver. So if the alloy is little and the gold or silver is predominant, then that small amount of alloy is attached to low quality (radha'a). That is, the alloyed gold and silver are attached to naturally low-quality gold and silver. And the hadith has already passed that good and bad are equal; that is, if good is exchanged for bad, disparity is forbidden just as disparity is forbidden when exchanging good for good.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof. It states that dirhams and dinars in which the precious metal (silver or gold) is predominant are treated as pure silver or gold. Therefore, ribawi rules apply: selling such coins for their own kind (e.g., dirham for dirham) requires equality in weight; any excess is haram. The same applies to loans: they must be repaid by weight, not by count, because these coins are considered mawzunat (weighed items). The proof is that coins cannot be minted without some alloy, so a small amount of alloy is ignored and the coin is treated as pure. The hadith that good and bad are equal in exchange supports this: if good silver is exchanged for bad, disparity is prohibited just as in pure-for-pure exchange.

Key Terms
دراہم مغشوشہ (daraahim mughashshasha): Dirhams mixed with an alloy (e.g., copper) where silver is predominant.
موزونات (mawzunat): Items that are sold by weight, such as gold, silver, and other precious metals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling a mixed dirham (where silver is predominant) for another mixed dirham with an excess in weight?
A) Permissible because they are not pure
B) Haram because they are treated as pure silver
C) Permissible if both are of equal count
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, coins with predominant silver or gold are legally equivalent to pure, so ribawi rules apply strictly by weight.

Coins with Predominant Alloy: Commodity or Currency?
Ruling on mixed coins with predominant alloy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on coins with predominant alloy and apply the principle of al-ghalabah to determine the validity of a transaction involving mixed coins.

Core Idea
When alloy dominates, the coin is a commodity, not currency.

This passage explains a key Hanafi principle: the legal status of a composite object is determined by its predominant element. The author applies this to mixed coins (dirhams/dinars containing alloy) and then derives the transaction rules by analogy to a sword's hilt. By the end, you will know when buying pure silver with such coins is valid or invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? Coins where the alloy (e.g., copper) is predominant over silver or gold. The ruling: they are not treated as dirhams/dinars but as commodities containing silver/gold.
The principle of al-ghalabah (considering the predominant) is key.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof is cited? The author refers to the case of hilyat al-sayf (sword hilt) as a precedent. This is an analogy (qiyas).
This is a dalil 'aqli (rational proof) based on ijtihad.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the analogy work? Both the coin and the sword hilt are composite objects with a predominant element. The shared effective cause (illa) is ghalabah (predominance).
The hukm of the sword hilt is applied to the coin due to shared illa.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Do other schools disagree? Yes, some scholars treat such coins as currency regardless of alloy. But the Hanafi school relies on the predominant element.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi? The Hanafi position as stated in Al-Hidayah, considering the predominant, is the relied-upon view.
Al-Marghinani's tarjih in Al-Hidayah is authoritative.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان كان الغالب عليهما الغش فليسا فى حكم الدراهم والدنانير اعتبارًا للغالب فان لشترى بها فضة خالصة فهو على الوجره التي ذكرنا ها في حلية السيف ترجمہ اور اگر سونے اور چاندی پر کھوٹ غالب ہو تو وہ غالب کا اعتبار کرتے ہوئے دراہم ودنا نیر کے حکم میں نہیں ہوں گے پس اگر کھوٹے دراہم کے عوض خالص چاندی خریدی تو اس میں وہی صورتیں نکلیں گی جو ہم نے تلوار کے حلیہ میں بیان کیں ہیں۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر دراہم یا دنا نیر میں کھوٹ اور غش غالب ہو اور چاندی یا سونا مغلوب ہوتو یہ دراہم مغشوشہ اور دنا نیر مغشوشہ دراہم اور دنا نیر کے حکم میں نہیں میں کیونکہ غالب کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے پس ان دراہم مغشوشہ اور دنا نی مغشوشہ کو چاندی اور سونا نہیں سمجھا جائے گا بلکہ ایسا سامان اور اسباب شمار کیا جائے گا جس میں چاندی یا سونے کی آمیزش اور ملاوٹ ہے چنانچہ اگر کسی نے مغلوب چاندی والے دراہم معونہ کے عوض خالص چاندی خریدی تو اس میں وہی صورتیں نکلیں گی جو تلوار کے حلیہ میں بیان کی گئی ہیں یعنی اگر در اہم مغشوشہ میں ہے تو ان تینوں صورتوں میں بیچ نہ چاندی میں صحیح ہوگی اور نہ اس دھات میں صحیح ہو گی جو دھات دراہم معشوشہ میں ہے۔ اور اگر خالص چاندی اس چاندی سے زائد ہو جو دراہم معشوشہ میں ہے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ دراہم معشوشہ کی چاندی ، خالص چاندی میں سے اپنے مثل کے عوض ہو جائے گی اور جو چاندی زائد ہے وہ فش اور درا ہم مغشوشہ کی دھات کے عوض ہو جائے گی۔
And if the alloy is predominant in them (dirhams and dinars), then they are not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars, considering the predominant. So if one buys pure silver with them, then it follows the path we mentioned in Hilyat al-Sayf (the decoration of the sword). Translation: And if the alloy is predominant over gold and silver, then considering the predominant, they will not be in the ruling of dirhams and dinars. So if one buys pure silver with mixed dirhams, then the same scenarios will arise as we mentioned in the decoration of the sword. Explanation: The issue is that if alloy and mixture are predominant in dirhams or dinars, and silver or gold is overcome, then these mixed dirhams and mixed dinars are not in the ruling of dirhams and dinars because the predominant is considered. Therefore, these mixed dirhams and dinars will not be considered silver and gold, but rather counted as goods and articles in which silver or gold is mixed. Consequently, if someone buys pure silver with dirhams that have overcome silver, then the same scenarios occur as were mentioned in the decoration of the sword: i.e., if the pure silver is less than, equal to, or more than the silver in the mixed dirhams? (the text cuts off) ... in these three cases, the sale is valid neither for the silver nor for the metal that is in the mixed dirhams. And if the pure silver is greater than the silver in the mixed dirhams, then it is permissible, because the silver of the mixed dirhams will be offset by an equal amount of pure silver, and the excess silver will be for the alloy and the metal of the mixed dirhams.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof. It rules that when the alloy (like copper) is predominant in a coin, the coin is no longer treated as dirham/dinar but as a composite commodity containing silver/gold. This is based on the principle of considering the predominant element (al-ghalabah). The proof is analogical: it follows the same rulings as the case of a sword's hilt (hilyat al-sayf) that contains silver and other metals. The text outlines three scenarios from that case: if the pure silver bought is less than, equal to, or more than the silver content in the mixed coin. The sale is invalid if the pure silver is less than or equal? Actually the text says: if the pure silver is less than or equal? It states 'in these three cases the sale is valid neither for the silver nor for the metal' - meaning if the pure silver is not more than the silver in the coin, the sale fails. But if the pure silver is greater, the sale is valid as the excess is for the alloy.

Key Terms
غالب (ghalib): The dominant element in a mixture; here, if alloy is dominant (more than 50%?), the coin is not a dirham/dinar.
حلیة السيف (hilyat al-sayf): The decoration or hilt of a sword, often made of silver and other metals; used as a legal analogy for composite objects.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, a coin with 60% copper and 40% silver is treated as:
A) A dirham (currency)
B) A commodity containing silver
C) An invalid object for sale
D) Pure copper

Key Takeaway
Coins with predominant alloy are commodities, and transactions with them for pure silver are valid only if the pure silver exceeds the silver content in the coins.

intermediate
6 min
Mixed Coins: Disparity and the Fatwa Restriction
Explains the permissibility and its limitation for valuable coins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling mixed dirhams with predominant alloy for their own kind with disparity, explain the ta'lil, and identify the fatwa restriction for valuable coins.

Core Idea
Mixed coins are treated as two substances, allowing disparity, but later scholars blocked this for precious coins to prevent riba.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling from al-Hidayah on selling mixed dirhams (with majority alloy) for their own kind with disparity. The text presents a theoretical permissibility based on treating the coins as two different substances, but then notes a critical fatwa restriction by later Hanafi scholars. This example illustrates the school's approach to blocking means (sadd al-dhara'i) to riba while maintaining theoretical consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the theoretical ruling
Determine the act being discussed: selling mixed dirhams (with predominant alloy) for their own kind with disparity (excess or deficiency in weight). The theoretical ruling is ja'iz (permissible).
2
Understand the ta'lil (rational proof)
The coins are considered two substances: silver and brass. By ascribing the silver of one coin to the brass of the other and vice versa, the counter-values are of different kinds, so disparity is allowed. However, because silver exists on both sides, the transaction is still sarf, requiring possession in the session.
3
Address the objection
An objector might claim that if we treat it as exchange of different substances, it is not sarf, so possession should not be required. The answer is that the silver cannot be separated from the brass without harm, so the entire transaction is treated as sarf.
4
Note the fatwa restriction
The author reports that his teachers did not give fatwa for this permissibility in precious coins like 'adali and ghatarifa. Allowing disparity in such valuable coins would open the door to riba.
5
Understand the practical consequence
For ordinary mixed coins, disparity may be permitted under the ta'lil, but for coins that are precious and widely used, the fatwa prohibits disparity to block means to riba.

فان بيعت بجنسها متفا ضلا جاز صرفاً للجنس الى خلاف الجنس فهى فى حكم شيأين فضة وصفر ولكنه صرف حتى يشترط القبض فى المجلس لوجود الفضة من الجانبين فاذا شرط القبض في القضة يشترط في الصفر لانه لا يتميز عنه الابضرر قال رضى الله عنه ومشائخنا لم يفتوا بجواز ذلك في العدالى والغطارفة لانها اعز الاموال في ديارنا فلوا بيح التفاضل فيه يفتح باب الربوا ترجمہ پھر اگر دراہم مغشوشہ کو ان کی جنس کے عوض متفائلا فروخت کیا گیا تو جائز ہے ( اس طور پر کہ ) ایک جنس کو خلاف جنس کی طرف پھیرا جائیگا۔ پس یہ دراہم مغشوشہ دو چیزوں یعنی چاندی اور پیتل کے حکم میں ہیں لیکن یہ بیچ صرف ہے حتی کہ مجلس ہی میں قبضہ کرنا شرط ہے کیونکہ دونوں طرف چاندی موجود ہے پس جب چاندی میں قبضہ شرط ہے تو پیتل میں بھی شرط ہوگا۔ اس لئے کہ چاندی سے اس کا بغیر ضرر کے جدا ہونا ممکن نہیں ہے فاضل مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ہمارے مشائخ نے عدالی اور خطا رفہ میں اس کے جواز کا فتویٰ نہیں دیا ہے کیونکہ ہمارے دیار میں عدالی اور خطا رفہ عزیز مالوں میں سے ہیں پس اگر ان میں زیادتی مباح کر دی گئی تو ر ہوا کا دروازہ کھل جائے گا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایسے دراہم مغشوشہ جن میں کھوٹ غالب ہو اگر ان کو ان کے ہم جنس دراہم کے عوض کمی ، زیادتی کے ساتھ فروخت کیا گیا تو جائز ہے اور وجہ جواز ہیے کہ ایسے دراہم معشوشہ دو چیزوں کے حکم میں ہیں ا چاندی -۲ پیتل اور کانسہ پس ہر ایک کو اسکی جنس کے خلاف کی طرف منسوب کیا جائے گا یعنی احد العوضین کے پینل کو عوض آخر کی چاندی کے مقابلہ میں اور چاندی کو عوض آخر کے پیتل کے مقابلہ میں قرار دیا جائے گا۔ اور جب ایسا ہے تو دونوں عوضوں کی جنس مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے تفاضل اور کمی ، زیادتی جائز ہوگی۔ ولكنه صرف الخ سے ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ جب چاندی اور پیتل میں سے ہر ایک کو خلاف جنس کی طرف منسوب کیا گیا تو اب یہ بیچ بیچ صرف نہ ہوگی اور جب یہ بیچ ، بیچ صرف نہیں ہے تو اس کے عوضین پر جدا ہونے سے پہلے قبضہ کرنا بھی شرط نہ ہونا چاہئے ۔ کیونکہ بیع صرف کے علاوہ کسی بیع کے دونوں عوضوں پر مجلس کے اندر قبضہ کرنا شرد نہیں ہے۔
Then if they (mixed dirhams) are sold for their own kind with disparity, it is permissible, by turning the kind to the opposite kind. So these mixed dirhams are in the ruling of two things: silver and brass. But it is sarf (currency exchange), so that possession is required in the session because silver exists on both sides. So when possession is required for silver, it is also required for brass because it cannot be separated from it without harm. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Our teachers did not give fatwa for its permissibility in 'adali and ghatarifa (types of coins) because they are precious goods in our land; if disparity is allowed in them, the door of riba would open. Translation: Then if mixed dirhams are sold for their own kind with disparity, it is permissible (in such a way that) one kind is turned to the opposite kind. So these mixed dirhams are in the ruling of two things: silver and brass. But this sale is sarf, so that possession in the session is a condition because silver is present on both sides. So when possession is a condition for silver, it will also be a condition for brass, because it cannot be separated from silver without harm. The author (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Our teachers did not give fatwa for its permissibility in 'adali and ghatarifa, because in our land, 'adali and ghatarifa are precious goods; if disparity is made permissible in them, the door of riba would open. Explanation: The issue is that such mixed dirhams in which alloy is predominant, if they are sold for their own kind dirhams with excess or deficiency, it is permissible. The reason for permissibility is that such mixed dirhams are in the ruling of two things: (1) silver, (2) brass and bell-metal. So each one will be ascribed to the opposite kind of its own kind. That is, the brass of one counter-value will be set against the silver of the other counter-value, and the silver against the brass of the other. So when this is the case, due to the difference in kind of the two counter-values, excess and deficiency are permissible. But the phrase 'but it is sarf' is a response to an objection. The objection is that when each of silver and brass is ascribed to the opposite kind, then this sale would not be sarf. And when it is not sarf, then possession before separation should not be a condition for its counter-values, because besides sarf, possession in the session is not a condition in any other sale.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof addressing the permissibility of selling mixed dirhams (with predominant alloy) for their own kind with disparity (e.g., more weight for less). The reasoning: such coins are considered two substances: silver and brass. By treating each substance as exchanged for the opposite substance in the other coin, the transaction involves different kinds, so disparity is allowed. However, it is still considered sarf (currency exchange) because silver exists on both sides, so immediate possession in the session is required. The text then notes a fatwa restriction: the author's teachers did not allow this for valuable coins like 'adali and ghatarifa to prevent riba. The commentary also addresses an objection: if we treat it as two different substances, why is it still sarf? The answer: because the silver content is inseparable from the brass, so the entire transaction is treated as sarf.

Key Terms
عدالی و غطارفہ ('adali wa ghatarifa): Types of coins that were precious and commonly used in the author's region (possibly gold coins or high-value coins).
صرف (sarf): Currency exchange; a sale involving gold or silver, requiring immediate possession in the session to avoid riba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the author's teachers not give fatwa for selling 'adali coins with disparity?
A) Because the alloy is not predominant
B) Because they are precious and allowing disparity would lead to riba
C) Because they are pure silver
D) Because the sale would not be valid as sarf

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits disparity in mixed coins by treating them as two substances, but later fatwa restricts this for valuable coins to block the means to riba.
